![Diagram 1](diagrams/diagram-001.svg)

The Fabric platform orchestrates and manages concurrent LLM-based agents. It defines agent configurations, manages their lifecycle, and establishes their execution environments. A central Hub API client and a real-time event bus facilitate agent interaction and communication.

Agents operate within isolated environments, often with their own Git worktrees and credentials. This prevents conflicts during concurrent execution and supports various container runtimes such as Docker, Podman, and Kubernetes. The platform uses a "Harness" abstraction to encapsulate agent-specific logic, such as environment variables and command construction, which provides LLM agnosticism. For more details, see [Harness Abstraction and Provisioning](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-harness-abstraction-and-provisioning).

The system manages the complete lifecycle of agents, including provisioning, starting, stopping, deleting, listing, and messaging. The [`Manager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/manager.go#L33) interface orchestrates these operations for both standard and cloud-managed agents. More information is available in [Agent Lifecycle Management and Orchestration](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-agent-lifecycle-management-and-orchestration).

Agents fetch and utilize capabilities from various sources through skill resolution mechanisms. Supported sources include GCP Vertex AI registries, GitHub repositories, and the Fabric Hub API, with caching and security checks to enhance efficiency. Explore [Skill Resolution Mechanisms](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-skill-resolution-mechanisms) for further details.

- A Go client in [`pkg/hubclient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient) provides extensive services for managing agents, authentication, projects, and skills with the central Fabric Hub.
- Another Go client in [`pkg/brokerclient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/brokerclient) enables agent-specific actions like listing, creating, and executing commands within an agent's container via the Fabric Runtime Broker API.

Real-time, publish/subscribe messaging between Fabric components occurs through an [`EventBus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/eventbus.go#L40) abstraction in [`pkg/eventbus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus). It routes structured messages based on topic matching. Refer to [Event Bus for Real-time Messaging](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-event-bus-for-real-time-messaging) for more.

- Database operations leverage [`ent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/tx.go#L1) ORM-generated code in [`pkg/ent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent) for robust interactions with entities such as [`AccessPolicy`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/schema/policy.go#L29) and [`Agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L28).
- Core data structures and API definitions for agent configurations, actions, and telemetry reside in [`pkg/api`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api).

Developers and users interact with the platform through a command-line interface (CLI) in [`cmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd) and a web user interface (Web UI) in [`web`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web). The CLI manages agent lifecycle and configurations, while the Web UI offers real-time state synchronization via Server-Sent Events (SSE).

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management"></a>

## Fabric Agent Orchestration and Management

The Fabric platform facilitates the orchestration and management of concurrent LLM-based agents, enabling them to collaborate within a structured environment. This involves defining the overall architecture, configuring individual agents, managing their complete lifecycle, and establishing the execution environments in which they operate. The system provides a fundamental Go client for interacting with the Fabric Hub API, an event bus for real-time messaging, and mechanisms for skill resolution and database operations that underpin agent behavior.

Agents within Fabric are designed to operate within isolated environments, each often equipped with its own Git worktree and credentials to prevent conflicts during concurrent execution. The system supports various container runtimes, including Docker, Podman, Apple Container, and Kubernetes, providing flexibility in deployment. A central aspect of Fabric is its "Harness" abstraction, which encapsulates agent-specific logic related to environment variables, command construction, and authentication, contributing to LLM agnosticism.

Agent lifecycle management in Fabric involves provisioning, starting, stopping, deleting, listing, and messaging agents. The [`Manager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/manager.go#L33) interface, with distinct implementations for standard and cloud-managed agents, orchestrates these operations. This allows for both local and distributed agent deployments, with the ability to send buffered or immediate messages to an agent's harness. For more details on these operations, see [Agent Lifecycle Management and Orchestration](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-agent-lifecycle-management-and-orchestration).

Skill resolution is a critical component, allowing agents to fetch and utilize capabilities from various sources. The platform supports fetching skills from GCP Vertex AI registries, GitHub repositories, and the Fabric Hub API, incorporating caching and retry mechanisms to enhance efficiency and reliability. Security checks are in place to prevent vulnerabilities like Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF) during skill acquisition. The directory [`pkg/agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent) contains the implementations for these skill resolvers. For further exploration of this topic, refer to [Skill Resolution Mechanisms](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-skill-resolution-mechanisms).

Interactions with the central Fabric Hub are managed through a comprehensive Go client located in [`pkg/hubclient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient). This client provides extensive services for managing agents, handling authentication, and overseeing projects and skills. It also incorporates mechanisms for backward compatibility, particularly concerning terminology changes. Similarly, a Go client for the Fabric Runtime Broker API, found in [`pkg/brokerclient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/brokerclient), enables agent-specific actions such as listing, creation, starting, stopping, messaging, and command execution within an agent's container. For a detailed understanding of these client functionalities, refer to [Fabric Hub API Client and Services](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-fabric-hub-api-client-and-services) and [Runtime Broker API Client and Agent Interaction](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-runtime-broker-api-client-and-agent-interaction).

Real-time communication within the Fabric ecosystem is facilitated by an [`EventBus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/eventbus.go#L40) abstraction, located in [`pkg/eventbus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus). This event bus supports publish/subscribe messaging, offering both in-process and fan-out implementations to distribute messages across various Fabric components based on topic matching. This ensures that agents and other system components can communicate dynamically as events unfold. More information can be found in [Event Bus for Real-time Messaging](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-event-bus-for-real-time-messaging).

Database operations are handled using [`ent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/tx.go#L1), an ORM (Object-Relational Mapper), which generates Go code for robust interactions with the underlying database. This includes schema definitions, CRUD (Create, Read, Update, Delete) operations, relationship management, and query capabilities for key entities such as [`AccessPolicy`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/schema/policy.go#L29), [`Agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L28), [`AllowListEntry`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L710), and [`ApiKey`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/schema/apikey.go#L34). The generated code resides in [`pkg/ent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent). For more details, see [Database Operations with Ent ORM](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-database-operations-with-ent-orm).

The core definitions and data structures that underpin Fabric agents are located in [`pkg/api`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api). This includes configurations for agents, definitions for agent actions, authentication settings, telemetry configurations, and utilities for parsing skill URIs and generating slugs for unique identifiers. These API definitions establish the foundational contracts for how agents are configured and interact within the platform. See [Fabric API Definitions and Core Data Structures](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-fabric-api-definitions-and-core-data-structures) for further details.

The [`Harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L23) abstraction, detailed in [`pkg/harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness), is crucial for enabling agent-agnostic execution. It provides interfaces and implementations for various agent execution environments, managing authentication gathering, configuration loading, and provisioning. This allows the Fabric platform to integrate diverse LLMs and execution strategies seamlessly. More information is available in [Harness Abstraction and Provisioning](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-harness-abstraction-and-provisioning).

To enhance local development and user experience, Fabric includes a local, filesystem-based cache for agent names in [`pkg/agentcache`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agentcache). This cache significantly speeds up shell completion and improves reliability by reducing dependencies on the Hub API, especially when network conditions are suboptimal or the API is under load. For a deeper understanding, refer to [Local Agent Cache for Shell Completion](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-local-agent-cache-for-shell-completion).

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-agent-lifecycle-management-and-orchestration"></a>

### Agent Lifecycle Management and Orchestration

![Diagram 2](diagrams/diagram-002.svg)

FABRIC agents undergo a comprehensive lifecycle, from initial provisioning to eventual deletion, managed through a set of core functionalities. The primary interface for orchestrating these agents is the [`Manager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/manager.go#L33), which has different implementations to accommodate standard and cloud-managed agents.

For standard agents, the [`AgentManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/manager.go#L68) in [`pkg/agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent) facilitates operations such as [`Provision`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L36) to prepare agent environments, [`Start`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L1956) to launch new agents, [`Stop`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/mock.go#L55) to terminate them, and [`Delete`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/storage/gcs.go#L219) to remove their associated resources, including files and Git worktrees. Agent information is retrieved and reconciled from both the runtime environment and local storage, with an emphasis on the [`agent-info.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L965) file for status reporting. Communication with agents is handled by the [`Message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/output.go#L60) function, which can send buffered or immediate messages, often using [`tmux`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L74) commands, with a [`MessageBuffer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/msgbuffer.go#L40) to debounce messages and prevent overwhelming the agent.

Cloud-managed agents are handled by the [`ManagedAgentManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/managed_manager.go#L34) in [`pkg/agent/managed_manager.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/managed_manager.go). This implementation delegates operations to a [`managedagent.ManagedAgentBackend`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/managed_manager.go#L35), managing state locally and providing status updates through a [`Watch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/manager.go#L61) mechanism. A factory function, [`NewManagerForProfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/manager_factory.go#L29) in [`pkg/agent/manager_factory.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/manager_factory.go), determines whether to instantiate an [`AgentManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/manager.go#L68) or a [`ManagedAgentManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/managed_manager.go#L34) based on the agent's profile, providing a unified entry point for agent management. For a broader view of agent configuration and API definitions, refer to [Fabric API Definitions and Core Data Structures](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-fabric-api-definitions-and-core-data-structures).

The CLI plays a significant role in agent lifecycle management, offering commands for creation, deletion, and other operational utilities. More details can be found in [Agent Lifecycle and Management Commands](#command-line-interface-cli-operations-agent-lifecycle-and-management-commands). The system also manages the secure storage and retrieval of credentials, which is essential for agent operations. See [Secure Credential and Daemon Management](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-secure-credential-and-daemon-management) for further information.

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-skill-resolution-mechanisms"></a>

### Skill Resolution Mechanisms

![Diagram 3](diagrams/diagram-003.svg)

FABRIC agents resolve and fetch skills from various sources through a flexible mechanism supported by several dedicated resolvers. Each resolver handles a specific source type, while a caching layer optimizes performance and security checks protect against vulnerabilities.

The primary mechanism for fetching skills from different locations is the [`SkillResolver`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/skill_resolver.go#L44) interface, which is implemented by several components. A [`CachingSkillResolver`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/caching_skill_resolver.go#L30), defined in [`pkg/agent/caching_skill_resolver.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/caching_skill_resolver.go), wraps other resolvers to provide a content-hash based caching layer. This prevents redundant skill downloads by storing previously resolved skills, improving efficiency. The cache is passed through the execution context, allowing deeper functions to access it without explicit arguments.

For skills hosted on Google Cloud Platform, the [`GCPSkillResolver`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/gcp_skill_resolver.go#L53) in [`pkg/agent/gcp_skill_resolver.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/gcp_skill_resolver.go) handles [`gcp-skill://`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/gcp_uri.go#L33) URIs. It fetches skill metadata and files from GCP Vertex AI skill registries. This resolver includes critical security checks, such as [`validateFileURL`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/gcp_skill_resolver.go#L291) and [`isBlockedHost`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/gcp_skill_resolver.go#L314), to mitigate Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF) vulnerabilities during file downloads. GCP skill URIs are parsed and validated by logic within [`pkg/agent/gcp_uri.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/gcp_uri.go).

GitHub-hosted skills, identified by [`gh://`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/github_uri.go#L35) or [`https://github.com/`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/github_uri.go#L44) URIs, are managed by the [`GitHubSkillResolver`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/github_skill_resolver.go#L50) located in [`pkg/agent/github_skill_resolver.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/github_skill_resolver.go). This resolver interacts with the GitHub Contents API and raw content endpoints to retrieve skill files. It incorporates retry mechanisms with exponential backoff and rate limit handling, managed by the [`doWithRetry`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/github_skill_resolver.go#L316) function, to ensure robustness against transient API errors. A [`GitHubResolutionCache`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/github_resolution_cache.go#L40) in [`pkg/agent/github_resolution_cache.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/github_resolution_cache.go) provides persistent caching for GitHub resolution results, improving performance for frequently accessed skills. GitHub skill URIs are parsed and validated by [`pkg/agent/github_uri.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/github_uri.go).

Finally, for skills managed directly by the Fabric Hub, the [`HubSkillResolver`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/hub_skill_resolver.go#L26) in [`pkg/agent/hub_skill_resolver.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/hub_skill_resolver.go) delegates resolution requests to a remote Hub API client. This allows the Hub to centralize skill management and distribution. The [`HubSkillResolver`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/hub_skill_resolver.go#L26) translates local skill references into appropriate requests for the [`hubclient.SkillService`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/hub_skill_resolver.go#L27) and maps the responses back. More information on the Fabric Hub API client can be found in [Fabric Hub API Client and Services](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-fabric-hub-api-client-and-services).

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-fabric-hub-api-client-and-services"></a>

### Fabric Hub API Client and Services

The Fabric Hub API Client provides a Go interface for managing and orchestrating agents, projects, and skills within the Fabric platform. This client, primarily implemented within [`pkg/hubclient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient), facilitates interactions with the Fabric Hub, acting as a central point for administrative and operational tasks.

The client is structured around a set of specialized services, each responsible for a distinct domain of functionality:

- **Agent Services** manage the full lifecycle of agents, including creation, deletion, starting, stopping, and updating. It also provides capabilities for agent communication through structured messages and access to agent logs, including streaming logs from Cloud Logging. This is primarily handled by the [`AgentService`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/agents.go#L34) defined in [`pkg/hubclient/agents.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/agents.go).
- **Authentication Services** handle user authentication workflows, including logging in, logging out, token refreshing, and obtaining WebSocket tickets. It supports various OAuth flows suitable for web, CLI, and device-based clients.
- **Project Services** provide comprehensive management for projects, which serve as organizational containers for agents and other resources. This includes registering, creating, updating, and deleting projects, as well as managing associated providers and project settings.
- **Skill Services** manage the lifecycle of skills, which represent capabilities that agents can acquire and execute. This involves listing, getting, creating, updating, and deleting skills, along with support for skill versioning and file transfers.
- **Runtime Broker Services** enable the management of runtime brokers, which are responsible for executing agents. This includes operations such as creating, joining, listing, and updating runtime brokers, and handling heartbeats.
- **Harness Configuration Services** manage the configurations for agent harnesses, which define how agents operate within their execution environments. This includes CRUD operations, file uploads/downloads, and validation of harness configurations.
- **Credential and Secret Services** manage various types of credentials and secrets. This includes storing and retrieving user access tokens, and managing project-scoped secrets, with an emphasis on security by ensuring secret values are write-only and never returned.

A key design aspect of the Hub API client is its approach to **backward compatibility**. Many data structures within the client, especially those related to projects and runtime brokers (defined in [`pkg/hubclient/types.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/types.go) and other service-specific files), include custom JSON marshaling and unmarshaling logic. This allows the client to gracefully handle transitions from older API versions that used "grove" terminology (e.g., [`groveId`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138), [`groveName`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L290)) to newer versions using "project" terminology (e.g., [`ProjectID`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L882), [`ProjectName`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/types.go#L312)). This ensures that the client can interact with both legacy and modern Fabric Hub deployments without requiring client-side code changes.

For **secure communication**, the client integrates various authentication mechanisms. It supports bearer token authentication for general API access, and specialized tokens for brokers and agents. In development environments, it can generate and manage development tokens for simplified authentication. A robust [`Transport`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/apiclient/transport.go#L31) mechanism, as described in [Fabric API Definitions and Core Data Structures](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-fabric-api-definitions-and-core-data-structures), handles HTTP requests, retries, and user agent management, ensuring reliable and secure interactions with the Fabric Hub API. This [`Transport`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/apiclient/transport.go#L31) is also responsible for standardized error handling, converting API error responses into structured [`APIError`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/errors.go#L31) objects for consistent processing across the client.

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-runtime-broker-api-client-and-agent-interaction"></a>

### Runtime Broker API Client and Agent Interaction

![Diagram 4](diagrams/diagram-004.svg)

The Go client for the Fabric Runtime Broker API facilitates programmatic interaction with the Runtime Broker, primarily for managing agents. This client allows for comprehensive control over agent instances, abstracting the underlying HTTP communication and providing a straightforward interface for various operations.

The client is initialized with a base URL for the broker and can be configured with options such as bearer token authentication, broker-specific tokens, custom HTTP clients, timeouts, and retry mechanisms. It also supports automatic resolution of development tokens from environment variables or local files.

The core functionality of the Runtime Broker API client revolves around agent management. It provides methods for:

- **Agent Lifecycle Management**: Creating, listing, retrieving details, starting, stopping, restarting, and deleting agent instances.
- **Messaging**: Sending both plain text and structured messages to agents, enabling communication and command execution within the Fabric ecosystem.
- **Command Execution**: Executing arbitrary commands directly within an agent's container, which is critical for dynamic interactions and troubleshooting.
- **Monitoring**: Retrieving logs and resource statistics for agents, offering insights into their operational status and performance.

These operations are managed through an [`AgentService`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/agents.go#L34) interface, which encapsulates the details of constructing API requests and parsing responses. For instance, [`ListAgentsOptions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/agents.go#L127) allows filtering and pagination when listing agents, while [`DeleteAgentOptions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/agents.go#L275) provides granular control over file and branch removal during agent deletion. The client also offers direct methods for retrieving broker-level information and health checks, which are essential for understanding the broker's status and capabilities.

The design emphasizes flexibility through functional options for configuration and separation of concerns, with agent-specific actions delegated to the [`AgentService`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/agents.go#L34). This allows for a modular and extensible approach to interacting with the Runtime Broker API.

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-event-bus-for-real-time-messaging"></a>

### Event Bus for Real-time Messaging

![Diagram 5](diagrams/diagram-005.svg)

The Fabric platform utilizes an [`EventBus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/eventbus.go#L40) abstraction to facilitate real-time publish/subscribe messaging among its various components. This system, inspired by NATS-style subject matching, routes structured messages, abstracting the underlying communication mechanism.

The core [`EventBus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/eventbus.go#L40) interface, defined in [`pkg/eventbus/eventbus.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/eventbus.go), provides methods for [`Publish`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/config.go#L136)ing a message to a specific topic, [`Subscribe`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/events.go#L52)ing to topics using wildcard patterns, and [`Close`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/events.go#L54)ing the bus to release resources. Message handlers receive the structured message along with the context and the topic it arrived on. Standardized topic naming conventions are used for agent-specific messages, project-wide broadcasts, and global broadcasts, ensuring consistent addressing across the system.

Two primary implementations of the [`EventBus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/eventbus.go#L40) are provided:

- **In-Process Event Bus**: Implemented in [`pkg/eventbus/inprocess.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/inprocess.go), this version offers an efficient, low-latency messaging solution for single-node deployments. It uses Go channels for message delivery and manages concurrency with read-write mutexes. Publishers operate non-blockingly, with messages potentially dropped if a subscriber's buffer is full, prioritizing throughput. Each subscriber handler runs in its own goroutine, preventing slow consumers from impacting overall performance. Graceful shutdown mechanisms ensure that all active subscriber goroutines terminate cleanly when the bus is closed.
- **Fan-Out Event Bus**: The [`FanOutEventBus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/fanout.go#L46), found in [`pkg/eventbus/fanout.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/fanout.go), acts as a composite event bus. It delegates operations to multiple underlying [`EventBus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/eventbus.go#L40) instances, allowing messages to be distributed concurrently to several different bus implementations. This is useful for scenarios where messages need to be sent to both an in-process bus and potentially an external messaging system. It supports routing messages to specific child buses using a channel ID within the message or broadcasting to all configured buses. Errors from "observer" buses (configured for fire-and-forget publishing) are logged but do not block the publisher, while errors from critical buses are returned.

The [`EventBus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/eventbus.go#L40) facilitates loose coupling between Fabric components, allowing for flexible and scalable communication patterns essential for orchestrating concurrent LLM-based agents. Further details on core data structures, including [`messages.StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/message.go#L373), can be found in [Fabric API Definitions and Core Data Structures](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-fabric-api-definitions-and-core-data-structures).

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-secure-credential-and-daemon-management"></a>

### Secure Credential and Daemon Management

![Diagram 6](diagrams/diagram-006.svg)

The Fabric platform incorporates mechanisms for managing authentication credentials for Fabric Hub instances and for controlling background daemon processes. These systems are designed to handle sensitive information securely and ensure the reliable operation of various Fabric components.

Authentication credentials, consisting of access and refresh tokens, are stored persistently in a [`credentials.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L507) file. This credential store supports multiple Fabric Hub URLs, allowing users to authenticate with different environments. A key feature of this system is its automatic token refresh mechanism, which attempts to retrieve a new access token using a refresh token when the current access token is nearing expiration. This helps maintain continuous authenticated sessions without requiring repeated manual logins. Operations such as storing, loading, and removing credentials are provided, with appropriate file permissions ([`0600`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L691)) to protect sensitive data. The system also includes utilities for testing credential management by allowing temporary overrides of the credential file path.

For broker-specific authentication, the platform provides distinct [`BrokerCredentials`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/brokercredentials/store.go#L59) management. This system supports both a legacy single-file format and a more flexible multi-file system, where each hub connection's credentials are stored in a separate JSON file within a dedicated directory. This multi-file approach facilitates managing distinct configurations for various hub connections. The [`MultiStore`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/brokercredentials/multistore.go#L52) implementation provides CRUD operations for these credentials and includes a migration utility to transition from the single-file legacy format. It also enforces naming conventions for hub connections and limits the number of "dev-auth" credentials to prevent misconfigurations. Thread-safe access to credential files is ensured through the use of read-write mutexes.

In addition to credential management, the platform offers utilities for controlling background daemon processes. These daemons are long-running processes essential for various Fabric functionalities. The daemon management system enables starting, stopping, and checking the status of these processes. It handles the persistence of operational data, such as Process IDs (PIDs) and command-line arguments, in dedicated files. Log outputs from daemons are redirected to component-specific log files for monitoring and debugging. Furthermore, the system includes tools for managing network port usage. These tools can detect occupied ports, identify the processes listening on specific ports, and, if necessary, gracefully or forcefully terminate processes that are holding required ports. This ensures that Fabric components can consistently acquire and release network resources.

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-database-operations-with-ent-orm"></a>

### Database Operations with Ent ORM

The [`ent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/tx.go#L1) ORM-generated code in [`pkg/ent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent) provides a robust and type-safe layer for interacting with the database, abstracting SQL details into Go objects and methods. This framework is central to managing key entities such as [`AccessPolicy`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/schema/policy.go#L29), [`Agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L28), [`AllowListEntry`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L710), [`ApiKey`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/schema/apikey.go#L34), and [`BrokerDispatch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L825).

For each entity, [`ent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/tx.go#L1) generates a comprehensive set of functionalities:

- **Schema Definitions:** Files like [`pkg/ent/accesspolicy/accesspolicy.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy/accesspolicy.go) define the structure of each entity, including fields, their types, validation rules, and default values. This ensures data integrity and consistency at the application level. Enumerated types, such as [`ScopeType`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/store.go#L808) and [`Effect`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L333) for [`AccessPolicy`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/schema/policy.go#L29), are also defined here.
- **Query Capabilities:** The generated code provides a fluent API for constructing and executing complex database queries. For instance, [`AccessPolicyQuery`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy_query.go#L23) in [`pkg/ent/accesspolicy_query.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy_query.go) allows filtering ([`Where`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/mutation.go#L979)), ordering ([`Order`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/user_query.go#L66)), pagination ([`Limit`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L1018), [`Offset`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/user_query.go#L53)), and fetching related entities ([`WithBindings`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy_query.go#L290) for [`AccessPolicy`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/schema/policy.go#L29)). Predicates, generated by files like [`pkg/ent/accesspolicy/where.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy/where.go), enable granular filtering based on field values and logical operators.
- **CRUD Operations:** The [`ent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/tx.go#L1) framework provides builders for creating, reading, updating, and deleting entities.

  - **Create:** [`AccessPolicyCreate`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy_create.go#L22) in [`pkg/ent/accesspolicy_create.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy_create.go) facilitates the creation of new [`AccessPolicy`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/schema/policy.go#L29) records, supporting single and bulk insertions, as well as upsert operations (insert or update on conflict).
  - **Read:** Queries retrieve entities, often returning them as Go structs like the [`AccessPolicy`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/schema/policy.go#L29) struct defined in [`pkg/ent/accesspolicy.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy.go).
  - **Update:** [`AccessPolicyUpdate`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy_update.go#L23) and [`AccessPolicyUpdateOne`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy_update.go#L498) allow for modifying existing records, including individual fields and relationships.
  - **Delete:** [`AccessPolicyDelete`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy_delete.go#L16) in [`pkg/ent/accesspolicy_delete.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/accesspolicy_delete.go) enables the removal of entities based on specified criteria.
- **Relationships:** The [`ent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/tx.go#L1) ORM handles relationships between entities, such as the [`Bindings`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/handlers_policies.go#L71) edge for [`AccessPolicy`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/schema/policy.go#L29) entities. This allows for querying related data efficiently and managing these connections during create and update operations.

The use of [`ent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/tx.go#L1) ensures that database interactions are type-safe, reducing common errors associated with raw SQL, and promotes a consistent approach to data persistence across the Fabric platform. For more details on the overarching agent management framework, refer to [Fabric Agent Orchestration and Management](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management).

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-fabric-api-definitions-and-core-data-structures"></a>

### Fabric API Definitions and Core Data Structures

![Diagram 7](diagrams/diagram-007.svg)

The Fabric platform defines a comprehensive set of API data structures and interfaces for managing autonomous agents, their configurations, and their interactions. This includes configuration types, agent actions, authentication mechanisms, and telemetry, along with utilities for skill URI parsing and slug generation.

The core configuration for a Fabric agent is managed through the [`FabricConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L437) structure defined in [`pkg/api/types.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go). This structure encapsulates various aspects of an agent's operational environment, such as the [`Harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L23) type (which dictates the execution environment), environment variables ([`Env`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L162)), [`VolumeMount`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L248)s for persistent storage, [`KubernetesConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L314) for orchestrating agents within Kubernetes clusters, and resource specifications ([`ResourceSpec`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L343)). It also includes [`ServiceSpec`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L38)s for defining sidecar processes that run alongside the main agent, [`MCPServerConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L76)s for Micro-Control Plane server configurations, and [`TelemetryConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L364) for managing observability data. Required secrets for agent startup are declared using [`RequiredSecret`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L664).

The behavior of an agent is guided by the [`Harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L23) interface, specified in [`pkg/api/harness.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go). This interface sets the contract for different agent execution environments, detailing how they provide configurations, set up environments, provision resources, and handle interactions. Implementations of this interface define methods for actions such as [`Provision`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L36) (for setting up the agent's environment), [`GetEnv`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L26) (for retrieving environment variables), and [`GetCommand`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L27) (for constructing the command to execute a task). Optional interfaces like [`AuthSettingsApplier`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L70), [`TelemetrySettingsApplier`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L77), and [`MCPSettingsApplier`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L87) allow harnesses to integrate authentication, telemetry, and MCP configurations directly into their native settings. The capabilities of these harnesses, including support for various features like run limits, system prompts, authentication types, and MCP transports, are declaratively described using structures like [`HarnessAdvancedCapabilities`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness_capabilities.go#L72) in [`pkg/api/harness_capabilities.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness_capabilities.go). Declarative authentication preflight metadata for harnesses is also defined, detailing environmental and file requirements for different authentication types in [`pkg/api/harness_auth_metadata.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness_auth_metadata.go).

Agent interactions are standardized through defined constants in [`pkg/api/agent_actions.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/agent_actions.go). These constants represent a range of actions an agent can perform or respond to, including [`AgentActionStatus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/agent_actions.go#L20), [`AgentActionStart`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/agent_actions.go#L21), [`AgentActionStop`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/agent_actions.go#L22), [`AgentActionMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/agent_actions.go#L25), and [`AgentActionExec`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/agent_actions.go#L28). A utility function, [`RuntimeBrokerAgentActionMethod`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/agent_actions.go#L46), maps these actions to specific HTTP methods for routing through a runtime broker.

Authentication credentials and configurations are centralized in the [`AuthConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/auth.go#L31) and [`ResolvedAuth`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L315) structures within [`pkg/api/types.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go). These structures manage the chosen authentication method, environment variables, and file mappings required for secure credential injection into agent containers.

Telemetry settings are configured via [`TelemetryConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L364) in [`pkg/api/types.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go), enabling the management of observability data, including cloud, hub, and local configurations, filtering options, and resource attributes.

Utilities for skill URI parsing are managed by the [`SkillURI`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/skill_uri.go#L24) struct and associated functions in [`pkg/api/skill_uri.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/skill_uri.go). These functions, such as [`ParseSkillURI`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/skill_uri.go#L78), enable the parsing of various URI formats into structured components, facilitating the resolution and fetching of agent skills. [Skill Resolution Mechanisms](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-skill-resolution-mechanisms) provides further details on how skills are resolved.

URL-safe slugs and unique identifiers are generated and managed using utilities found in [`pkg/api/slug.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/slug.go). Functions like [`Slugify`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/slug.go#L45) convert strings into URL-safe, lowercase forms, while [`MakeProjectID`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/slug.go#L138) constructs hosted-format project IDs. These utilities ensure consistent naming conventions and identifier management across the platform.

The [`ResolveContent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/content.go#L32) function in [`pkg/api/content.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/content.go) provides a mechanism for interpreting content strings, allowing them to be either inline text or [`file://`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/common.go#L115) URIs that reference local or relative file paths. This supports flexible content loading for agent configurations and instructions.

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-harness-abstraction-and-provisioning"></a>

### Harness Abstraction and Provisioning

![Diagram 8](diagrams/diagram-008.svg)

Harnesses in Fabric abstract the execution environments for agents, defining how an agent is provisioned, its commands are constructed, and its configuration is loaded. The [`pkg/harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness) directory implements the core logic for managing these harnesses, centralizing authentication, configuration parsing, and environment setup.

The [`Harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L23) interface is central to achieving LLM agnosticism, allowing agents to operate across different underlying Large Language Models and execution contexts. Fabric supports various harness types, primarily determined by the [`Resolve`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/secret/secret.go#L131) function in [`pkg/harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness).

- **Container-Script Harnesses** ([`ContainerScriptHarness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness/container_script_harness.go#L41)) are used when a [`provisioner`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/settings_v1.go#L741) block is present in the agent's configuration. These harnesses manage the staging of configuration files and Python scripts, such as [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91) and [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130), into an agent's home directory. This process sets up a [`pre-start`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/common.go#L581) hook that invokes [`fabrictool harness provision`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L10) inside the agent's container.
- **Declarative Generic Harnesses** are utilized when no custom [`provisioner`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/settings_v1.go#L741) is defined but the agent's configuration includes declarative settings like [`Command`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/output.go#L58), [`Capabilities`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L354), or [`EnvTemplate`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/settings_v1.go#L749). This allows for defining harness behavior purely through configuration files without custom code.
- A **Generic Harness** serves as a baseline implementation, providing default capabilities, environment variables, and command generation when more specific configurations are absent.

A key aspect of harness management is authentication. The system gathers authentication configuration ([`api.AuthConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L443)) from diverse sources, including environment variables, well-known file paths (e.g., [`application_default_credentials.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L1270)), and resolved secrets provided by the Fabric Hub. Functions like [`GatherAuth`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness/auth.go#L33) in [`pkg/harness/auth.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness/auth.go) are responsible for collecting these details, with [`GatherAuthWithEnv`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness/auth.go#L50) prioritizing values from an [`env`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L162) map. The system can automatically detect the most suitable authentication type (e.g., "api-key", "auth-file", "vertex-ai") based on the available credentials and configuration, and it validates the integrity of the resolved authentication configuration before use. Config-driven authentication metadata, specified in [`config.HarnessAuthMetadata`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L219), allows for dynamic definition of required environment variables and file secrets. For more details on the design of this system, refer to [Authentication and Security Design](#design-specifications-and-architecture-authentication-and-security-design).

Harnesses also manage the generation of environment variables and command-line arguments for agent execution. They support templating for environment variables, allowing for dynamic values such as agent names. Furthermore, harnesses facilitate the injection of agent instructions and system prompts into specific files within the agent's home directory, ensuring consistent operational guidelines. Multi-Channel Proxy (MCP) server configurations and telemetry settings are also staged by the harnesses.

The [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) helper script is fundamental for Python-based harnesses, standardizing authentication, instruction projection, MCP server configuration, and file operations. This script's content is embedded and written to the agent's environment during provisioning, either by vendoring or injection, depending on the [`provisioner.lib`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L143) mode. For CLI operations related to harness configuration, see [Harness Configuration Management and Synchronization](#command-line-interface-cli-operations-harness-configuration-management-and-synchronization).

<a id="fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-local-agent-cache-for-shell-completion"></a>

### Local Agent Cache for Shell Completion

![Diagram 9](diagrams/diagram-009.svg)

A local, filesystem-based cache enhances the responsiveness and reliability of shell completion for agent names. This cache, managed by the [`pkg/agentcache`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agentcache) directory, stores lists of agent names associated with specific projects. By retrieving agent names from a local cache rather than repeatedly querying the Hub API, shell completion operates more quickly, especially in scenarios where the Hub API might be slow or temporarily unavailable.

The cache uses [`CacheEntry`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agentcache/cache.go#L35) structs to store agent names and their last update times, which are then marshaled to and from JSON for persistent storage. A unique cache key, generated from the project path using a SHA256 hash, ensures that each project's agent list is stored in a distinct, filesystem-safe file. This allows for efficient retrieval and prevents naming conflicts. The system is designed to handle missing or corrupted cache files gracefully, treating them as cache misses without generating errors, thereby prioritizing application robustness. The cache can be completely cleared when necessary to ensure fresh data. This mechanism complements the broader agent management capabilities discussed in [Agent Lifecycle Management and Orchestration](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-agent-lifecycle-management-and-orchestration).

<a id="command-line-interface-cli-operations"></a>

## Command-Line Interface (CLI) Operations

![Diagram 10](diagrams/diagram-010.svg)

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) command-line interface provides the primary means for users and automated systems to interact with FABRIC agents and manage the platform. This CLI tool, defined within [`cmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd), offers functionalities spanning agent lifecycle, configuration management, runtime broker operations, container image building, and workspace navigation. It is structured using the [`spf13/cobra`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L36) library to provide a consistent and extensible command set, with support for JSON output for programmatic consumption.

A core capability of the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI is its comprehensive [Agent Lifecycle Management and Orchestration](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-agent-lifecycle-management-and-orchestration). The [`fabric attach`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1) command, implemented in [`cmd/attach.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/attach.go), allows users to connect to interactive sessions of running FABRIC agents, whether they are managed locally or by a remote FABRIC Hub. The command employs a dual attachment mechanism to support various deployment scenarios, and includes robust agent discovery. The [`fabric create`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) command, detailed in [`cmd/create.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go), provisions new agents, handling template resolution and configuration overrides, while the [`fabric delete`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) command in [`cmd/delete.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/delete.go) facilitates agent removal, including cleanup of associated resources. Common agent operations, such as running agents and loading configurations, are supported through shared utilities in [`cmd/common.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/common.go).

For managing the execution environments of agents, the CLI includes functionality for runtime broker operations. The [`runtime-broker`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L2741) command group, primarily defined in [`cmd/broker.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/broker.go), allows a local machine to function as a runtime broker, executing agents on behalf of a Hub. This includes commands for registering, deregistering, starting, stopping, and restarting the broker daemon, as well as managing project providers and monitoring status. The [`broker_test.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/check-project-compat-literals.sh#L148) file within the same directory contains tests verifying the command's metadata and flag registration.

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI also enables the building of container images for agents. The [`fabric build`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L1) command, found in [`cmd/build.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go), orchestrates the creation of container images from [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138)s within harness configuration directories. It supports local builds using Docker or Podman, and integrates with Google Cloud Build for more complex or multi-platform builds. After a successful build, it updates the associated harness configuration with the new image reference and can synchronize these changes with a FABRIC Hub.

Navigation and project management are supported by commands like [`fabric cdw`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cdw.go#L24), implemented in [`cmd/cdw.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cdw.go). This command helps users quickly change their current directory to an agent's workspace or a Git branch's worktree, then spawns a new interactive shell in that location. For system maintenance, the [`fabric clean`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1) command in [`cmd/clean.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/clean.go) removes FABRIC project configurations, with options to unlink from a Hub if connected.

Configuration management for the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI is handled by the [`fabric config`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1) command group in [`cmd/config.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/config.go). This group allows users to list, set, get, and validate [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) settings, and includes utilities for migrating legacy settings and navigating configuration directories. The [`fabric config schema`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/server.go#L25) command, defined in [`cmd/config_schema.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/config_schema.go), displays the schema for agent configuration files.

Diagnostic capabilities are provided by the [`fabric doctor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L12) command in [`cmd/doctor.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/doctor.go), which verifies system prerequisites and runtime configurations. Advanced CLI features also include explicit CLI operational modes (human, assistant, agent) that restrict command availability, as defined and enforced in [`cmd/cli_mode.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cli_mode.go). Shell completion for agent names, fetching suggestions from both local sources and the Hub, is facilitated by functions in [`cmd/completion_helper.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/completion_helper.go).

<a id="command-line-interface-cli-operations-agent-lifecycle-and-management-commands"></a>

### Agent Lifecycle and Management Commands

![Diagram 11](diagrams/diagram-011.svg)

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI provides commands for managing FABRIC agents throughout their lifecycle. This includes the ability to create, delete, and interact with agents.

Agent creation is handled by the [`create`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/agents.go#L42) command, which allows provisioning new FABRIC agents. This can be done for local agents using an agent manager or for remote agents managed by a Fabric Hub. The process involves template resolution, configuration overrides, and integration with skill resolution mechanisms. Agents can be provisioned on disk or through the Hub, and the command facilitates the setup of their initial configuration.

For managing agents that are no longer needed, the [`delete`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/storage/gcs.go#L219) command removes FABRIC agents. Users can delete specific agents by name or opt to remove all stopped agents. Deletion operations can target agents managed locally or through the Hub, ensuring that associated containers, files, and Git branches are cleaned up.

Interaction with running agents is facilitated by the [`attach`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L409) command, which connects to interactive sessions of FABRIC agents. This command supports attaching to local agents via the container runtime and to remote agents managed by a Fabric Hub through a WebSocket connection. The system includes mechanisms to discover agents, whether they are local or Hub-managed, and to provide user-friendly error messages if an agent is not found or is not in a running state. The implementation of [`attach`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L409) in [`cmd/attach.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/attach.go) distinguishes between local and Hub-managed agents, ensuring appropriate connection methods are used.

Beyond creation and deletion, other common operational utilities for agents are provided. For example, [`cmd/common.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/common.go) contains helper functions for starting or resuming agents, parsing labels from command-line arguments, and loading agent configurations.

The [`cdw`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cdw.go#L31) command in [`cmd/cdw.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cdw.go) allows users to change their current directory to an agent's workspace or a Git branch's worktree, then spawns a new shell in that directory. This streamlines navigation to project-specific environments.

Additionally, the [`clean`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L19) command in [`cmd/clean.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/clean.go) removes [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) project configurations. This involves locating the project directory, checking its link status with a Fabric Hub, offering to unlink from the Hub if connected and reachable, and then removing the local project directory. This effectively reverses the project initialization process.

<a id="command-line-interface-cli-operations-harness-configuration-management-and-synchronization"></a>

### Harness Configuration Management and Synchronization

![Diagram 12](diagrams/diagram-012.svg)

The Fabric platform provides a comprehensive set of command-line operations for managing agent harness configurations, which define how agents are provisioned and interact with their environments. These operations facilitate listing, resetting, upgrading, and synchronizing harness configurations with the Fabric Hub.

Harness configurations can be installed from various sources, including local paths, URLs, or remote repositories. This flexibility allows developers to easily integrate custom harnesses or leverage pre-defined ones. The CLI supports installation to a local directory for individual use or directly to a Hub for shared access across a team. The [`fabric harness-config install`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L1) command, implemented by [`harnessConfigInstallCmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/harness_config_install.go#L29) in [`cmd/harness_config_install.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/harness_config_install.go), orchestrates this process, with [`resolveInstallSource`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/harness_config_install.go#L107) handling the parsing of diverse input types.

Once installed, configurations can be listed to inspect their details, reset to their default states, or upgraded to newer versions. A key aspect of harness management is synchronization with the Fabric Hub. The [`harnessConfigCmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/harness_config.go#L32) within [`cmd/harness_config.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/harness_config.go) provides subcommands to [`push`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/bridge.go#L58) local configurations to the Hub, [`pull`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L107) configurations from the Hub to the local filesystem, and [`sync`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/mock.go#L101) to perform a bidirectional synchronization. The [`pullHarnessConfigFromHub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/harness_config.go#L752) and [`syncHarnessConfigToHub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/harness_config.go#L535) functions, specifically tested in [`cmd/harness_config_hub_test.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/harness_config_hub_test.go), ensure robust two-phase downloads with hash verification and reliable updates to local and remote configurations. These mechanisms ensure consistency and facilitate collaboration across development environments.

<a id="command-line-interface-cli-operations-runtime-broker-operations-and-daemon-management"></a>

### Runtime Broker Operations and Daemon Management

![Diagram 13](diagrams/diagram-013.svg)

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI provides a dedicated set of commands for managing a Runtime Broker, which enables a local machine to execute agents on behalf of a Fabric Hub. These commands cover the entire lifecycle of a Runtime Broker, from initial registration to ongoing management and monitoring.

To begin, a Runtime Broker must be registered with a Fabric Hub. The CLI facilitates this process, establishing a connection between the local broker and the remote Hub. During registration, the broker's identity is recorded with the Hub, and necessary credentials are securely stored locally, often involving a two-phase process for robust authentication. Conversely, a registered Runtime Broker can be deregistered from the Hub, removing its association and cleaning up local credentials. This operation typically includes user confirmation prompts to prevent accidental removal.

The Runtime Broker operates as a daemon, allowing agents to run in the background. The CLI provides commands to start, stop, and restart this daemon process. When starting the broker, it can either run in the foreground for debugging or as a background daemon, leveraging a daemon management utility to ensure it persists across user sessions. The [`restart`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/agents.go#L60) command combines the stop and start operations, ensuring a clean refresh of the broker service.

Beyond lifecycle management, the CLI also supports configuring the broker's interaction with projects and Hub connections. A Runtime Broker can be designated as a "project provider," meaning it is authorized to execute agents for a specific project on the Hub. This involves registering the broker with the project and, optionally, setting it as the default provider for that project. The corresponding command allows for withdrawing this provider status. The CLI also enables users to list all configured Hub connections the local broker is aware of, providing an overview of its operational context.

For monitoring and diagnostics, a dedicated command provides a comprehensive status report for the Runtime Broker. This report includes the local server's operational status, the daemon's activity, its registration status with the Hub, and its role as a project provider. This functionality can also extend to querying the status of remote brokers directly through the Hub. The CLI ensures that operations are performed within the correct project context, either by inferring it from the current directory or allowing explicit specification via command-line flags. User prompts are integrated into significant operations, such as deregistration or changing default project providers, to ensure intentional actions.

<a id="command-line-interface-cli-operations-advanced-cli-mode-restrictions-and-completion"></a>

### Advanced CLI Mode Restrictions and Completion

![Diagram 14](diagrams/diagram-014.svg)

CLI operational modes in Fabric define the behavior and available commands based on the context in which the CLI is executed. Three primary modes exist: [`human`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L15), [`assistant`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L77), and [`agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L28). The system resolves the active mode by first checking the [`FABRIC_CLI_MODE`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cli_mode.go#L102) environment variable and then falling back to configured settings. Once resolved, CLI mode restrictions are applied dynamically, which filters the set of available commands. This ensures that agents or automated processes are prevented from executing commands intended only for human interaction, thereby enhancing security and preventing unintended actions. The resolution and enforcement of these modes are managed in [`cmd/cli_mode.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cli_mode.go).

For an improved user experience, particularly in interactive shell environments, the CLI also provides mechanisms for shell completion. This functionality suggests agent names as arguments for commands, fetching these suggestions from both local configurations and the Fabric Hub. This process, defined in [`cmd/completion_helper.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/completion_helper.go), includes caching and silent error handling to maintain responsiveness even when external sources are slow or unavailable. This capability streamlines command input and reduces errors for users.

<a id="command-line-interface-cli-operations-fabrictool-container-init-and-lifecycle-management"></a>

### Fabrictool: Container Init and Lifecycle Management

![Diagram 15](diagrams/diagram-015.svg)
