[`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) serves as the primary entry point and process manager (PID 1) within Fabric agent containers. Its central role, defined by the [`initCmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/init.go#L25) in [`cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go), is to orchestrate the agent's lifecycle, manage child processes, and ensure stable operation. This involves supervising a main child process, reaping zombie processes to prevent resource leaks, and forwarding signals for graceful shutdowns.

A key function of [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) is managing secrets and environment setup within the container. It decodes and stages secrets, making them available to child processes and lifecycle hooks. For example, [`setupHostUser`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go#L1171) ([`cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go)) adjusts user IDs and group IDs to ensure the agent operates with appropriate permissions.

[`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) is also responsible for Git workspace operations. The [`gitCloneWorkspace`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/provision/provision.go#L301) function ([`cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go)) handles cloning repositories, managing authentication, selecting branches, and configuring Git credential helpers, ensuring the agent has access to its code and data. Further details on how [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) acts as a Git credential helper can be found in [Fabrictool: Authentication and `gh` CLI Integration](#command-line-interface-cli-operations-fabrictool-authentication-and-gh-cli-integration).

Coordination with the Fabric Hub is another critical aspect. [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) actively updates the Hub on the agent's status, including phases like [`state.PhaseRunning`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/list.go#L644) or [`state.PhaseCloning`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/list.go#L183), and handles heartbeats and token refreshes. It also enforces resource limits such as maximum duration ([`FABRIC_MAX_DURATION`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L618)), turns ([`FABRIC_MAX_TURNS`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L612)), and model calls ([`FABRIC_MAX_MODEL_CALLS`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L615)), signaling when these limits are exceeded to the Hub. The various states and their management are implemented in functions like [`handleLimitsExceeded`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go#L1029) and [`watchLimitsTriggerFile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go#L1155) within [`cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go).

<a id="command-line-interface-cli-operations-fabrictool-harness-hook-processing-and-telemetry"></a>

### Fabrictool: Harness Hook Processing and Telemetry

![Diagram 16](diagrams/diagram-016.svg)

[`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) plays a central role in processing agent harness hook events, which are crucial for real-time communication and status updates within the Fabric ecosystem. When an agent performs an action or reaches a specific state, it emits a hook event, which [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) intercepts. This tool normalizes event data, which can come from various "dialects" (e.g., [`claude`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L27), [`gemini`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L26), [`codex`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L83)), ensuring consistency across different types of agents and platforms.

Once normalized, these events are routed through a series of handlers. These handlers are responsible for different aspects of agent management and observability:

- **Status Updates**: Events can trigger updates to the agent's current operational status, indicating if it's waiting for input, blocked, or has completed a task.
- **Logging**: Detailed information about the event is logged, providing a comprehensive audit trail of agent activities.
- **User Prompts**: If an agent requires user interaction, the event can trigger a prompt, facilitating real-time communication between the agent and a human operator.
- **Hub Communication**: Critical events are communicated back to the Fabric Hub, the central orchestration component, to maintain an up-to-date view of all running agents.
- **Telemetry Collection**: Events contribute to telemetry data, enabling the collection of metrics, traces, and logs that are essential for monitoring agent performance and behavior.

The [`hookCmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/hook.go#L34) in [`cmd/fabrictool/commands/hook.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/hook.go) is the primary mechanism for this processing. It enables [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) to act as an intermediary, translating raw agent events into structured information that can be consumed by other Fabric components, thereby facilitating the intelligent orchestration and management of agents. [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) also directly supports [`ask_user`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13) and [`task_completed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13) signals, allowing agents to explicitly communicate their need for input or the completion of a task. The [`statusCmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/status.go#L22) in [`cmd/fabrictool/commands/status.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/status.go) is dedicated to updating an agent's activity status, dispatching to various functions that update handlers, log events, and report to the Hub. These mechanisms collectively ensure that the Fabric platform has a real-time, comprehensive understanding of each agent's state and progress.

<a id="command-line-interface-cli-operations-fabrictool-authentication-and-gh-cli-integration"></a>

### Fabrictool: Authentication and `gh` CLI Integration

![Diagram 17](diagrams/diagram-017.svg)

[`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) provides functionalities to manage Git credentials, particularly for refreshing GitHub App tokens, and integrates with the [`gh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go#L147) CLI by injecting fresh GitHub tokens before execution.

The [`credentialHelperCmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/credential_helper.go#L38) within [`cmd/fabrictool/commands/credential_helper.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/credential_helper.go) operates as a Git credential helper. When configured, it automatically provides Git with up-to-date GitHub tokens. This is especially useful in continuous integration/continuous deployment (CI/CD) environments where GitHub App tokens are often short-lived and require frequent refreshing. The credential helper checks if GitHub App integration is enabled and attempts to read or refresh a token from the Fabric Hub. If a valid token is obtained, it is supplied to Git, enabling seamless authenticated Git operations.

Additionally, the [`ghWrapperCmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/gh_wrapper.go#L34) in [`cmd/fabrictool/commands/gh_wrapper.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/gh_wrapper.go) acts as a wrapper around the [`gh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go#L147) command-line interface. When [`gh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go#L147) is invoked, [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) intercepts the call, fetches a fresh GitHub token from the Hub, and injects it into the environment as [`GH_TOKEN`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/copilot/README.md?plain=1#L42) before executing the actual [`gh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go#L147) binary. This ensures that the [`gh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go#L147) CLI always operates with a current and valid token. The wrapper is designed to replace the current process with the [`gh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go#L147) binary, which is an efficient way to transfer control while preserving the environment. The wrapper also includes logic to locate the legitimate [`gh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go#L147) binary and can be configured to respect user-provided [`GITHUB_TOKEN`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L1612) values if [`FABRIC_USER_GITHUB_TOKEN`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/httpdispatcher.go#L489) is set to "true". For more details on the [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44)'s overall functionality within agent containers, refer to [Fabrictool: Container Init and Lifecycle Management](#command-line-interface-cli-operations-fabrictool-container-init-and-lifecycle-management).

<a id="command-line-interface-cli-operations-fabrictool-gce-metadata-server-emulation-and-diagnostics"></a>

### Fabrictool: GCE Metadata Server Emulation and Diagnostics

![Diagram 18](diagrams/diagram-018.svg)

[`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) includes functionality for emulating the Google Compute Engine (GCE) metadata server within agent containers. This emulation provides a consistent interface for agents to retrieve information about their environment and credentials, even when not running directly on a GCE VM. The local metadata server can fetch credentials via the Fabric Hub API, offering a secure way for agents to obtain necessary authentication tokens for GCP services.

To ensure the proper functioning of this emulation, [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) provides diagnostic capabilities. The [`metadataCmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/metadata.go#L22) within [`cmd/fabrictool/commands/metadata.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/metadata.go) offers tools for checking the health and configuration of the emulated metadata server. Specifically, the [`metadataStatusCmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/metadata.go#L28) subcommand assesses:

- **Configuration**: It verifies environment variables such as [`FABRIC_METADATA_MODE`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L1289) and [`FABRIC_METADATA_PORT`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/fabrictool/metadata/server.go#L95), which dictate how the emulation operates and on which port it listens.
- **Connectivity**: It checks if the configured port is open and accessible, ensuring agents can communicate with the emulated server.
- **Endpoints**: It validates the reachability and responsiveness of key metadata server endpoints, including the health endpoint and token endpoints, which are crucial for credential acquisition.
- **Network Rules**: It inspects [`iptables`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L1286) rules to confirm that network traffic is correctly routed to the emulated server, preventing common misconfigurations that could block communication.

These diagnostic checks, as detailed in the [`runDoctor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/doctor.go#L48) function within [`cmd/fabrictool/commands/doctor.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/doctor.go), ensure that the agent's environment is correctly set up for GCP integration. The [`checkGCPMetadata`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/doctor.go#L295) function, for instance, specifically validates the local GCP metadata server's reachability and its ability to vend access tokens when in "assign" mode. This proactive diagnostic approach helps in troubleshooting and maintaining the reliability of agent operations that depend on GCP services.

<a id="fabric-web-user-interface"></a>

## Fabric Web User Interface

![Diagram 19](diagrams/diagram-019.svg)

The Fabric Agent Orchestration Platform provides a client-side single-page application (SPA) located in the [`web`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web) directory, which serves as the primary user interface for managing agents, projects, and brokers. This dynamic interface enables users to interact with the platform through real-time state synchronization via Server-Sent Events (SSE) and direct API interactions.

The architecture is centered around a frontend built with Lit web components and utilizes the Shoelace UI library. While Node.js and npm are used for client-side asset compilation and bundling with Vite, the Go [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) binary serves the compiled web assets at runtime. This binary also handles server-side functionalities such as OAuth, sessions, SSE, and API routing, which are activated when the [`--enable-web`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L29) flag is used.

Key to the application's responsiveness is its state management system, implemented by the [`StateManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts#L67) class in [`web/src/client/state.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts). This system maintains the application's state for agents, projects, and brokers, synchronizing data with the backend through the [`SSEClient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/sse-client.ts#L42) in [`web/src/client/sse-client.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/sse-client.ts). The [`SSEClient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/sse-client.ts#L42) connects to the [`/events`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/README.md?plain=1#L78) endpoint, automatically reconnects upon disconnection, and handles authentication checks to ensure continuous data flow. It processes updates using delta merging and dispatches custom events to ensure the UI reflects real-time changes. The [`index.html`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/vite.config.ts#L66) file, located in [`web/index.html`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/index.html), serves as the main entry point, bootstrapping the client-side application and applying theme preferences based on user settings or system defaults.

All API interactions are centralized through an [`apiFetch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts#L45) wrapper, defined in [`web/src/client/api.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts). This wrapper manages credentials, logs slow requests, and handles specific HTTP error responses, such as 401 (unauthorized) and 403 (forbidden), to ensure secure communication and proper access control. Further details on UI components and design patterns can be found in [UI Component Ecosystem and Design Patterns](#fabric-web-user-interface-ui-component-ecosystem-and-design-patterns), and styling information is available in [Theming, Styling, and Accessibility](#fabric-web-user-interface-theming-styling-and-accessibility). For advanced details on client-side architecture and routing, refer to [Client-Side Architecture and Routing](#fabric-web-user-interface-client-side-architecture-and-routing).

<a id="fabric-web-user-interface-client-side-architecture-and-routing"></a>

### Client-Side Architecture and Routing

![Diagram 20](diagrams/diagram-020.svg)

The client-side single-page application (SPA) provides the user interface for the Fabric Agent Orchestration Platform. The Go [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) binary serves the compiled web assets and handles server-side functionalities such as OAuth, sessions, Server-Sent Events (SSE), and API routing. Node.js and [`npm`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L90) are used during the build process with [`Vite`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L35) to compile and bundle client assets.

The core of the client-side application is located in the [`web/src`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src) directory. The main entry point, [`web/src/client/main.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/main.ts), manages the application's initial setup. This includes injecting CSS, configuring the [`Shoelace`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L70) UI library, and hydrating data from server-side rendering (SSR) to populate initial page and user information.

Client-side routing is also handled by [`web/src/client/main.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/main.ts), which defines routes that map URL patterns to specific page components. It dynamically imports and renders these components, enabling smooth navigation within the SPA without full page reloads.

The application integrates the [`Shoelace`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L70) UI library, a collection of web components, for its user interface elements. This library is configured and its assets are managed via [`setBasePath`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/main.ts#L43) during the application's initialization.

The [`StateManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts#L67) class, found in [`web/src/client/state.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts), is central to managing the application's real-time state. It maintains [`AppState`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts#L44) for agents, projects, and brokers, synchronizing data with the backend using an [`SSEClient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/sse-client.ts#L42). This client, defined in [`web/src/client/sse-client.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/sse-client.ts), connects to the [`/events`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/README.md?plain=1#L78) endpoint to receive real-time updates via Server-Sent Events. The [`StateManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts#L67) processes these [`update`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/users.go#L32) events, performs delta merging, and dispatches custom events to ensure the UI remains reactive and up-to-date. For more details on real-time state management, refer to [Real-time State Management and SSE](#fabric-web-user-interface-real-time-state-management-and-sse).

API interactions are centralized through the [`apiFetch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts#L45) function in [`web/src/client/api.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts). This wrapper around the standard [`fetch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L107) API handles credentials, logs slow requests, and manages HTTP error responses, such as redirecting to [`/login`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L1138) on a 401 (Unauthorized) status or dispatching an access-denied event on a 403 (Forbidden) status. For more information, see [API Communication and Error Handling](#fabric-web-user-interface-api-communication-and-error-handling).

The application's UI components, built with [`LitElement`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L173), are located in [`web/src/components`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components). These include the main application shell ([`FabricApp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/app-shell.ts#L59)), shared reusable components, and specific pages for administrative tasks, agent management, and project oversight. [UI Component Ecosystem and Design Patterns](#fabric-web-user-interface-ui-component-ecosystem-and-design-patterns) provides a deeper dive into these components. Theming and styling are managed through [`web/src/styles`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles), utilizing CSS custom properties for a consistent look and support for light and dark modes. See [Theming, Styling, and Accessibility](#fabric-web-user-interface-theming-styling-and-accessibility) for further details.

<a id="fabric-web-user-interface-real-time-state-management-and-sse"></a>

### Real-time State Management and SSE

![Diagram 21](diagrams/diagram-021.svg)

The [`StateManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts#L67) class in [`web/src/client/state.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts) is central to managing the application's client-side state for entities such as agents, projects, and brokers. This class ensures that the user interface remains synchronized with backend data through Server-Sent Events (SSE). The [`SSEClient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/sse-client.ts#L42) in [`web/src/client/sse-client.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/sse-client.ts) establishes and maintains a connection to the backend's [`/events`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/README.md?plain=1#L78) endpoint, facilitating real-time updates.

The [`StateManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts#L67) processes incoming [`update`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/users.go#L32) events by applying delta merging, which efficiently updates only the changed parts of the application state, reducing the overhead of full state refreshes. It also manages view-scoped subscriptions, allowing different parts of the application to subscribe only to the data relevant to their current context. After processing updates, the [`StateManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts#L67) dispatches custom events, such as [`agents-updated`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts#L58), to trigger UI reactivity and ensure that components re-render as needed to reflect the latest state. The [`SSEClient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/sse-client.ts#L42) handles automatic reconnection with exponential backoff and performs authentication checks to ensure continuous and secure data flow.

For more information on the overall client-side architecture, see [Client-Side Architecture and Routing](#fabric-web-user-interface-client-side-architecture-and-routing). For details on the API communication patterns, refer to [API Communication and Error Handling](#fabric-web-user-interface-api-communication-and-error-handling).

<a id="fabric-web-user-interface-api-communication-and-error-handling"></a>

### API Communication and Error Handling

![Diagram 22](diagrams/diagram-022.svg)

The [`apiFetch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts#L45) function in [`web/src/client/api.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts) centralizes all interactions with the backend API. This wrapper around the standard [`fetch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L107) API ensures consistent handling of credentials for authenticated requests and includes built-in logging for slow requests to aid in performance monitoring. Crucially, it manages specific HTTP error responses related to authentication and access control: an HTTP 401 response triggers a redirect to the [`/login`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L1138) page, while an HTTP 403 response dispatches a custom [`fabric:access-denied`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts#L21) event, providing a standardized mechanism for the UI to react to unauthorized access attempts. Error parsing utilities, [`extractApiError`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts#L96) and [`parseApiError`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts#L129), convert raw API error responses into structured [`ApiErrorInfo`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts#L117) objects for easier consumption by the frontend.

<a id="fabric-web-user-interface-ui-component-ecosystem-and-design-patterns"></a>

### UI Component Ecosystem and Design Patterns

![Diagram 23](diagrams/diagram-023.svg)

The Fabric web user interface is built as a single-page application (SPA), primarily using [`LitElement`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L173)-based web components. This component-driven architecture facilitates a modular and reactive user experience for managing agents, projects, and brokers. The application shell, defined by the [`FabricApp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/app-shell.ts#L59) class in [`web/src/components/app-shell.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/app-shell.ts), serves as the top-level container, orchestrating the overall layout, navigation, and global UI state. It manages elements such as the header, breadcrumbs, navigation, and a debug panel, handling responsive design and persistence of UI preferences.

A comprehensive set of shared UI components, located in [`web/src/components/shared`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/shared), provides consistent functionality and appearance across the application. These components address various needs, including status indicators and real-time notifications, debugging and observability tools (e.g., for connection status, subscriptions, and event logs), and robust data display and editing capabilities. For instance, [`FabricJsonBrowser`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/shared/json-browser.ts#L29) provides interactive viewing of JSON data, while [`FabricAgentLogViewer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/shared/agent-log-viewer.ts#L53) and [`FabricAgentMessageViewer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/shared/agent-message-viewer.ts#L65) manage detailed agent logs and message streams. File and directory management is handled by components such as [`FabricFileBrowser`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/shared/file-browser.ts#L436) and [`FabricFileEditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/shared/file-editor.ts#L189), which integrate syntax highlighting and Markdown rendering.

The user profile and settings, managed by components in [`web/src/components/profile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/profile), provide a dedicated area for user-specific configurations. [`FabricProfileNav`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/profile/profile-nav.ts#L61) offers responsive navigation for profile sections, displaying user information, while [`FabricProfileShell`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/profile/profile-shell.ts#L43) provides the main layout for these sections, handling navigation states and title updates.

The application also features numerous dedicated pages, defined as [`LitElement`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L173) components within [`web/src/components/pages`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages). These pages facilitate interaction with the backend API for specific functionalities, encompassing administrative tasks, agent management, broker oversight, and project configurations. Examples include pages for listing and creating agents, configuring agent details, managing administrative groups and integrations, and overseeing skill registries. Common design patterns across these pages include leveraging [`apiFetch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts#L45) for backend communication and [`stateManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/state.ts#L515) for real-time updates and reactive UI, ensuring that the interface remains synchronized with the system's state. The web client also incorporates features for [Real-time State Management and SSE](#fabric-web-user-interface-real-time-state-management-and-sse) and [API Communication and Error Handling](#fabric-web-user-interface-api-communication-and-error-handling) to maintain a dynamic and responsive user experience.

<a id="fabric-web-user-interface-theming-styling-and-accessibility"></a>

### Theming, Styling, and Accessibility

![Diagram 24](diagrams/diagram-024.svg)

The Fabric web user interface employs a centralized styling system to ensure a consistent look and feel, support theming, and integrate effectively with the Shoelace UI library. This system is primarily defined within the [`web/src/styles`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles) directory.

The core theming is established in [`web/src/styles/theme.css`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/theme.css), which leverages CSS custom properties, all prefixed with [`--fabric-`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L208). This approach defines a comprehensive color palette and semantic colors, such as [`--fabric-primary`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L236) and [`--fabric-bg`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L288), providing a foundation for the application's visual design. The styling system includes support for both light and dark modes, which can be activated through explicit selectors like [`.sl-theme-dark`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/theme.css#L288) or [`[data-theme='dark']`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/theme.css#L289), and automatically based on user system preferences via [`@media (prefers-color-scheme: dark)`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L255). Integration with the Shoelace UI library is achieved by mapping these [`--fabric-`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L208) custom properties to Shoelace's own custom properties, ensuring a unified visual style across all components. Layout variables, font stacks, font sizes, spacing values, and border radii are also defined within this file to maintain consistency.

In addition to theming, the application utilizes a set of reusable utility classes defined in [`web/src/styles/utilities.css`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/utilities.css). These classes, also prefixed with [`fabric-`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/common.go#L572), provide atomic styling for common UI patterns. Examples include utilities for [`flex`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/utilities.css#L27) and [`grid`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/utilities.css#L52) layouts (e.g., [`fabric-flex`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/utilities.css#L27), [`fabric-grid`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/utilities.css#L52)), consistent spacing (e.g., [`fabric-gap-1`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/utilities.css#L60)), and typographic styles (e.g., [`fabric-text-xs`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/utilities.css#L83), [`fabric-font-medium`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/utilities.css#L105)). These utilities contribute to responsive design, accessibility (such as [`fabric-sr-only`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/styles/utilities.css#L194) for screen reader-only content), and standardized interactive states. The utility-first approach and extensive use of CSS variables help streamline UI development and ensure a cohesive user experience across the application. Further details on the overall architecture and component ecosystem can be found in [Client-Side Architecture and Routing](#fabric-web-user-interface-client-side-architecture-and-routing) and [UI Component Ecosystem and Design Patterns](#fabric-web-user-interface-ui-component-ecosystem-and-design-patterns).

<a id="fabric-web-user-interface-end-to-end-testing-for-real-time-features"></a>

### End-to-End Testing for Real-time Features

![Diagram 25](diagrams/diagram-025.svg)

End-to-end testing for real-time features in the Fabric web application employs a two-pronged approach to validate both client-side UI reactivity and server-side event delivery. This ensures that actions in the backend correctly trigger Server-Sent Events (SSEs) and that the frontend dynamically updates in response.

The first strategy involves simulating user interactions and UI updates within a browser environment. This is achieved using [`playwright`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L288) through the script located at [`web/test-scripts/realtime-lifecycle-test.js`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/test-scripts/realtime-lifecycle-test.js). This script launches a Chromium browser and navigates to relevant application pages. It then performs agent lifecycle operations, such as creating, updating, and deleting agents, by directly interacting with the API via [`fetch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L107) calls. Critically, instead of relying on page reloads, the script observes and verifies that the UI updates dynamically as expected in response to SSEs. Screenshots are captured at various stages to visually confirm these UI reactions. The script also monitors console messages and HTTP responses, providing insight into the real-time communication flow.

The second strategy focuses on server-side validation of SSE delivery, independent of a browser. The [`bash`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/advanced-local/completions.md?plain=1#L35) script at [`web/test-scripts/sse-curl-test.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/test-scripts/sse-curl-test.sh) uses [`curl`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L229) to listen for SSEs directly from the server. This allows for verification that the backend is correctly emitting event types, such as [`agent.created`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/common.go#L913), [`agent.status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/sync.go#L542), and [`agent.deleted`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/events.go#L417), and that the [`event: update`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L279) type is correctly formatted. This method helps to isolate and confirm the integrity of the server-side event publishing mechanism.

Both testing approaches are configured via environment variables, allowing for flexible setup of project IDs, authentication tokens, base URLs, and output directories. This separation of concerns in testing helps ensure the robustness of the Fabric platform's real-time features. For further details on the web application's architecture and development workflow, refer to [Fabric Web User Interface](#fabric-web-user-interface).

<a id="agent-configuration-and-operational-parameters"></a>

## Agent Configuration and Operational Parameters

| Agent Role | Primary Responsibilities | Configuration File Path | Key Operational Parameters / Constraints |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Documentation Writer | Maintain and improve project documentation; ensure clarity, conciseness, and accuracy. | `.fabric/templates/docs-writer/system-prompt.md` | Adhere to conventions, mimic style, proactively update all affected docs. |
| Git Workflow Protocol | Manage Git operations in a restricted, non-interactive sandbox environment. | `.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents-git.md` | Local-only operations, worktree-aware branch management, non-interactive conflict resolution. |
| Fabric CLI Operating | Interact with the Fabric orchestration system within a containerized sandbox. | `.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents-hub.md` | Non-interactive mode (`--non-interactive`), structured output (`--format json`), no `sync` or `cdw`. |
| Agent Status Signals | Signal agent state to the orchestration system. | `.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents.md` | `ask_user`, `blocked`, `task_completed` signals. |
| GCP VM Manager | Manage and interact with a GCP VM via `gcloud compute ssh`. | `.fabric/templates/instance-manager/system-prompt.md` | Specific VM details (instance, zone, project), repository config, Hub service management. |
| Release Engineer | Generate semantic release notes from Git commit history. | `.fabric/templates/release-notes/system-prompt.md` | Read-only operations, precision with Git, categorize commits (Features, Fixes, Breaking Changes). |
| Frontend Developer | Front-end web development, debugging, and troubleshooting. | `.fabric/templates/web-dev/agents.md` | Use Chrome DevTools for verification and debugging. |
| Team Creation & Extension | Create/extend Fabric agent templates from high-level descriptions. | `.fabric/templates/team-creation/SKILL.md` | Define roles, workflow, and communication patterns for multi-agent teams. |

Fabric agents operate with defined workflows and communication protocols, managed through configuration templates and bundled platform skills. This framework provides specific operational parameters for various autonomous agents, including those specializing in technical documentation, GCP VM integration testing, semantic release note generation, and web development.

The [`.fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L34) directory serves as a central repository for defining these operational parameters. Within this directory, configuration files and markdown documents specify how agents are expected to behave, interact, and perform their designated tasks.

For example, the Documentation Writer agent, configured through [`.fabric/templates/docs-writer/system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/docs-writer/system-prompt.md), is designed to review Git changes and ensure documentation alignment with code. Its responsibilities include maintaining consistency in tone and formatting, organizing documentation, and integrating with [`AGENTS.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/codex/config.yaml#L37) for site-specific details. The agent employs advanced reasoning to analyze tasks against defined policies, evaluate the consequences of changes, and update plans if refactoring becomes complex. Its workflow involves understanding the task, planning, implementation using [`replace`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cdw.go#L103) and [`write_file`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/scripts/inspect_logs.py#L92) tools, verification of documentation accuracy, and finalization.

The Instance Manager agent, detailed in [`.fabric/templates/instance-manager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/instance-manager), manages autonomous Fabric agents and GCP VM integration testing. It defines strict Git workflows for non-interactive, sandboxed environments, requiring local-only operations and non-interactive conflict resolution using specific Git commands. Operational instructions in [`.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents-hub.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents-hub.md) mandate the use of [`--non-interactive`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L40) and [`--format json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L1045) flags for [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI commands, while prohibiting commands like [`sync`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/mock.go#L101) or [`--global`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L234). The [`system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/provision.go#L960) within this directory guides the agent in managing a GCP VM for [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) repository integration testing, including [`gcloud compute ssh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/README.md?plain=1#L224) access, VM configuration, [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) repository location, and [`fabric-hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L213) service management via [`systemd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L93). It also outlines how to generate test user tokens using integration hub signing keys.

The Release Notes agent, configured in [`.fabric/templates/release-notes/system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/release-notes/system-prompt.md), functions as an expert Release Engineer. Its primary role is to generate high-quality, semantic release notes from Git commit history. This agent operates in read-only mode, uses [`run_shell_command`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-24-changelog.md?plain=1#L19) for Git operations, and adheres to strict Markdown formatting rules, categorizing commits into "Features" and "Fixes." It also prioritizes changes by significance, highlights breaking changes, synthesizes related commits, and filters out irrelevant information.

For web development tasks, the Web Development agent, specified in [`.fabric/templates/web-dev/agents.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/web-dev/agents.md), outlines communication protocols and defines the role of a Frontend Developer, including the use of Chrome DevTools for verification and debugging. The [`SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/skills.go#L193) file within [`.fabric/templates/web-dev/skills/chrome-devtools`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/web-dev/skills/chrome-devtools) details efficient Chrome DevTools usage via the Multi-Channel Proxy (MCP), covering browser lifecycle, page selection, element interaction, and workflow patterns for debugging and automation.

Bundled resources and platform skills are managed within the [`resources`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources) directory. This includes templates and platform-specific skills embedded directly into the application's binary. The [`resources/catalog.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/catalog.go) file defines structures and functions for handling [`BundledResource`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/catalog.go#L27) instances, which encapsulate metadata such as resource kind, name, scope, and source URL, along with an [`fs.FS`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L156) interface for content access. These resources ensure that agents operate with a consistent set of foundational knowledge and operational constraints. For instance, platform skills like [`agent-status-signals`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13), [`git-sandbox`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L14), and [`fabric-cli-operations`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L11) define mandatory protocols for status signaling, Git workflows in sandboxed environments, and CLI operational guidelines, respectively. The [`team-creation`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L10) skill provides a methodology for structuring multi-agent systems by defining roles, responsibilities, and workflows for orchestrator and worker agents. See [Fabric Platform Skills](#fabric-platform-skills) for a deeper dive into platform-level skill definitions.

<a id="agent-configuration-and-operational-parameters-documentation-writer-agent-configuration"></a>

### Documentation Writer Agent Configuration

![Diagram 26](diagrams/diagram-026.svg)

The Documentation Writer agent's configuration is primarily defined by the system prompt located at [`.fabric/templates/docs-writer/system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/docs-writer/system-prompt.md). This prompt establishes the agent's core mandates, specific responsibilities, advanced reasoning capabilities, and a structured workflow for documentation tasks. The agent is designed to integrate seamlessly into a Git-based development process, focusing on maintaining accurate, consistent, and secure technical documentation.

The agent's mandates require it to adhere to existing documentation conventions, including style guides, terminology, tone, and formatting (e.g., Markdown, Docusaurus, MkDocs). A key responsibility is to proactively update all affected documentation, including tutorials, READMEs, and API references, whenever code changes are identified. The agent is also instructed to note ambiguities as questions for clarification and include them in [`git`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102) commit messages, but it is prohibited from automatically summarizing modifications unless explicitly requested. Furthermore, it cannot revert version control changes without explicit instructions and should document discrepancies between code and documentation without altering the code itself.

The agent's responsibilities include reviewing Git branch changes for documentation impact, ensuring code-documentation alignment for specific project parts, and improving documentation organization and readability through consolidation and refactoring. It can discover documentation site specifics by looking for [`AGENTS.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/codex/config.yaml#L37) in relevant sub-directories.

To fulfill these responsibilities, the agent employs advanced reasoning and planning strategies. This includes analyzing logical dependencies against policies and prerequisites, assessing risks such as broken links, and using abductive reasoning to identify causes for code-documentation divergence. The agent prioritizes precision and grounding, ensuring documentation changes are based on actual code behavior and verifiable against existing documentation or code. It is also designed for adaptability, updating its plans and informing the user if initial refactoring becomes overly complex.

The agent follows a structured six-step workflow:

1. **Understand**: It uses [`glob`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/sync.go#L59) to comprehend documentation structure, site mechanics, and the underlying code.
2. **Plan**: It constructs a plan, which it may concisely share with the user.
3. **Implement**: It applies changes using tools like [`replace`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cdw.go#L103) and [`write_file`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/scripts/inspect_logs.py#L92), strictly adhering to project conventions.
4. **Verify (Accuracy)**: It checks that updated documentation accurately reflects the code, potentially executing doc-build or linting steps.
5. **Verify (Standards)**: It ensures language clarity, conciseness, and style adherence.
6. **Finalize**: Upon verification, it completes the task, presenting any concerns and awaiting further instructions.

Operational guidelines emphasize token efficiency, achieved by minimizing tool output tokens, using quiet/silent flags in shell commands, and redirecting large outputs to temporary files. The agent maintains a professional, direct, and concise tone and strictly adheres to security best practices, never exposing sensitive information. This comprehensive configuration ensures the Documentation Writer agent functions as an efficient and secure assistant, balancing conciseness with clarity and technical accuracy while prioritizing user control and project conventions. For details on how other agent configurations are managed, refer to [Agent Configuration and Operational Parameters](#agent-configuration-and-operational-parameters).

<a id="agent-configuration-and-operational-parameters-instance-manager-agent-configuration-and-gcp-vm-integration"></a>

### Instance Manager Agent Configuration and GCP VM Integration

![Diagram 27](diagrams/diagram-027.svg)

The Instance Manager agent's configuration is central to orchestrating autonomous Fabric agents and managing a dedicated GCP VM for integration testing. This setup enables automated testing and deployment within a controlled environment, ensuring the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) repository's changes are thoroughly validated.

The agent adheres to a strict Git workflow tailored for sandboxed, non-interactive environments, as defined in [`.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents-git.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents-git.md). This protocol emphasizes local-only operations, prohibiting network-dependent Git commands such as [`fetch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L107), [`pull`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L107), or [`push`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/bridge.go#L58). Instead, it mandates direct references for comparisons ([`git diff main...HEAD`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102)) and rebasing ([`git rebase main`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102)). A key aspect is non-interactive conflict resolution, which bypasses traditional editors like Vi/Vim using environment variables and flags such as [`GIT_EDITOR=true git rebase --continue`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102) to prevent execution hangs. This ensures that Git operations proceed automatically without requiring human intervention in the sandbox.

Operational instructions for interacting with the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI are provided in [`.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents-hub.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents-hub.md). Agents are required to use the [`--non-interactive`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L40) flag with all [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI commands to prevent blocking prompts and [`--format json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L1045) for machine-readable output. This ensures predictable and automatable command execution. Commands like [`fabric look <agent-id>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-cli-operations/SKILL.md?plain=1#L6) allow agents to inspect the output of other running agents, while [`fabrictool status blocked "<reason>"`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L15) is used to signal an intentional pause, preventing false stall detections. Agents are explicitly forbidden from using commands like [`sync`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/mock.go#L101) or [`cdw`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cdw.go#L31), or accessing system internals via [`--no-hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L793) or [`--global`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L234), reinforcing their operation within defined boundaries. The document also outlines how agents should manage their status and communicate with users, using commands like [`fabrictool status ask_user "<question>"`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L100) before prompting for input and [`fabrictool status task_completed "<task title>"`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L100) upon task completion, as detailed in [`.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/instance-manager/agents.md). See [Standard Agent Status Signaling Protocol](#fabric-platform-skills-standard-agent-status-signaling-protocol) for a more general overview of status signaling.

The comprehensive management procedures for the GCP VM dedicated to [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) repository integration testing are detailed in [`.fabric/templates/instance-manager/system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/instance-manager/system-prompt.md). This includes specifics on SSH access via [`gcloud compute ssh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/README.md?plain=1#L224), VM configuration (instance name, zone, project), and the location of the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) repository ([`/home/fabric/fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/server_foreground.go#L2039)). The [`fabric-hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L213) service, managed by [`systemd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L93), is central to this environment, with its configuration, environment variables, settings, and database paths explicitly defined. The document also provides common [`gcloud compute ssh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/README.md?plain=1#L224) commands for service management, such as checking service status, pulling the latest code, rebuilding and restarting the hub, and viewing logs. The integration testing workflow involves pushing changes to a remote repository and then pulling and rebuilding them on the VM.

Furthermore, the configuration addresses secure communication and authentication within the integration environment. It specifies the use of Integration Hub Signing Keys (user and agent keys using [`HS256`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L451) from GCP Secret Manager) and provides instructions for generating test user tokens. These JWTs include specific headers and claims (e.g., [`iss`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/proxyauth.go#L145), [`sub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/inprocess.go#L51), [`aud`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/proxyauth.go#L147), [`uid`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/settings_v1.go#L517), [`email`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L98), [`role`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/devauth.go#L96)) to facilitate testing of authentication and authorization mechanisms. This robust setup ensures that all interactions, from Git operations to [`fabric-hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L213) service management and token generation, are controlled and secure.

<a id="agent-configuration-and-operational-parameters-semantic-release-notes-agent-configuration"></a>

### Semantic Release Notes Agent Configuration

![Diagram 28](diagrams/diagram-028.svg)

The Release Notes agent is designed to automate the generation of high-quality, semantic release notes directly from a Git commit history. Its configuration focuses on ensuring accuracy, adherence to specific formatting rules, and secure operation within the Fabric platform. This agent operates primarily as a read-only entity, though it can write generated notes to a file like [`CHANGELOG.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.gcloudignore#L90) upon explicit instruction.

A central configuration for this agent is defined within the file [`.fabric/templates/release-notes/system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/release-notes/system-prompt.md). This prompt acts as an expert Release Engineer, outlining the agent's core mandates and operational guidelines. It emphasizes the need for Git precision, requiring exact Git-compatible date strings for queries and translating vague user inputs into precise ranges for [`git log`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L44) commands. Security is a paramount concern, with strict prohibitions against exposing sensitive information such as secrets or API keys during its operation.

The agent follows a defined four-step workflow for generating release notes:

1. **Information Gathering and Abductive Reasoning:** This involves parsing date ranges and extracting commits using shell commands.
2. **Risk Assessment and Deep Analysis:** The agent assesses the significance of commit messages and performs deeper analyses using [`git show`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L130) for potentially vague but important commits.
3. **Synthesis and Planning:** Commits are grouped and condensed into logical features and fixes, with noise (e.g., minor cleanup, non-behavior-affecting refactors) filtered out.
4. **Execution and Output:** The final Markdown output is generated, presenting release notes clearly and concisely.

The release notes must adhere to strict formatting guidelines, categorizing changes into [`Features`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/README.md?plain=1#L5) and [`Fixes`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-04-27-changelog.md?plain=1#L16), prioritizing them by significance, and prominently highlighting [`⚠️ BREAKING CHANGES`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-04-27-changelog.md?plain=1#L5). Related serial commits are synthesized into single bullet points to improve readability. The agent's adaptability allows it to adjust its strategy for large numbers of commits, such as filtering by [`git log --merges`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102) or prompting the user for a more summarized approach.

Interaction protocols for this agent are specified in [`.fabric/templates/release-notes/agents.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/release-notes/agents.md). This document details how the agent should communicate with a user within the [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) environment, specifically by using [`fabrictool status ask_user`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L100) before requesting input and [`fabrictool status task_completed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L100) to signal task completion. These commands ensure that the agent's interaction with the user is structured and that it avoids unnecessary conversational loops after a task is finished. For a broader understanding of how agents manage their lifecycle and orchestrate tasks, refer to [Agent Lifecycle Management and Orchestration](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-agent-lifecycle-management-and-orchestration).

<a id="agent-configuration-and-operational-parameters-web-development-agent-and-chrome-devtools-integration"></a>

### Web Development Agent and Chrome DevTools Integration

![Diagram 29](diagrams/diagram-029.svg)

The Web Development agent's configuration, found in [`.fabric/templates/web-dev`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/web-dev), outlines its operational protocols and skill set. The agent is designed to interact with users and perform web development tasks, particularly leveraging Chrome DevTools through the Managed Cloud Platform (MCP). Communication protocols dictate that the agent must signal its need for user input by executing [`fabrictool status ask_user "<question>"`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L100) and mark task completion with [`fabrictool status task_completed "<task title>"`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L100). This ensures clear communication and prevents unintended further interactions.

The agent is defined with the skills of a Frontend Developer, with an initial action of reviewing instructions in [`.fabric/templates/web-dev/agents.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/web-dev/agents.md). A core component of this agent's capabilities is its efficient use of Chrome DevTools, detailed in [`.fabric/templates/web-dev/skills/chrome-devtools/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/web-dev/skills/chrome-devtools/SKILL.md). This involves understanding the browser lifecycle, where Chrome starts automatically and maintains a persistent profile configured via MCP server arguments. Interaction with web pages is managed by selecting active pages and then using unique identifiers ([`uid`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/settings_v1.go#L517)s) retrieved from snapshots to interact with elements (e.g., [`click`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L112), [`fill`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L139)).

The workflow for web development tasks emphasizes a sequence of actions: navigating to a page, waiting for content to load, taking a snapshot of the page structure to identify elements, and then performing interactions. For efficiency, the agent can retrieve data by specifying file paths for large outputs, using pagination, and filtering by data types. The system distinguishes between [`take_snapshot`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L303) for automation due to its speed and text-based output, and [`take_screenshot`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L303) for visual inspection. Parallel execution of tool calls is supported, provided the order of operations—navigate, wait, snapshot, interact—is maintained. A [`system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/provision.go#L960) file in [`.fabric/templates/web-dev/system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.fabric/templates/web-dev/system-prompt.md) acts as a placeholder for future system prompt definitions.

<a id="agent-configuration-and-operational-parameters-bundled-resources-and-platform-skills"></a>

### Bundled Resources and Platform Skills

![Diagram 30](diagrams/diagram-030.svg)

Bundled resources, including default templates, harness configurations, and platform-specific skills, are embedded directly into the application's binary to ensure consistency and availability. These resources are accessed and managed to maintain proper structure and adherence to operational standards. The [`resources`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources) directory is central to this mechanism, defining how various built-in assets, such as agent templates and platform skills, are cataloged and made available to the system.

The [`embed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L80) package in Go is used to integrate static assets directly into the Fabric application's binary. This includes templates from the [`resources/templates`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/templates) directory and platform skills from [`resources/platform_skills`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/platform_skills). Each embedded resource is represented by a [`BundledResource`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/catalog.go#L27) object, which encapsulates its kind, name, scope, and provides an interface for accessing its content. For example, [`BuiltinTemplates`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/catalog.go#L54) and [`BuiltinHarnessConfigs`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/catalog.go#L73) functions systematically retrieve these predefined resources. The system also generates [`SourceURL`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L484) values for these bundled resources, typically using a [`builtin://fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/catalog.go#L46) scheme, which helps in tracking their origin.

The templates, found in [`resources/templates/default`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/templates/default), define core operational protocols for autonomous Fabric agents. These include specific guidelines for Git workflows in restricted, non-interactive sandbox environments ([`resources/templates/default/agents-git.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/templates/default/agents-git.md)), instructions for interacting with the Fabric orchestration system via the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI ([`resources/templates/default/agents-hub.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/templates/default/agents-hub.md)), and protocols for managing agent status signals ([`resources/templates/default/agents.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/templates/default/agents.md)).

Platform skills, located in [`resources/platform_skills`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/platform_skills), provide foundational knowledge and operational constraints for agents. These skills cover a range of functionalities:

- **Agent Status Signaling**: The [`resources/platform_skills/agent-status-signals`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/platform_skills/agent-status-signals) directory defines a mandatory protocol for agents to signal their status using [`fabrictool status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50) commands, such as [`ask_user`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13), [`blocked`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L436), and [`task_completed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13). This prevents false stall detections and facilitates real-time communication of agent states. See [Standard Agent Status Signaling Protocol](#fabric-platform-skills-standard-agent-status-signaling-protocol) for more details.
- **Git Sandbox Operations**: The [`resources/platform_skills/git-sandbox`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/platform_skills/git-sandbox) directory outlines a strict Git workflow for agents operating in restricted [`worktree`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102) environments. This ensures agents perform Git operations in an air-gapped, non-interactive manner, emphasizing local-only operations and structured conflict resolution. See [Git Workflow for Sandboxed Environments](#fabric-platform-skills-git-workflow-for-sandboxed-environments) for further information.
- **Fabric CLI Operations**: The [`resources/platform_skills/fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/platform_skills/fabric) and [`resources/platform_skills/fabric-cli-operations`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/platform_skills/fabric-cli-operations) directories provide core functionalities for orchestrating concurrent LLM-based agents via the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI tool and its wrapper scripts ([`resources/platform_skills/fabric/scripts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/platform_skills/fabric/scripts)). These skills define lifecycle management commands, inter-agent messaging, and crucial operational constraints, such as mandatory use of [`--non-interactive`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L40) and [`--format json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L1045), and prohibiting certain commands.
