See [Fabric CLI Operations and Constraints](#fabric-platform-skills-fabric-cli-operations-and-constraints) and [Fabric Agent Lifecycle and Project Management](#fabric-platform-skills-fabric-agent-lifecycle-and-project-management) for comprehensive insights.
- **Inter-Agent Messaging**: The [`resources/platform_skills/fabric-messaging`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/platform_skills/fabric-messaging) directory details the effective use of the [`fabric message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1) command for communication within the Fabric ecosystem, covering recipient types, best practices for message content and timing, and advanced messaging flags. See [Inter-Agent and User Communication Protocols](#fabric-platform-skills-inter-agent-and-user-communication-protocols) for more information.
- **Team Creation**: The [`resources/platform_skills/team-creation`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/resources/platform_skills/team-creation) directory describes a methodology for creating and extending Fabric agent team templates, enabling the definition of agent roles, workflows, and the integration of reusable harness skills for multi-agent orchestration. See [Team Creation and Multi-Agent Orchestration Templates](#fabric-platform-skills-team-creation-and-multi-agent-orchestration-templates) for further details.

<a id="fabric-agent-development-kit-and-examples"></a>

## Fabric Agent Development Kit and Examples

![Diagram 31](diagrams/diagram-031.svg)

The [`examples`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples) directory contains various demonstrations of [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) agent functionalities and orchestration patterns. These examples showcase how to develop and integrate agents within the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) platform, including their lifecycle management, multi-agent interactions, and different execution flows.

One example, found in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent), illustrates how an Agent Development Kit (ADK) agent integrates with [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1)'s lifecycle management. This agent can report its status via [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) for orchestration within a [`grove`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L72). The container image for this agent, defined in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent/Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/Dockerfile), extends a base image to include [`google-adk`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-04-09-changelog.md?plain=1#L8) and the agent's Python code, configuring the environment for execution and task delivery. The entry point, [`examples/adk_fabric_agent/__main__.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/__main__.py), provides robust crash reporting, ensuring import errors and runtime failures are logged to container logs, a status file ([`agent-info.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L965)), and standard error. A lazy import mechanism in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent/__init__.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/__init__.py) allows [`__main__.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/README.md?plain=1#L116) to catch startup errors.

The multi-agent Texas Hold'em poker game simulation in [`examples/agent-poker`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker) demonstrates how [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) can coordinate LLM agents through shared state and group messaging. In this simulation, [`Dealer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/README.md?plain=1#L9), [`Player`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-player/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L1), and [`Auditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L87) agents interact to manage game flow, player actions, and ensure game integrity. The [`Dealer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/README.md?plain=1#L9) agent, for instance, manages the game state in [`card-table.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-dealer/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L22) and controls game flow, while the [`Auditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L87) agent monitors for cheating.

Another example, located in [`examples/amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp), provides an Amp harness for [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1). This demonstrates how to integrate external tools without modifying [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1)'s core Go code. It involves installing the [`amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI, handling authentication, setting up the environment, and reconciling [`amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L1) settings, all through configuration and scripting.

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) orchestration patterns are further explored in [`examples/orchestration-basics`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics). This directory showcases both parallel fan-out processing, where an orchestrator agent dispatches tasks to multiple researcher agents concurrently, and sequential task execution, illustrating a workflow involving data fetching, processing, and reporting across agents.

<a id="fabric-agent-development-kit-and-examples-adk-agent-lifecycle-and-status-reporting"></a>

### ADK Agent Lifecycle and Status Reporting

![Diagram 32](diagrams/diagram-032.svg)

ADK (Agent Development Kit) agents integrate with Fabric's lifecycle management through various mechanisms for reporting status, handling interactive input, and ensuring robust execution within a containerized environment. This integration is exemplified by the [`adk_fabric_agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/run.py#L27) example in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent).

The agent employs two types of status reporting via [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44). Transient activities, such as "thinking," "executing," or "working," are managed by writing to a local JSON file ([`agent-info.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L965)) using [`fabrictool.write_agent_status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/callbacks.py#L33) in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent/fabrictool.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/fabrictool.py). These updates provide real-time feedback on the agent's immediate state. For critical, persistent state changes, or "sticky" activities like "ask_user," "blocked," or "task_completed," the agent invokes the [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) CLI via [`fabrictool.run_status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/tools.py#L50) in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent/tools.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/tools.py). This mechanism ensures that important lifecycle events are reported to the Fabric Hub, preventing less significant transient states from overwriting them. Guidelines for when an agent should signal these states are defined in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent/templates/adk`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/templates/adk).

Interactive input handling for ADK agents is facilitated through a custom runner in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent/run.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/run.py). This runner allows an initial message to be provided via a command-line flag and then transitions into an interactive loop. This design enables Fabric's runtime to deliver subsequent messages to the agent using [`tmux send-keys`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/message.go#L271) when operating within a container.

Agents are containerized using a [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138) located in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent/Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/Dockerfile). This Dockerfile extends a [`fabric-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L84) image, setting up the necessary Python environment and dependencies like [`google-adk`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-04-09-changelog.md?plain=1#L8) from source. It configures the container for agent execution, including the specific entry point for task delivery.

A robust entry point, implemented in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent/__main__.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/__main__.py), wraps the agent's core application logic with comprehensive crash reporting. This ensures that any import errors or runtime failures are logged to container logs, a designated status file ([`agent-info.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L965)), and standard error. This multi-channel reporting mechanism enhances observability and aids in debugging agents running in isolated or headless environments. Additionally, an [`__init__.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/README.md?plain=1#L115) in [`examples/adk_fabric_agent/__init__.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/__init__.py) uses lazy importing for the agent to allow [`__main__.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/README.md?plain=1#L116) to catch startup errors.

<a id="fabric-agent-development-kit-and-examples-multi-agent-poker-simulation"></a>

### Multi-Agent Poker Simulation

The Fabric platform demonstrates multi-agent collaboration through a simulated Texas Hold'em poker game, involving [`Dealer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/README.md?plain=1#L9), [`Player`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-player/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L1), and [`Auditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L87) agents. This simulation orchestrates LLM-based agents to manage game flow, player actions, and ensure game integrity, relying on shared state and inter-agent messaging.

The [`Dealer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/README.md?plain=1#L9) agent, defined by [`examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-dealer/system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-dealer/system-prompt.md), acts as the central orchestrator. It is responsible for game setup, including initializing [`Player`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-player/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L1) and [`Auditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L87) agents, managing the card deck using the [`python3 ~/deck.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-dealer/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L11) script located at [`examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-dealer/home/deck.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-dealer/home/deck.py), and establishing the initial game state in [`card-table.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-dealer/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L22). The [`Dealer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/README.md?plain=1#L9) progresses the game through phases (e.g., Pre-flop, Flop, Turn, River, Showdown), enforcing betting rules and resolving hands. It uses [`broadcast`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/stream.go#L114) messages for public announcements and [`direct message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L113) for private communications, such as dealing hole cards to players and providing a shadow record to the [`Auditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L87).

[`Player`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-player/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L1) agents, guided by [`examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-player/system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-player/system-prompt.md), make betting decisions (e.g., [`fold`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/entc/migrate_alpha.go#L212), [`check`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/imagecheck/checker.go#L20), [`call`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L2260), [`raise`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L177), [`all-in`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L170)). They receive private hole cards from the [`Dealer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/README.md?plain=1#L9) and observe the shared [`card-table.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-dealer/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L22) for current game state information. Player actions are communicated via [`broadcast`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/stream.go#L114) messages. The simulation allows [`Player`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-player/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L1) agents to attempt cheating, which introduces a challenge for the [`Auditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L87).

The [`Auditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L87) agent, specified in [`examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-auditor/system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-auditor/system-prompt.md), functions as an independent observer to maintain game integrity. It receives shadow copies of dealt cards from the [`Dealer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/README.md?plain=1#L9) via [`direct message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L113) and monitors [`group messages`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L34) for player actions. The [`Auditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L87) identifies and reports procedural [`Warnings`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/output.go#L61) (e.g., acting out of turn) and more severe [`Cheating Violations`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-auditor/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L23) (e.g., card fraud, bet manipulation). [`Warnings`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/output.go#L61) are communicated via [`direct message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L113), while [`Cheating Violations`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-auditor/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L23) are announced via [`group message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L34) ([`AUDIT VIOLATION`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-auditor/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L31)). The [`Auditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L87) maintains an audit log in [`~/audit-log.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-auditor/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L64) and performs end-of-hand verifications, broadcasting [`AUDIT: Hand [N] verified clean.`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-auditor/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L45) if no issues are found.

The simulation relies on a shared [`card-table.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-dealer/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L22) file in the workspace as the single source of truth for the game state. Only the [`Dealer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/README.md?plain=1#L9) has write access to this file, ensuring data consistency, while [`Player`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/agent-poker/templates/poker-player/system-prompt.md?plain=1#L1) and [`Auditor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L87) agents have read-only access. All inter-agent communication, including [`broadcast`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/stream.go#L114) for public events and [`direct message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L113) for private information, is managed through [`fabric CLI messaging commands`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1). Agent status reporting, such as [`fabrictool status ask_user`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L100), [`fabrictool status blocked`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50), and [`fabrictool status task_completed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L100), is used to indicate an agent's state and facilitate interaction within the [`Fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) environment. Further details on core architectural principles and agent management can be found in [Core Architectural Principles and Agent Management](#design-specifications-and-architecture-core-architectural-principles-and-agent-management).

<a id="fabric-agent-development-kit-and-examples-amp-cli-harness-integration"></a>

### AMP CLI Harness Integration

![Diagram 33](diagrams/diagram-033.svg)

The integration of the [`amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L1) tool with Fabric agents utilizes a [`ContainerScriptHarness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness/container_script_harness.go#L41) to enable [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) agents to leverage [`amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L1)'s capabilities without requiring modifications to Fabric's core Go codebase. This integration provides a pattern for community harness authors.

The core of this integration is the Docker image construction defined in [`examples/amp/Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/Dockerfile). This Dockerfile extends a base Fabric image to install the [`amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI tool globally, ensuring its availability within the agent's container environment.

Authentication handling and environment provisioning are managed by the [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91) script, executed during the [`pre-start`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/common.go#L581) lifecycle hook within the container. This script determines the appropriate authentication method for [`amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L1), prioritizing explicitly provided API keys or falling back to environment variables like [`AMP_API_KEY`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L11) or [`ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L1226). It then securely projects the resolved API key into the agent's environment as [`AMP_API_KEY`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L11), ensuring [`amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L1) can authenticate consistently. Additionally, [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91) reconciles [`amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L1)'s settings to ensure necessary defaults for non-interactive container operation are present without overriding user-defined configurations.

Agent instructions for status reporting are detailed in [`examples/amp/templates/amp/agents.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/templates/amp/agents.md). This documentation guides [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) agents on how to use [`fabrictool status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50) commands to communicate their operational state to the user and the orchestration system. These instructions clarify that the agent's workspace is a Git worktree mounted at [`/workspace`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L39), facilitating independent commit operations. This approach allows for a flexible and extensible integration of external tools like [`amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L1) within the Fabric agent ecosystem. For more details on the general Harness abstraction and its provisioning mechanisms, refer to [Harness Abstraction and Provisioning](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-harness-abstraction-and-provisioning).

<a id="fabric-agent-development-kit-and-examples-orchestration-patterns-parallel-fan-out"></a>

### Orchestration Patterns: Parallel Fan-Out

![Diagram 34](diagrams/diagram-034.svg)

This orchestration pattern demonstrates how an [`orchestrator`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L30) agent can manage multiple [`researcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L29) agents concurrently to perform tasks in parallel. The [`examples/orchestration-basics/fan-out-parallel`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics/fan-out-parallel) directory contains the example, where an [`orchestrator`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L30) agent dispatches research topics to several [`researcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L29) agents. Each [`researcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L29) agent is designed to follow a strict protocol for unbiased, evidence-based reporting.

The [`orchestrator`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L30) agent utilizes the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI to dynamically start [`researcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L29) agents, each assigned a topic from [`examples/orchestration-basics/fan-out-parallel/topics.txt`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics/fan-out-parallel/topics.txt). It then waits for completion notifications from these [`researcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L29) agents before deleting them. The [`researcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L29) agents are guided by a system prompt in [`examples/orchestration-basics/fan-out-parallel/researcher-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics/fan-out-parallel/researcher-prompt.md) that defines a cognitive framework, a planning process, and a mandatory five-phase research protocol. This protocol emphasizes rigorous methodology, critical analysis, and iterative refinement to ensure quality output. The research findings are structured according to the Markdown template specified in [`examples/orchestration-basics/fan-out-parallel/research-template.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics/fan-out-parallel/research-template.md), which helps ensure consistency across all research outputs. The setup process for this example involves several [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) commands for initializing a grove, creating agent templates, and configuring the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) server, as detailed in [`examples/orchestration-basics/fan-out-parallel/README.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics/fan-out-parallel/README.md).

<a id="fabric-agent-development-kit-and-examples-orchestration-patterns-sequential-task-execution"></a>

### Orchestration Patterns: Sequential Task Execution

![Diagram 35](diagrams/diagram-035.svg)

Sequential task execution within Fabric agents is demonstrated through a workflow where an orchestrator agent manages a series of tasks, ensuring each is completed before proceeding to the next. This pattern is illustrated by an example in the [`examples/orchestration-basics/sequence`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics/sequence) directory. The orchestration logic relies on the Fabric CLI tool for agent management, with tasks assigned to individual agents.

The core of this pattern involves:

- **Agent Management:** Starting a new agent for each specific task.
- **Task Assignment:** Assigning distinct work items to these agents. The orchestrator uses a notification mechanism (e.g., [`--notify`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L192) flag with the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI) to await completion.
- **Synchronous Workflow:** The orchestrator idles and waits for an agent to signal task completion. This ensures that tasks are executed in a predefined order.
- **Resource Cleanup:** Once a task is complete and acknowledged, the agent responsible for that task is stopped and deleted, managing system resources efficiently.
- **Sequential Processing:** This cycle repeats for each step in the workflow, guaranteeing that the tasks are processed sequentially by dedicated agents.

The workflow example, detailed in [`examples/orchestration-basics/sequence/work-sequence.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics/sequence/work-sequence.md), demonstrates a five-step process:

1. **Data Fetching:** A Python script ([`fetch_data.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics/sequence/work-sequence.md?plain=1#L3)) queries a public API and saves the raw JSON data.
2. **Data Processing:** Another Python script ([`process_data.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics/sequence/work-sequence.md?plain=1#L5)) parses the fetched JSON, extracts specific information, and appends it to a log file.
3. **Data Accumulation and Verification:** The fetching and processing steps are repeated multiple times to accumulate data, followed by a verification step.
4. **Report Generation:** A Python script ([`generate_report.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/orchestration-basics/sequence/work-sequence.md?plain=1#L9)) reads the processed data and creates an HTML report.
5. **Final Output and Archiving:** The report is generated, and all relevant scripts and the final report are archived into a compressed file.

This example highlights how a series of interdependent operations can be systematically executed across different agents, with each agent handling a specific part of the overall workflow. Further details on managing agent lifecycles and orchestrating agents can be found in [Agent Lifecycle Management and Orchestration](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-agent-lifecycle-management-and-orchestration).

<a id="agent-harness-management"></a>

## Agent Harness Management

![Diagram 36](diagrams/diagram-036.svg)

The Fabric platform supports the integration of "opt-in" coding agents, which are not installed by default, through a structured approach centered around harness configuration bundles. These bundles provide all necessary components for an agent's operation, including configuration, container-side provisioning scripts, and Docker build specifications. This modular design allows users to selectively install and manage various coding agents such as Antigravity, Claude, Codex, and Copilot, minimizing the platform's default footprint while offering broad extensibility.

Each agent's integration is defined within a dedicated directory under [`harnesses`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses), acting as a "harness bundle." These bundles typically include a [`config.yaml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L45) to define the harness's core configuration and capabilities, a [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91) script for container-side setup tasks (like authentication and configuration file generation), a [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138) for image construction, and a [`capture_auth.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L83) script for credential management. An optional [`home`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L361) directory can also provide initial user files within the agent's container.

A shared Python library, [`harnesses/fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py), plays a central role in standardizing the provisioning process. This library offers utilities for declarative authentication, instruction projection, and Multi-Channel Proxy (MCP) server configuration. Declarative authentication, using [`AuthSpec`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L297) and [`AuthMethod`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L249), allows agents to define their credential requirements, which are then resolved based on manifest data, environment variables, or staged secrets. Instruction projection ([`project_instructions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L769)) enables the dynamic composition of agent prompts and instructions from multiple sources into a single target file, preserving user-authored content. Utilities like [`apply_mcp_servers_simple`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L167) and [`apply_mcp_translated`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L844) facilitate the translation and merging of MCP server configurations into an agent's native configuration files.

The platform ensures consistency across these harness bundles through an automated vendoring process. A Go program located at [`harnesses/gen/main.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/gen/main.go) automatically integrates the canonical [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) into each harness subdirectory that contains a [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91) script. This mechanism guarantees that all provisioning and authentication capture scripts utilize a consistent version of the shared library, preventing divergence and ensuring predictable behavior.

Specific harness implementations cater to the unique requirements of each agent. For instance, the Antigravity harness ([`harnesses/antigravity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/antigravity)) handles [`gnome-keyring`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/antigravity/README.md?plain=1#L5) integration for authentication and bypasses interactive onboarding. The Claude harness ([`harnesses/claude`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/claude)) manages network egress control through [`iptables`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L1286) and includes specialized logic for extracting OAuth tokens from [`tmux`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L74) scrollback. The Codex harness ([`harnesses/codex`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/codex)) focuses on resolving API keys, configuring OpenTelemetry, and translating MCP settings into its [`config.toml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/codex/README.md?plain=1#L37). The Copilot harness ([`harnesses/copilot`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/copilot)) is designed for non-interactive use, managing GitHub token authentication and configuring default settings to avoid interactive prompts.

This structured approach to harness management streamlines the integration of diverse coding agents, enabling the Fabric platform to support a wide range of AI-driven development workflows while maintaining consistency and security.

<a id="agent-harness-management-harness-bundle-structure-and-core-functionality"></a>

### Harness Bundle Structure and Core Functionality

| File/Directory | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `<name>/` | Root directory for the harness bundle. |
| `config.yaml` | Defines harness configuration, including provisioner settings, capabilities, and authentication. |
| `provision.py` | Contains the container-side provisioner, acting as a pre-start hook for the harness. |
| `Dockerfile` | Specifies the Docker image build process, based on `fabric-base`. |
| `cloudbuild.yaml` | Configuration for Cloud Build to manage the harness. |
| `README.md` | Provides bundle-specific documentation, such as authentication modes and build instructions. |
| `home/` | Directory for files that are seeded into the agent's home directory upon installation. |
| `fabric_harness.py` | Vendored copy of the shared `fabric_harness` library, essential for harness functionality. |

Agent harness bundles provide a structured approach for integrating external coding agents that are not installed by default, ensuring a consistent and manageable way to extend the Fabric platform's capabilities. Each harness bundle encapsulates all necessary components for a specific agent, supporting its installation, configuration, and runtime provisioning. This modular design allows users to selectively install agents, reducing the system's default footprint.

A harness bundle typically consists of several key files and directories:

- [`config.yaml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L45): Defines the core configuration for the harness, including its provisioner settings and declared capabilities.
- [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91): A Python script executed within the agent's Docker container during the pre-start phase. Its role is to perform essential setup tasks, such as handling authentication, generating configuration files, and preparing the agent's environment. This script leverages a shared Python library, [`harnesses/fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py), to standardize these provisioning tasks.
- [`capture_auth.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L83): This Python script is responsible for capturing authentication credentials, often after an interactive login, and securely storing them using [`fabrictool secret set`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50).
- [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138): Specifies the instructions for building the Docker image for the agent. This includes installing dependencies, setting up the environment, and defining the container's entry point.
- [`cloudbuild.yaml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L199): Contains the Google Cloud Build configuration for automating the image build process, ensuring consistent and reproducible builds.
- [`README.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L83): Provides documentation specific to the agent's harness, detailing installation procedures, supported authentication modes, and any other relevant information.
- [`home`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L361) directory (optional): This directory can contain files that are seeded into the agent's home directory at installation time, such as shell configuration files ([`.bashrc`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L524)), agent-specific settings, or system prompts.

The overall design emphasizes standardization through the shared [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) library, which offers utilities for declarative authentication, instruction projection, and Multi-Channel Proxy (MCP) server configuration. This library ensures consistency across different agent integrations. The use of [`go generate`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L15) and associated tests ([`harnesses/vendored_lib_test.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/vendored_lib_test.go)) automates the vendoring of [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) into each bundle, ensuring all [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91) and [`capture_auth.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L83) scripts utilize a consistent version of the shared library, maintaining compatibility and preventing divergence.

<a id="agent-harness-management-shared-python-harness-library-fabric-harness-py"></a>

### Shared Python Harness Library (`fabric_harness.py`)

![Diagram 37](diagrams/diagram-037.svg)

The [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) library, located at [`harnesses/fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py), provides a standardized toolkit for Fabric's agent harness scripts. It encapsulates common logic required for provisioning and authenticating agents, ensuring consistency and reducing boilerplate across different harness implementations. This library is automatically vendored into each agent's harness directory by a Go program at [`harnesses/gen/main.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/gen/main.go), ensuring all [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91) and [`capture_auth.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L83) scripts utilize a consistent version and preventing manual modifications.

A core function of [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) is streamlining [Authentication and Credential Capture Mechanisms](#agent-harness-management-authentication-and-credential-capture-mechanisms). It offers declarative authentication through [`AuthMethod`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L249) and [`AuthSpec`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L297) objects, which define how an agent should acquire credentials. The [`ProvisionContext`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L337) class's [`select_auth`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L487) method resolves the appropriate authentication method based on manifest data, environment variables, and staged secrets, supporting both environment variable-based ([`env_method`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L274)) and file-based ([`file_method`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L286)) credential acquisition.

The library also facilitates [Instruction Projection and Prompt Management](#agent-harness-management-instruction-projection-and-prompt-management). The [`project_instructions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L769) function merges various input files, such as [`instructions.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L789), [`system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/provision.go#L960), and [`SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/skills.go#L193), into a single target instruction file within the agent's container. This process is designed to respect and manage "Fabric-managed" blocks (identified by markers like [`_MANAGED_BEGIN_STANDARD`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L671) and [`_MANAGED_END_STANDARD`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L672)), allowing user-authored content to persist while integrating system-generated instructions.

For [Multi-Channel Proxy (MCP) Server Configuration](#agent-harness-management-multi-channel-proxy-mcp-server-configuration), [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) includes utilities like [`apply_mcp_servers_simple`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L167) and [`apply_mcp_translated`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L844). These functions translate and merge MCP server configurations into an agent's native configuration formats, ensuring that agents can communicate effectively within the Fabric ecosystem.

The library offers robust file operations through functions such as [`atomic_write_json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L75), [`atomic_write_text`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L946), [`load_json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L69), and [`read_json_skipping_comment_lines`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L964). These utilities ensure safe and consistent handling of configuration and data files, preventing race conditions and data corruption.

Finally, [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) provides standardized entry points for [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91) and [`capture_auth.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L83) scripts. The [`run`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/wsclient/pty.go#L156) function acts as a main scaffold for provisioning scripts, handling argument parsing, manifest loading, command dispatch, and error handling. Similarly, [`capture_auth_main`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L1040) serves as the entry point for authentication capture scripts, managing credential acquisition and storage via [`fabrictool secret set`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50).

<a id="agent-harness-management-authentication-and-credential-capture-mechanisms"></a>

### Authentication and Credential Capture Mechanisms

![Diagram 38](diagrams/diagram-038.svg)

Authentication and credential capture are critical aspects of integrating external tools and services with Fabric agents. The platform employs a declarative [`AuthSpec`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L297) and [`AuthMethod`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L249) system to define and manage various authentication strategies across different harnesses. This system allows for flexible configuration, supporting methods such as API keys, OAuth tokens, and authentication files.

The core mechanism for acquiring and storing these credentials involves specialized [`capture_auth.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L83) scripts within each harness. These scripts are responsible for retrieving authentication details and then securely persisting them using [`fabrictool secret set`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50). This utility ensures that sensitive information is stored securely and can be accessed by agents as needed.

For instance, the Antigravity harness uses a [`capture_auth.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L83) script that extends the standard capture functionality to integrate with [`gnome-keyring`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/antigravity/README.md?plain=1#L5). This allows it to extract OAuth tokens from the keyring, especially when [`AGY_KEYRING_TOKEN`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/antigravity/README.md?plain=1#L25) is used, and then stores them securely. The script ensures [`DBUS_SESSION_BUS_ADDRESS`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/antigravity/Dockerfile#L38) is correctly configured for communication with [`secret-tool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-06-22-changelog.md?plain=1#L10), which is essential for keyring operations. Similarly, the Claude harness's [`capture_auth.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L83) includes specialized logic to extract [`sk-ant`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L29) OAuth tokens from [`tmux`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L74) scrollback buffers, often used in interactive login flows, and then stores them via [`fabrictool secret set`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50).

In cases like the Copilot harness, the [`capture_auth.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L83) acts as a shim, invoking a shared [`capture_auth_main`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L1040) function. This shared function is designed to capture credentials after an interactive login, such as when a user runs [`copilot login`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/copilot/README.md?plain=1#L1), and then registers the resulting tokens with [`fabrictool secret set`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50). This approach allows for a streamlined experience, enabling users to authenticate interactively and have those credentials automatically picked up by the Fabric platform.

The [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) library, shared across various harnesses, provides a standardized framework for these operations. It defines [`AuthMethod`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L249) and [`AuthSpec`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L297) classes for declarative authentication, allowing harnesses to specify their supported authentication types and precedence. This library also includes the [`capture_auth_main`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L1040) function, which manages the generic credential capture process, including conflict detection and storage via [`fabrictool secret set`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50). This standardization simplifies the development of new harnesses and ensures consistency in how credentials are handled across the Fabric ecosystem. For further details on the common harness utilities, see [Shared Python Harness Library (`fabric_harness.py`)](#agent-harness-management-shared-python-harness-library-fabric-harness-py).

<a id="agent-harness-management-instruction-projection-and-prompt-management"></a>

### Instruction Projection and Prompt Management

![Diagram 39](diagrams/diagram-039.svg)

The [`project_instructions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L769) mechanism, implemented within the shared Python harness library at [`harnesses/fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py), addresses the challenge of composing agent prompts and instructions from various sources into a single, cohesive target file. This process is crucial for providing agents with the necessary context and directives for their tasks, while also ensuring that user-authored content is preserved and not overwritten by automated system updates.

At its core, the [`project_instructions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L769) function merges content from multiple input files, such as [`instructions.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L789), [`system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/provision.go#L960), and [`SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/skills.go#L193), into a designated target instruction file within the agent's container. A key design consideration is the use of "Fabric-managed" blocks, delimited by markers like [`_MANAGED_BEGIN_STANDARD`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L671) and [`_MANAGED_END_STANDARD`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L672). These markers delineate sections of the instruction file that are maintained by the Fabric system, allowing for consistent updates to platform-level guidance or skill definitions. Content outside these managed blocks, typically user-authored, remains untouched, thereby preventing accidental loss of custom instructions or contextual information.

This projection mechanism ensures that agents receive a comprehensive set of instructions, combining general operational guidelines, specific task prompts, and relevant skill documentation. For example, the Claude harness uses this to copy [`instructions.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L789) to the user's home directory as [`GEMINI.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/gemini-cli/config.yaml#L31), while the Copilot harness writes instructions to [`.github/copilot-instructions.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/copilot/README.md?plain=1#L63). This standardized approach to prompt management contributes to predictable agent behavior and simplifies the process of updating agent capabilities or core directives without disrupting custom workflows.

<a id="agent-harness-management-multi-channel-proxy-mcp-server-configuration"></a>

### Multi-Channel Proxy (MCP) Server Configuration

![Diagram 40](diagrams/diagram-040.svg)

The Fabric platform utilizes Multi-Channel Proxy (MCP) servers to enable flexible communication between agents and external services. These proxies allow agents to communicate over various protocols and channels, such as standard input/output (stdio), Server-Sent Events (SSE), or streamable HTTP, without requiring the agent itself to directly manage the complexities of these communication methods. The [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) shared Python library, located in [`harnesses/fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py), plays a central role in translating and integrating these MCP server configurations into the native configuration formats of different coding agents.

Specifically, the [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) library provides utilities such as [`apply_mcp_servers_simple`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L167) and [`apply_mcp_translated`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py#L844). These functions are designed to abstract away the differences in how various agents (e.g., Antigravity, Claude, Codex, Copilot, Hermes, OpenCode) consume network proxy settings. For instance, the [`harnesses/copilot/provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/copilot/provision.py) script leverages [`translate_mcp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/copilot/provision.py#L162) to convert Fabric's universal MCP server configurations into Copilot's specific format and writes them to a dedicated configuration file within the agent's environment. Similarly, the [`harnesses/codex/provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/codex/provision.py) script uses [`_build_mcp_section`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/codex/provision.py#L254) and [`_write_mcp_to_config`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/codex/provision.py#L287) to translate MCP definitions into TOML sections for the Codex agent's [`config.toml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/codex/README.md?plain=1#L37). The [`harnesses/claude/provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/claude/provision.py) script also uses [`fabric_harness.apply_mcp_servers_simple`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L127) to adapt MCP settings for the Claude Code CLI.

This approach ensures that regardless of an agent's internal configuration mechanisms, it can consistently leverage the MCP servers defined by the Fabric platform for its communication needs. This standardization simplifies the integration of new agents and ensures uniform network behavior across the ecosystem. For further details on the common functionalities provided by this library, refer to [Shared Python Harness Library (`fabric_harness.py`)](#agent-harness-management-shared-python-harness-library-fabric-harness-py).

<a id="agent-harness-management-automated-vendoring-and-consistency-enforcement"></a>

### Automated Vendoring and Consistency Enforcement

![Diagram 41](diagrams/diagram-041.svg)

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) platform maintains consistency across its agent harness configurations through an automated vendoring process. A Go program located at [`harnesses/gen/main.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/gen/main.go) is responsible for distributing a canonical Python utility library, [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130), to all relevant harness subdirectories. This ensures that agent-specific [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91) and [`capture_auth.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L83) scripts consistently utilize the same version of shared functionalities for tasks like authentication resolution and instruction projection, as described in [Harness Bundle Structure and Core Functionality](#agent-harness-management-harness-bundle-structure-and-core-functionality).

When executed, the Go program reads the contents of the central [`harnesses/fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py). It then iterates through the harness directories, identifying those that contain a [`provision.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L91) file, which signifies an active harness bundle. For each identified bundle, it creates or overwrites a [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) file within that subdirectory. Each generated file includes a header indicating its machine-generated status, effectively discouraging manual modifications that would otherwise be overwritten during subsequent runs. This mechanism standardizes the shared Python library and prevents divergence across different agent harnesses.

To further enforce this consistency, a Go test, [`harnesses/vendored_lib_test.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/vendored_lib_test.go), verifies that all vendored copies of [`fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/README.md?plain=1#L130) precisely match the canonical source and retain the expected generated header. This test acts as a safeguard against accidental or intentional changes to vendored copies, ensuring that any modifications must be made to the central [`harnesses/fabric_harness.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/fabric_harness.py) file, thereby maintaining a single source of truth for the shared harness logic.

<a id="container-image-build-and-management"></a>

## Container Image Build and Management

![Diagram 42](diagrams/diagram-042.svg)

Fabric manages container image builds for its various components, encompassing base images, server images, and specialized harness images for different execution environments. This process is orchestrated through a flexible system that supports multiple build backends, including Docker, Podman, and Google Cloud Build. The system is designed to provide consistency and efficiency in image creation, ensuring that Fabric components have the necessary runtime environments.

The image hierarchy is structured to promote layering and reuse. Core images, such as [`core-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138), provide fundamental development tools like Go, Git, and various Unix utilities without any Fabric-specific tooling. Building upon this, [`fabric-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L84) incorporates the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) and [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) binaries, alongside a wrapper for the [`gh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go#L147) CLI to manage GitHub authentication. Further specialization leads to the [`hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/apitest/main.go#L28) image, which is configured to run the Fabric Hub server, and [`gemini`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L26) for a [`gemini-cli`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/embed.go#L24) environment. Additionally, various harness images are dynamically discovered from their respective configuration bundles, extending [`fabric-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L84) to support specific agent execution requirements. This hierarchical approach minimizes duplication and facilitates efficient updates across the Fabric ecosystem.

Build orchestration is managed by a central script, [`build-images.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/project.go#L413) in [`image-build/scripts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts), which acts as the primary interface for initiating image builds. This script utilizes a pluggable backend system, allowing users to choose their preferred build environment via flags like [`--builder local-docker`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L31), [`--builder local-podman`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L31), or [`--builder cloud-build`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L70). This design decouples the build logic from the underlying container technology, making the system adaptable to different infrastructure choices. The script also handles target sequencing, tag computation, and dependency resolution to ensure a consistent and reproducible build process.

For those utilizing Google Cloud Build, a dedicated setup script, [`setup-cloud-build.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L35) in [`image-build/scripts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts), automates the necessary Google Cloud Project configurations. This includes enabling required APIs, creating Artifact Registry Docker repositories, and setting appropriate Identity and Access Management (IAM) permissions to allow Cloud Build to push images. This integrated approach streamlines the setup of cloud-based build environments for Fabric components.

The build system also includes mechanisms for image metadata and dependency management. The script [`targets.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L32) in [`image-build/scripts/lib`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/lib) serves as the authoritative source for defining the Directed Acyclic Graph (DAG) of image builds, specifying dependencies, Dockerfile locations, build contexts, and arguments. This ensures that images are built in the correct order with the necessary upstream components. For more details on the automated vendoring process for shared harness libraries, refer to [Automated Vendoring and Consistency Enforcement](#agent-harness-management-automated-vendoring-and-consistency-enforcement).

In addition to building, the system also provides utilities for pulling pre-built images. The [`pull-containers.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L34) script in [`image-build/scripts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts) automates the retrieval of Fabric container images from a specified registry, supporting various container runtimes and dynamically discovering images including [`fabric-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L84), [`fabric-hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L213), and harness images. This ensures that users can easily deploy Fabric components with pre-configured images.

<a id="container-image-build-and-management-image-hierarchy-and-base-images"></a>

### Image Hierarchy and Base Images

![Diagram 43](diagrams/diagram-043.svg)

Fabric container images are structured hierarchically to promote efficient layering and reuse across different Fabric components. This architecture ensures that core dependencies are established once and then extended for more specialized images, streamlining maintenance and reducing build times. The entire image build process is managed from the [`image-build`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build) directory.

The foundational image in this hierarchy is the [`core-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138) image, defined by the [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138) in [`image-build/core-base/Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/core-base/Dockerfile). This image provides a robust development environment with essential tools such as Go, Git, various Unix utilities, and Google Cloud Storage FUSE. It serves as a generic, language-specific base without any Fabric-specific tooling or user configurations, making it broadly reusable.

Building upon the [`core-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138) image is the [`fabric-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L84) image, located in [`image-build/fabric-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/fabric-base). This image integrates the core Fabric binaries, specifically [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) and [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44). It also configures a [`gh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go#L147) CLI wrapper for managing GitHub authentication and sets up a dedicated [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) user to handle permissions within the container environment. The [`fabrictool init`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/common.go#L294) command is set as the entrypoint, allowing for flexible user ID/group ID mapping to the host system.

Harness images, located within the [`harnesses`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses) directory, are optional extensions that build on the [`fabric-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L84) image. These images provide specialized environments tailored for specific coding agents or workflows. Their discovery and integration into the build process are dynamic, allowing for flexible inclusion of various toolchains and dependencies as needed by different harnesses.

The [`hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/apitest/main.go#L28) image, defined by the [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138) in [`image-build/hub/Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/hub/Dockerfile), specializes the [`fabric-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L84) image to run the Fabric Hub server. It configures the necessary filesystem structure and sets the default command to start the hub server in foreground mode, enabling all hub-specific functionalities.

Finally, the [`gemini`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L26) image, configured in [`image-build/gemini/Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/gemini/Dockerfile), provides an environment for the [`gemini-cli`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/embed.go#L24) application. It installs the [`gemini-cli`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/embed.go#L24) globally via npm and sets up the required user directories for its operation. This image leverages a flexible base image argument, allowing it to integrate with different underlying environments.

<a id="container-image-build-and-management-build-orchestration-with-build-images-sh"></a>

### Build Orchestration with `build-images.sh`

![Diagram 44](diagrams/diagram-044.svg)

The [`build-images.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/project.go#L413) script, located at [`image-build/scripts/build-images.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/build-images.sh), serves as the central orchestrator for building Fabric container images. It manages the entire build process, from determining which images to build to executing the builds using various backend technologies. This orchestration script supports several key functionalities, including managing the sequence of image builds, computing appropriate tags, and enabling multi-platform builds.

The script's core strength lies in its pluggable backend architecture. It can delegate the actual image construction to different builders, such as [`local-docker`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L31), [`local-podman`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L31), or [`cloud-build`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L70), depending on the specified [`--builder`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L173) argument.
