This modularity allows the Fabric project to leverage diverse containerization tools and environments without altering the fundamental orchestration logic. Each builder ([`image-build/scripts/builders/local-docker.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/builders/local-docker.sh), [`image-build/scripts/builders/local-podman.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/builders/local-podman.sh), [`image-build/scripts/builders/cloud-build.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/builders/cloud-build.sh)) adheres to a defined interface, ensuring seamless integration with [`build-images.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/project.go#L413).

[`build-images.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/project.go#L413) is responsible for resolving build targets and their dependencies, as defined in [`image-build/scripts/lib/targets.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/lib/targets.sh). This file acts as the single source of truth for the Directed Acyclic Graph (DAG) of images, ensuring that base images are built before images that depend on them. The orchestrator also handles the computation of image tags, incorporating both mutable tags (like [`latest`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L76)) and short Git SHA hashes to prevent race conditions during chained builds. For details on how these images are defined, see [Image Metadata and Dependency Graph Management](#container-image-build-and-management-image-metadata-and-dependency-graph-management).

Furthermore, the script supports multi-platform builds, particularly when using the [`local-docker`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L31) builder with [`docker buildx`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L96) or when submitting builds to Google Cloud Build, which inherently supports multi-architecture images. This ensures that Fabric agents and services can run consistently across different hardware architectures.

In summary, [`build-images.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/project.go#L413) abstracts the complexities of container image building, providing a unified command-line interface for developers to build Fabric components while offering flexibility in choosing the underlying build technology and targeting various platforms.

<a id="container-image-build-and-management-pluggable-build-backends-docker-podman-cloud-build"></a>

### Pluggable Build Backends (Docker, Podman, Cloud Build)

![Diagram 45](diagrams/diagram-045.svg)

The Fabric image build system supports multiple pluggable backends for container image construction, allowing developers to choose their preferred environment. These backends are implemented as distinct scripts located in the [`image-build/scripts/builders`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/builders) directory.

The [`image-build/scripts/builders/local-docker.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/builders/local-docker.sh) script leverages [`docker buildx`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L96) to perform image builds. This backend is capable of orchestrating multi-architecture builds, meaning it can create images compatible with various processor architectures (e.g., [`linux/amd64`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L196), [`linux/arm64`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L196)). It manages the [`buildx`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L204) environment, creating dedicated builder instances when necessary to handle complex build requirements, such as pushing multi-platform images to a registry.

For users preferring Podman, the [`image-build/scripts/builders/local-podman.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/builders/local-podman.sh) script provides a wrapper around the [`podman build`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L171) command. This backend is primarily designed for single-architecture builds. Notably, it explicitly prevents implicit multi-platform builds and guides users to manually configure QEMU [`binfmt`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/builders/local-podman.sh#L19) for such capabilities or to utilize an alternative builder like [`image-build/scripts/builders/local-docker.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/builders/local-docker.sh). This ensures clarity regarding the underlying infrastructure required for advanced build scenarios.

The [`image-build/scripts/builders/cloud-build.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/builders/cloud-build.sh) script integrates with Google Cloud Build, acting as a "target-mode" builder. Instead of building individual images, it submits predefined [`cloudbuild-*.yaml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L240) configurations, such as the ones found within the top-level [`image-build`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build) directory, to Google Cloud Build. This allows the build process, including caching and multi-step image creation, to be managed and executed within the Google Cloud environment. It handles the dynamic determination of the Google Cloud Project and manages substitutions for variables like image tags and Git commit SHAs, ensuring that the Cloud Build configurations receive the necessary context for the build. This separation allows for the complexity of the build logic to reside within version-controlled Cloud Build configurations.

The overall build orchestration is managed by [`image-build/scripts/build-images.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/build-images.sh), which selects and invokes these backend scripts based on user preferences or specified build targets. This modular approach allows for flexible and extensible image building within the Fabric platform. For more details on the orchestration, refer to [Build Orchestration with `build-images.sh`](#container-image-build-and-management-build-orchestration-with-build-images-sh).

<a id="container-image-build-and-management-image-metadata-and-dependency-graph-management"></a>

### Image Metadata and Dependency Graph Management

![Diagram 46](diagrams/diagram-046.svg)

The file [`image-build/scripts/lib/targets.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/lib/targets.sh) functions as the central repository for metadata related to Fabric container image builds. It defines the relationships and properties of various images, ensuring a consistent and ordered build process. This includes specifying which images need to be built, in what sequence, and with what configurations.

This file explicitly lists all known buildable images and groups them into logical targets, such as [`all`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/user_query.go#L238) or [`harnesses`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L203), which represent collections of images for different purposes. A key function of this metadata store is to resolve dependencies, meaning it determines the correct order in which images must be built to satisfy their base image requirements. For example, building [`fabric-hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L213) requires [`fabric-base`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L84) to be built first.

A notable feature is the dynamic discovery of harness images. The system automatically identifies [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138)s within the [`harnesses`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses) directory. This allows new harness images to be incorporated into the build process without manual updates to the core configuration. For each image, the metadata also specifies the location of its [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138), its build context directory, and any arguments needed during the build process, such as the base image tag or registry. These definitions enable the build orchestrator, typically [`image-build/scripts/build-images.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/build-images.sh), to execute builds consistently across different environments.

<a id="container-image-build-and-management-google-cloud-build-environment-setup-and-verification"></a>

### Google Cloud Build Environment Setup and Verification

![Diagram 47](diagrams/diagram-047.svg)

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) project includes automated processes for setting up and verifying a Google Cloud Project for container image builds using Google Cloud Build. This setup involves enabling necessary APIs, creating an Artifact Registry repository, and granting appropriate IAM permissions to the Cloud Build service account.

The [`setup-cloud-build.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L35) script automates this initial provisioning. It enables the [`cloudbuild.googleapis.com`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/setup-cloud-build.sh#L76) and [`artifactregistry.googleapis.com`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/README.md?plain=1#L40) APIs, creates an Artifact Registry Docker repository if one doesn't already exist, and then grants the Cloud Build service account the [`roles/artifactregistry.writer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/setup-cloud-build.sh#L104) permission on this repository. This permission is essential for Cloud Build to push newly built container images to the registry. The script also outputs the full registry path, which is critical for subsequent build and configuration steps.

Before initiating image builds, the [`verify-registry.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/cloudbuild.yaml#L20) script performs pre-flight checks to ensure that the Cloud Build environment is correctly configured. This script verifies two main conditions: first, that the specified Artifact Registry repository exists, and second, that the active service account has the [`artifactregistry.repositories.uploadArtifacts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/verify-registry.sh#L60) permission, enabling it to push images to the registry. These checks help to proactively identify and resolve potential configuration or permission issues before they lead to build failures.

Once the Cloud Build environment is set up and verified, image builds can be orchestrated using the main [`build-images.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/project.go#L413) script with the [`--builder cloud-build`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L70) option. This script, along with the builders defined in [`image-build/scripts/builders`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/scripts/builders), handles the mapping of build targets to Cloud Build configurations and manages the necessary substitutions for image tags and registry paths. For more details on the overall image build orchestration, refer to [Container Image Build and Management](#container-image-build-and-management).

<a id="auxiliary-tools-and-integrations"></a>

## Auxiliary Tools and Integrations

| Tool Name | Directory Path | Primary Function |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Agent Visualizer | `extras/agent-viz/` | Replays agent activity from Google Cloud Logging as a 2D force-directed graph visualization. |
| Fabric Docs Agent | `extras/docs-agent/` | Q&A service about Fabric using Gemini CLI, deployed as a Cloud Run service. |
| `fabric-fs-watcher` | `extras/fs-watcher-tool/` | Monitors filesystem activity across Fabric agent worktrees and attributes events to originating agents. |
| `fabric-a2a-bridge` | `extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/` | Exposes Fabric agents as A2A (Agent-to-Agent) endpoints, translating JSON-RPC requests to Hub API calls. |
| `fabric-broker-log` | `extras/fabric-broker-log/` | Logs all messages flowing through the Fabric message broker, serving as a reference and debugging tool. |
| Fabric Chat App | `extras/fabric-chat-app/` | Bridges Google Chat (and Slack) with the Fabric Hub for agent management and notifications. |
| `fabric-plugin-discord` | `extras/fabric-discord/` | Provides bidirectional messaging between Discord channels and Fabric agents. |
| `fabric-plugin-telegram` | `extras/fabric-telegram/` | Provides bidirectional messaging between Telegram group chats and Fabric agents. |

The [`extras`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras) directory provides a suite of supplementary tools and integrations designed to extend the Fabric platform's capabilities. These tools address various aspects of agent operation, observability, and communication, ranging from visualizing agent activity to integrating with popular messaging platforms.

One core utility is [`agent-viz`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/go.mod#L1), located in [`extras/agent-viz`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz). This web-based visualizer processes Google Cloud Logging exports to reconstruct and display [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) agent activity as a 2D force-directed graph. It illustrates inter-agent communications, file interactions, and agent states, offering playback controls and filtering for detailed analysis of agent behavior. The backend Go binary parses logs and serves the web frontend, which then visualizes the data.

For AI-powered Q&A, the [`Fabric Docs Agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/docs-agent/README.md?plain=1#L1) in [`extras/docs-agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/docs-agent) provides a service that answers questions about Fabric by querying its documentation, source code, and design documents. This agent leverages the Gemini CLI to process natural language queries and offers an embeddable chat widget, alongside endpoints for refreshing its knowledge base from the Git repository.

To monitor filesystem activity, [`fabric-fs-watcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/README.md?plain=1#L1) (in [`extras/fs-watcher-tool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool)) is a Linux utility that uses the [`fanotify`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/README.md?plain=1#L3) API. It tracks file system events within [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) agent worktrees and attributes these events to specific Docker-managed agents by correlating process IDs with Docker container labels. This tool is designed to identify which agent is responsible for which file modification, offering features like dynamic directory management, noise filtering, and event coalescing.

The directory also contains several messaging platform bridges that enable Fabric agents to interact with external systems. The [`fabric-a2a-bridge`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/README.md?plain=1#L1) in [`extras/fabric-a2a-bridge`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge) serves as a protocol bridge between A2A (Application-to-Application) clients and Fabric agents. It translates JSON-RPC requests, dynamically generates A2A Agent Cards, and supports various message delivery modes including blocking, Server-Sent Events (SSE), and webhooks, with robust authentication and rate limiting.

Beyond A2A, integrations exist for widely used chat platforms. The [`fabric-broker-log`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-broker-log/README.md?plain=1#L1) plugin in [`extras/fabric-broker-log`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-broker-log) acts as a reference implementation for a [`go-plugin`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L24) based broker plugin, logging all [`messages.StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/message.go#L373) instances processed by a Fabric Hub for debugging and observability. For Google Chat, the [`fabric-chat-app`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs/design/broker-fanout.md?plain=1#L322) in [`extras/fabric-chat-app`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app) provides bidirectional messaging, agent management via slash commands, real-time notifications, and interactive flows, deployable as a Google Workspace Add-on.

Similarly, [`extras/fabric-discord`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-discord) offers a Discord bot integration, facilitating bidirectional communication between Discord channels and Fabric agents. It supports both plugin and standalone operational modes and manages commands, callbacks, and user registration. The [`fabric-slack`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/go.mod#L1) plugin in [`extras/fabric-slack`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack) enables similar bidirectional messaging for Slack channels, handling Slack events, command processing, and message formatting. Finally, [`extras/fabric-telegram`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram) provides a Telegram message broker plugin, supporting bidirectional communication between Telegram group chats and Fabric agents, managing group linking, user identities, and notifications.

<a id="auxiliary-tools-and-integrations-agent-activity-visualization-with-agent-viz"></a>

### Agent Activity Visualization with `agent-viz`

![Diagram 48](diagrams/diagram-048.svg)

The [`agent-viz`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/go.mod#L1) tool visualizes [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) agent activity from Google Cloud Logging exports as a 2D force-directed graph. It reconstructs and displays inter-agent communications, file interactions, and agent lifecycle events in a web-based interface, providing playback controls and filtering capabilities.

The tool parses Google Cloud Logging (GCP) export JSON files and optional [`fs-watcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/go.mod#L1) NDJSON logs to identify agents, map their activities, and establish a chronological sequence of events. The parsed information includes agent states, messages exchanged between agents, and file modifications. The core processing logic for this is found within the [`extras/agent-viz/internal/logparser`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/internal/logparser) directory, with [`ParseLogFile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/internal/logparser/parser.go#L146) orchestrating the overall parsing process.

A playback engine, defined in [`extras/agent-viz/internal/playback`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/internal/playback), manages the sequence and timing of these events. It allows users to control the playback speed, seek to specific points in time, and apply filters based on agents or event types. This engine provides real-time event streams, status updates, and snapshots for client-side state reconstruction.

The visualization is presented through a web interface, managed by a server component located in [`extras/agent-viz/internal/server`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/internal/server). This server serves static web assets and establishes WebSocket connections with clients. It broadcasts playback events and status updates to connected clients and processes commands received from the client to control the playback engine.

The web frontend, found in the [`extras/agent-viz/web`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/web) directory, is a single-page application responsible for rendering the visualization. It displays a force-directed graph of files, a radial layout of agents, and visual cues for messages and file edits. Playback controls, filtering options, and a communication transcript panel are integrated into the user interface. The web frontend also handles WebSocket communication to receive data from the server and send playback commands.

Developers can build, run, and test the [`agent-viz`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/go.mod#L1) tool using the [`Makefile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1) located at [`extras/agent-viz/Makefile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/Makefile). Additionally, a Python script, [`extras/agent-viz/scripts/inspect_logs.py`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/scripts/inspect_logs.py), provides a command-line utility for parsing and summarizing GCP log exports.

<a id="auxiliary-tools-and-integrations-ai-powered-q-a-with-fabric-docs-agent"></a>

### AI-Powered Q&A with Fabric Docs Agent

![Diagram 49](diagrams/diagram-049.svg)

The [`Fabric Docs Agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/docs-agent/README.md?plain=1#L1) provides an AI-powered Q&A service, enabling users to query Fabric's documentation and source code using the Gemini CLI. This agent is designed to run as a standalone Cloud Run service and offers various interaction methods.

The agent's capabilities are exposed through several HTTP endpoints. The [`/ask`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/docs-agent/README.md?plain=1#L9) endpoint allows clients to submit natural language queries, which the agent processes using the [`gemini`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L26) CLI tool and returns a Markdown-formatted answer. For interactive use, the [`/chat`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/docs-agent/README.md?plain=1#L10) endpoint serves an embeddable HTML chat widget, allowing users to engage in real-time conversations with the agent. The agent's knowledge base, derived from Fabric's documentation, source code, and design documents, can be updated on demand via a [`git pull --ff-only`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/util/git.go#L637) operation triggered by the [`/refresh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/docs-agent/README.md?plain=1#L11) endpoint. A [`/health`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L1126) endpoint is also provided for operational status checks.

Configuration of the agent, including the AI model, workspace directories, and timeouts, is managed through environment variables, facilitating flexible deployment and customization. The web server uses a [`corsMiddleware`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L2816) to ensure secure cross-origin resource sharing for all endpoints.

The [`Fabric Docs Agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/docs-agent/README.md?plain=1#L1) adheres to specific guidelines for generating responses: answers must be concise and accurate, based solely on available source material. If information cannot be found, the agent explicitly states this, and it is strictly forbidden from fabricating or speculating about undocumented features. When possible, responses reference specific files or documentation pages and are always formatted in Markdown, as defined by the system prompt in [`extras/docs-agent/system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/docs-agent/system-prompt.md).

For further details on deployment, see the [`deploy.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/README.md?plain=1#L72) script in [`extras/docs-agent/deploy.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/docs-agent/deploy.sh). The Docker image for the agent is built using the [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138) located in [`extras/docs-agent/Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/docs-agent/Dockerfile).

<a id="auxiliary-tools-and-integrations-filesystem-activity-monitoring-with-fabric-fs-watcher"></a>

### Filesystem Activity Monitoring with `fabric-fs-watcher`

![Diagram 50](diagrams/diagram-050.svg)

The [`fabric-fs-watcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/README.md?plain=1#L1) is a Linux utility designed to monitor filesystem activity within [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) agent worktrees. Its primary function is to attribute filesystem events, such as file creation, modification, deletion, and renaming, to specific Docker-managed agents. This attribution is achieved by correlating process IDs (PIDs) from filesystem events with Docker containers and their [`fabric.name`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/stop.go#L155) labels.

The tool leverages the Linux [`fanotify`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/README.md?plain=1#L3) API for efficient filesystem observation. It captures events and, by inspecting [`/proc/<pid>/cgroup`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/README.md?plain=1#L170) and querying Docker, resolves the PID associated with an event to the Docker container and subsequently to an [`agent_id`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/mutation.go#L5939). This mapping is cached to enhance performance.

Key features of [`fabric-fs-watcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/README.md?plain=1#L1) include:

- **Dynamic Directory Management**: When configured with the [`--grove`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L188) flag, the watcher automatically discovers and monitors agent worktree directories by querying Docker for containers bearing a [`fabric.grove`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/list.go#L42) label. It also listens for Docker container lifecycle events to dynamically add or remove watched directories as agents start or stop.
- **Noise Filtering**: The utility supports filtering out unwanted events using glob patterns specified via [`--ignore`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Dockerfile#L5) flags or a [`.gitignore`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L167)-style filter file designated by [`--filter-file`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/README.md?plain=1#L82). This filter can be reloaded dynamically by sending a [`SIGHUP`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/main.go#L100) signal.
- **Event Coalescing**: To manage event volume and improve clarity, the watcher employs two coalescing mechanisms:

  - **Debouncing**: Rapid, successive events on the same file from the same agent are collapsed into a single [`modify`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/LICENSE#L117) event within a configurable debounce window.
  - **Rename Coalescing**: The tool identifies common editor save patterns, where content is written to a temporary file and then renamed over the target file, translating these into a single [`modify`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/LICENSE#L117) event rather than separate [`rename_from`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/README.md?plain=1#L142) and [`rename_to`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/README.md?plain=1#L142) events.

Events are output as line-delimited JSON (NDJSON) to a specified log file or standard output, providing structured data including a timestamp, [`agent_id`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/mutation.go#L5939), action type, path, and file size. For troubleshooting, a [`--debug`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L51) flag provides verbose logging of Docker interactions, PID resolution, [`fanotify`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/README.md?plain=1#L3) setup, and event processing. The tool is developed in Go, with its core logic residing in [`extras/fs-watcher-tool/pkg/fswatcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/pkg/fswatcher).

<a id="auxiliary-tools-and-integrations-a2a-protocol-bridge-for-fabric-agents"></a>

### A2A Protocol Bridge for Fabric Agents

![Diagram 51](diagrams/diagram-051.svg)

The [`fabric-a2a-bridge`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/README.md?plain=1#L1) application facilitates communication between A2A (Application-to-Application) clients and Fabric agents. It acts as a protocol translation layer, converting A2A JSON-RPC requests into Fabric Hub API calls and vice-versa, allowing external A2A clients to interact with Fabric agents.

The bridge dynamically generates A2A Agent Cards, which provide metadata about exposed Fabric agents to A2A clients. This enables discoverability and understanding of an agent's capabilities within the A2A ecosystem.

Communication between the A2A client and Fabric agents can occur in several modes:

- **Blocking Request/Response**: For synchronous interactions where the client waits for an immediate response.
- **Server-Sent Events (SSE)**: For real-time updates and streaming task status changes from the Fabric agent back to the A2A client. The [`StreamManager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/stream.go#L56) in [`extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/stream.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/stream.go) handles the server-side logic for managing these event streams.
- **Webhook-based Push Notifications**: For asynchronous delivery of task state changes to client-defined webhook URLs. The [`PushDispatcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/push.go#L38) in [`extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/push.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/push.go) manages the dispatching of these notifications, incorporating robust SSRF protection and retry mechanisms.

To ensure secure and controlled access, the bridge implements robust authentication and authorization mechanisms. Client authentication typically uses API keys or bearer tokens, which are processed by [`authMiddleware`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/server.go#L289) within the HTTP server handler ([`Server`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L559) in [`extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/server.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/server.go)). Authorization checks ([`AuthorizeExposed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/bridge.go#L1120), [`AuthorizeTask`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/bridge.go#L1139), [`AuthorizeContext`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/bridge.go#L1153) in [`extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/bridge.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/bridge.go)) enforce project and agent-level access control, preventing unauthorized interaction and maintaining tenant isolation for A2A tasks. Additionally, a [`RateLimitMiddleware`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/ratelimit.go#L136) (defined in [`extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/ratelimit.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/ratelimit.go)) is utilized to manage the rate of incoming requests, protecting the service from abuse and ensuring fair usage.

The bridge manages the lifecycle of tasks initiated by A2A clients, from creation through various states (e.g., submitted, working, completed, failed, input required) and eventual cleanup. Task lifecycle state is persistently stored, typically in a local SQLite database, allowing for resilience and continuity of operations.

The [`fabric-a2a-bridge`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/README.md?plain=1#L1) is deployable as a Docker container, as specified in its [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138) in [`extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/Dockerfile), providing a self-contained and portable solution for integrating A2A clients with the Fabric platform. For a deeper understanding of the overall design, refer to [A2A Bridge Design and Evolution](#design-specifications-and-architecture-a2a-bridge-design-and-evolution).

<a id="auxiliary-tools-and-integrations-fabric-message-broker-logging-plugin"></a>

### FABRIC Message Broker Logging Plugin

![Diagram 52](diagrams/diagram-052.svg)

The [`fabric-broker-log`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-broker-log/README.md?plain=1#L1) plugin, found in the [`extras/fabric-broker-log`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-broker-log) directory, functions as a reference implementation for [`go-plugin`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L24) based broker plugins within the Fabric ecosystem. Its primary purpose is to capture and log all [`messages.StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/message.go#L373) instances processed by a Fabric Hub. This plugin offers configurable output formats, allowing messages to be displayed in human-readable text or structured JSON Lines. Users can filter messages by topic using NATS-style subscription patterns and control the level of detail, including displaying full message bodies or truncated versions, and specifying which fields to include.

A notable feature of [`fabric-broker-log`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-broker-log/README.md?plain=1#L1) is its "forwarding mode." When enabled, the plugin acts as a proxy: it logs messages internally and then relays them to another specified broker plugin. This capability addresses the Fabric Hub's design, which typically supports only a single broker plugin at a time, allowing [`fabric-broker-log`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-broker-log/README.md?plain=1#L1) to coexist with other broker plugins and provide logging without disrupting the message flow. For more details on the event bus, refer to [Event Bus for Real-time Messaging](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-event-bus-for-real-time-messaging).

The plugin integrates with the Fabric Hub via HashiCorp's [`go-plugin`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L24) library, allowing it to run as a separate process and communicate through RPC. This design ensures that message processing, logging, and configuration occur out-of-process from the main hub. While message traffic is directed to standard output, lifecycle events and errors are routed to standard error, facilitating easier output filtering and debugging.

<a id="auxiliary-tools-and-integrations-google-chat-integration-with-fabric-hub"></a>

### Google Chat Integration with Fabric Hub

![Diagram 53](diagrams/diagram-053.svg)

The [`fabric-chat-app`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs/design/broker-fanout.md?plain=1#L322) is a Go application that bridges Google Chat with a Fabric Hub instance, enabling users to manage Fabric agents, receive real-time notifications, and interact with the platform directly from Google Chat. It operates as a Google Workspace Add-on, receiving HTTP events from Google Chat and responding with messages, cards, and interactive dialogs.

The application facilitates bidirectional communication, allowing users to issue slash commands within Google Chat to control agents (e.g., list, start, stop, create, delete, subscribe) and manage workspace links. It leverages a [`CommandRouter`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/chatapp/commands.go#L56) ([`extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/chatapp/commands.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/chatapp/commands.go)) to process incoming chat events and dispatch them to specific handlers, streamlining agent and space management.

A core feature is the [`NotificationRelay`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/chatapp/notifications.go#L28) ([`extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/chatapp/notifications.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/chatapp/notifications.go)), which processes messages from the Fabric Hub's message broker and delivers them as formatted cards or direct messages to Google Chat spaces. This ensures users receive timely updates on agent activities and project statuses.

User identity and authentication are managed by the [`identity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/identity.go#L25) package ([`extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/identity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/identity)), which handles the creation and signing of JSON Web Tokens (JWTs) for secure communication with the Fabric Hub. It also manages the mapping between Google Chat users and Fabric Hub accounts, supporting both automatic and manual user registration. This ensures that interactions are authenticated and authorized correctly. For more details on secure credential and daemon management, see [Secure Credential and Daemon Management](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-secure-credential-and-daemon-management).

Persistent local application state, such as user mappings, space-to-grove links, and agent subscriptions, is maintained in an SQLite database, managed by the [`state`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L833) package ([`extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/state`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/state)). This database handles schema migrations and CRUD operations to ensure data integrity and persistence.

The application integrates with Google Chat through an [`Adapter`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/googlechat/adapter.go#L39) ([`extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/googlechat/adapter.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/googlechat/adapter.go)), which normalizes Google Chat events into a platform-agnostic format for internal processing and renders generic UI components into Google Chat Cards V2. Authentication with Google Chat APIs is handled by [`auth.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtimebroker/handlers.go#L1976) ([`extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/googlechat/auth.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/googlechat/auth.go)), including preflight checks to verify credentials and permissions.

The [`fabric-chat-app`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs/design/broker-fanout.md?plain=1#L322) can be deployed in various ways, including as a Docker container, built and installed directly on a Hub VM, or deployed to Google Cloud Run, offering flexibility in its operational environment.

<a id="auxiliary-tools-and-integrations-discord-bot-integration-for-fabric"></a>

### Discord Bot Integration for Fabric

![Diagram 54](diagrams/diagram-054.svg)

The Discord bot integration for Fabric ([`extras/fabric-discord`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-discord)) facilitates bidirectional messaging between Discord channels and Fabric agents. This integration operates in two primary modes: [`Plugin mode`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L43) and [`Standalone mode`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L48).

In [`Plugin mode`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L43), the Discord bot functions as a [`go-plugin`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L24) subprocess, tightly coupled with the Fabric Hub. Alternatively, [`Standalone mode`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L48) allows the bot to run as an independent gRPC service. This mode provides high availability (HA) through the use of PostgreSQL advisory locks, ensuring that only one instance actively connects to the Discord Gateway at any given time, with automatic failover if the primary instance becomes unavailable.

The integration manages outbound [`StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L33)s from the Fabric Hub to Discord. These messages are formatted and sent to linked Discord channels. To enhance clarity and user experience, each Fabric agent is represented in Discord with a distinct identity (custom name and avatar), utilizing Discord webhooks for this purpose. Conversely, inbound messages from Discord are converted into [`StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L33)s and delivered to the relevant Fabric agents through the hub's inbound endpoint. Message routing to agents is determined by [`@-mentions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-discord/README.md?plain=1#L199) within Discord messages (e.g., [`@agentslug message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-discord/README.md?plain=1#L3) or [`@all message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-discord/README.md?plain=1#L3)) or by designating a [`default`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L433) agent for channels. Replies to bot messages automatically continue the conversation with the original agent.

The bot provides various command-line interface (CLI) commands for users to manage channel links, register Discord accounts with Fabric identities, and interact with agents. For instance, commands such as [`/fabric setup`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/dist.sh#L48), [`/fabric register`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/README.md?plain=1#L103), and [`/fabric agents`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/server.go#L86) enable users to configure the integration. For more details on Fabric's CLI, refer to [Command-Line Interface (CLI) Operations](#command-line-interface-cli-operations). The bot also supports agent-led installation, allowing AI coding assistants or deployment agents to remotely configure the plugin by gathering necessary Discord credentials and injecting them into the [`settings.yaml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L58) configuration.

To prevent Discord API rate limits, the integration incorporates a [`SendQueue`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-discord/internal/discord/sendqueue.go#L43) mechanism. This queue manages outbound messages with per-channel worker goroutines and configurable rate limiting, ensuring reliable message delivery. Persistence of channel links, user mappings, conversation contexts, and other state information is handled using an SQLite database in [`Plugin mode`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L43) or a PostgreSQL database in [`Standalone mode`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L48). Secure communication with the hub API for registration purposes in [`Standalone mode`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/image-build/README.md?plain=1#L48) is achieved using HMAC-SHA256 authentication.

<a id="auxiliary-tools-and-integrations-slack-messaging-integration-for-fabric"></a>

### Slack Messaging Integration for Fabric

![Diagram 55](diagrams/diagram-055.svg)

The [`fabric-slack`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/go.mod#L1) plugin facilitates bidirectional communication between Fabric agents and Slack channels, operating as a [`go-plugin`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L24) subprocess within the Fabric ecosystem. This integration enables agents to send messages to Slack users and channels, and conversely, allows Slack users to interact with Fabric agents via commands and interactive components.

The plugin's core logic is managed by the [`SlackBroker`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/broker.go#L102) in [`extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/broker.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/broker.go), which handles interactions with the Slack Bot API and the central Fabric Hub API. Configuration for the broker includes Slack API tokens, signing secrets, and a [`hub_url`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/manager.go#L445) for communication with the Fabric platform. The broker supports both HTTP webhooks and Socket Mode for receiving Slack events, providing flexibility in deployment. Messages originating from Fabric agents, encapsulated as [`messages.StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/message.go#L373) types, are published to Slack. The system intelligently routes these messages to appropriate channels or threads based on metadata, recipient emails, or project-linked channels. It also handles interactive messages, such as those requiring user input ([`messages.TypeInputNeeded`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/notifications.go#L392)), by rendering Slack Block Kit components for user interaction.

Incoming Slack events, whether general messages, mentions, or interactive component actions, are processed by an [`eventServer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/events.go#L27) defined in [`extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/events.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/events.go). This server verifies request signatures for security and dispatches events to specialized handlers. Commands issued via Slack, such as [`/fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L109) slash commands, and actions from interactive components are managed by functions in [`extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/commands.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/commands.go) and [`extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/modals.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/modals.go). These handlers route user input to the Fabric Hub, potentially triggering agent actions or workflows.

Message content is formatted for Slack's [`mrkdwn`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/blocks.go#L18) and Block Kit using utilities in [`extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/blocks.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/blocks.go), ensuring proper display and handling of message length constraints. To maintain state across interactions, the plugin employs an SQLite-based persistent store, implemented in [`extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/store.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/store.go). This store manages critical information such as links between Slack channels and Fabric projects, mappings between Slack users and Fabric identities, conversation contexts, and pending user input requests. Communication with the central Fabric Hub API is facilitated by the [`HubClient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/hubclient.go#L40) interface and its implementation in [`extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/hubclient.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/hubclient.go), which handles authenticated requests to fetch project and agent information. User registration and linking Slack users to Fabric identities are managed by the [`RegistrationHandler`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/register.go#L28) in [`extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/register.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-slack/internal/slack/register.go).

<a id="auxiliary-tools-and-integrations-telegram-message-broker-plugin-for-fabric"></a>

### Telegram Message Broker Plugin for Fabric

![Diagram 56](diagrams/diagram-056.svg)

The [`fabric-telegram`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/go.mod#L1) message broker plugin facilitates bidirectional communication between Telegram group chats and Fabric agents. This plugin can operate in various modes to integrate with the Fabric ecosystem, managing message flow, user identities, and interactive elements.

The plugin acts as an intermediary, formatting [`StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L33)s from the Fabric hub for delivery to Telegram users and converting inbound Telegram messages into [`StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L33)s for Fabric agents. This includes handling text messages, commands, and attachments. It relies on [`extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/api.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/api.go) for all interactions with the Telegram Bot API, managing functionalities such as sending messages, documents, and configuring webhooks.

For persistence, the plugin stores critical state information—such as linked Telegram groups to Fabric projects, user mappings, and notification preferences—in a database, either SQLite for local operation or PostgreSQL for high-availability scenarios. Rate limiting is enforced through a [`SendQueue`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-discord/internal/discord/sendqueue.go#L43) to comply with Telegram's API usage policies.

The plugin supports several operational modes, which are determined by environment variables or command-line arguments, as detailed in [`extras/fabric-telegram/cmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/cmd):

- **Plugin Mode**: In this mode, the [`fabric-telegram`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/go.mod#L1) plugin runs as a [`go-plugin`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L24) subprocess, integrating directly with the Fabric hub's [`FanOutBroker`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs/design/broker-fanout.md?plain=1#L82). This allows the Fabric hub to manage the plugin's lifecycle and communication.
- **Standalone gRPC Service Mode**: For deployments requiring higher availability or independent scaling, the plugin can run as a standalone gRPC service. This mode necessitates a PostgreSQL database for state persistence and exclusively uses webhooks for inbound messaging, rather than long-polling. It also incorporates mechanisms for gRPC health checks and uses PostgreSQL advisory locks to coordinate webhook registration across multiple instances, ensuring high availability.
- **Migration Tool Mode**: This mode provides a command-line utility for migrating data, such as group links and user mappings, from an SQLite database to a PostgreSQL database. This is useful when transitioning from a local setup to a more robust standalone deployment.

The plugin manages user and group interactions through several mechanisms:

- **Commands**: It processes various bot commands, such as [`/setup`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/cleanup.sh#L49) for linking Telegram groups to Fabric projects, [`/default`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/README.md?plain=1#L154) for setting default agents, and [`/register`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/README.md?plain=1#L144) for associating Telegram users with Fabric identities. Command handling logic resides in [`extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/commands.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/commands.go).
- **Callbacks**: Interactive inline keyboards, dynamically generated by functions in [`extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/cards.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/cards.go), allow users to interact with agents through button presses. The [`CallbackHandler`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-discord/internal/discord/callbacks.go#L18) in [`extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/callbacks.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/callbacks.go) processes these callback queries for various actions, including multi-step setup flows and user prompts.
- **Message Routing**: Inbound messages are routed to specific Fabric agents based on [`@`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L74)-mentions within the Telegram chat, a configured default agent for the group, or by replying to bot messages.
- **User Registration**: An HTTP-based registration server, implemented in [`extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/register.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/register.go), facilitates linking Telegram user accounts to Fabric email addresses, using time-limited tokens for secure association.

The plugin ensures that messages from Fabric agents are correctly formatted for Telegram, handling aspects like text rendering, HTML escaping, and message length limits, as implemented in [`extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/format.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/format.go). The Dockerfile at [`extras/fabric-telegram/Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/Dockerfile) outlines the build process for creating a minimal, [`distroless`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-discord/Dockerfile#L6) container image of the [`fabric-plugin-telegram`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/README.md?plain=1#L1) for deployment. For further details on configuration, deployment, and troubleshooting, refer to [`extras/fabric-telegram/README.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/README.md).

<a id="fabric-platform-skills"></a>

## Fabric Platform Skills

| Skill | Description | Path to SKILL.md |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `fabric/` | Fabric CLI reference for agent management, templates, and configuration. | `fabric/SKILL.md` |
| `team-creation/` | Guides the creation and extension of Fabric agent team templates based on role descriptions and workflows. | `team-creation/SKILL.md` |
| `fabric-cli-operations/` | Defines operational constraints for Fabric agents, including non-interactive mode and prohibited commands. | `fabric-cli-operations/SKILL.md` |
| `fabric-messaging/` | Teaches effective use of `fabric message` for inter-agent and agent-to-user communication, covering recipients, timing, and content. | `fabric-messaging/SKILL.md` |
| `agent-status-signals/` | Details the mandatory status signaling protocol (`ask_user`, `blocked`, `task_completed`) for Fabric agents. | `agent-status-signals/SKILL.md` |
| `git-sandbox/` | Provides a Git workflow protocol tailored for agents in restricted sandbox/worktree environments. | `git-sandbox/SKILL.md` |

Platform-level skill definitions are automatically injected into Fabric agents, providing foundational knowledge for agents to operate within the Fabric ecosystem. These skills, located in [`skills`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills), guide agent behavior, define operational constraints, and establish communication protocols essential for multi-agent coordination and task execution.

All skills within this directory are automatically injected into agents upon provisioning. Conditional injection is managed through an [`inject_when`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L18) field in the [`SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/skills.go#L193) frontmatter of each skill, allowing specific skills to be activated only when certain environmental conditions are met, such as the presence of a Git workspace. Each skill is organized into a dedicated directory containing a [`SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/skills.go#L193) file for its definition and an optional [`scripts/`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L225) subdirectory for backing shell scripts.

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) skill, defined in [`skills/fabric/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric/SKILL.md), provides a comprehensive command-line interface reference for agents, covering core agent lifecycle management, template handling, and configuration commands. It enables agents to initialize projects, start and stop other agents, list active agents, attach to interactive sessions, and manage agent templates.

For operational constraints, the [`fabric-cli-operations`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L11) skill, detailed in [`skills/fabric-cli-operations/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-cli-operations/SKILL.md), dictates mandatory guidelines for agents operating in containerized sandboxes. This includes enforcing non-interactive mode for commands, requiring structured JSON output, and prohibiting certain operations like direct synchronization or global configurations to ensure secure and autonomous execution within the Fabric platform.

Inter-agent and agent-to-user communication protocols are established by the [`fabric-messaging`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L12) skill, explained in [`skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md). This skill educates agents on effective usage of the [`fabric message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1) command, covering recipient types, message timing, content best practices for functional and concrete details, and advanced flags for channel and thread targeting. It also outlines coordination patterns such as [`Coordinator Relay`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L71) and [`Context Sharding`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L72), while identifying communication anti-patterns.

To prevent false stall detections and ensure accurate reporting, the [`agent-status-signals`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13) skill, specified in [`skills/agent-status-signals/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/agent-status-signals/SKILL.md), defines a standard status signaling protocol. This protocol mandates the use of [`fabrictool status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50) with signals like [`ask_user`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13) (awaiting input), [`blocked`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L436) (intentionally waiting), and [`task_completed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13) (task finished). This explicit signaling mechanism ensures that both the orchestration system and users are accurately informed of an agent's current state.

For agents operating within restricted Git environments, the [`git-sandbox`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L14) skill, outlined in [`skills/git-sandbox/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/git-sandbox/SKILL.md), provides a specialized Git workflow protocol. This skill, injected when a [`git_workspace`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L14) is active, guides agents through local-only Git operations (given no network access), worktree-aware branch management, and non-interactive conflict resolution techniques to prevent execution errors in sandboxed environments.

Finally, the [`team-creation`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L10) skill, described in [`skills/team-creation/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/team-creation/SKILL.md), facilitates the generation and extension of [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) agent templates from high-level descriptions. This enables the creation of multi-agent teams with specialized roles, defining workflows, and integrating reusable harness skills for coordinated LLM agent operations. It follows an "Orchestrator Pattern" where a single orchestrator manages multiple worker agents.

<a id="fabric-platform-skills-fabric-cli-operations-and-constraints"></a>

### Fabric CLI Operations and Constraints

| Category | Command/Option | Rule | Reason |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Mandatory** | `--non-interactive` | **MUST** be used with all commands. | Prevents indefinite blocking at interactive prompts. Implies `--yes`. |
| **Mandatory** | `--format json` | **SHOULD** be used for machine-readable output. | Provides detailed, structured output from most commands. |
| **Prohibited** | `sync`, `cdw` | **DO NOT USE**. | These commands are not permitted for agent operations. |
| **Prohibited** | `--no-hub` | **DO NOT USE**. | Agents only have access to the system through the hub. |
| **Prohibited** | `--global` | **NEVER USE**. | Agents operate in a grove workspace where this is implicitly set. |
| **Prohibited** | `settings`, `login` commands | **DO NOT INTERACT WITH**. | Agents should not manage system settings or authentication. |
| **Recommendation** | `fabric look <agent-id>` | Use to inspect agents. | View recent output and terminal-UI state of running agents. |
| **Recommendation** | `fabric --help` | Use for detailed CLI information. | Access specific details on all hierarchical commands. |
| **Recommendation** | Avoid pre-emptive exploration of `.fabric` folders or agent-template files. | Focus only on task-relevant CLI usage. | Prevents unnecessary actions and maintains focus. |

Fabric agents operate within containerized sandboxes, and their interactions with the Fabric CLI are subject to specific operational guidelines to ensure secure, autonomous, and non-interactive execution. These rules, detailed in [`skills/fabric-cli-operations/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-cli-operations/SKILL.md), prevent agents from blocking on user input and enforce a programmatic approach to command output.

A core directive is the mandatory use of the [`--non-interactive`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L40) flag with the Fabric CLI, which implicitly includes [`--yes`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L337). This prevents commands from pausing for user confirmation, instead causing an error if interaction is required, thereby maintaining the agent's autonomous operation. Similarly, agents are instructed to use the [`--format json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L1045) flag for nearly all commands. This ensures that command outputs are machine-readable, facilitating parsing and processing by other system components or agents.

Several commands and options are explicitly prohibited to maintain the integrity and controlled environment of the Fabric ecosystem. Agents are forbidden from using the [`sync`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/mock.go#L101) and [`cdw`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cdw.go#L31) commands, as well as the [`--no-hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L793) option, which mandates all system access to occur through the central Hub. The [`--global`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L234) option is also prohibited because agents inherently operate within a [`grove`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L72) workspace. Furthermore, agents are advised against resuming another agent unless they were the one that originally stopped it, to avoid conflicts or unintended behaviors with actively working agents.

System messages directed to an agent, such as instructions or notifications, are formatted within [`---BEGIN FABRIC MESSAGE---`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/messages/format.go#L22) and [`---END FABRIC MESSAGE---`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/messages/format.go#L22) markers, indicating a structured approach to inter-agent communication. These guidelines, while specific, collectively establish a framework for Fabric agents to function reliably and securely within their orchestrated environments. For more on inter-agent communication, see [Inter-Agent and User Communication Protocols](#fabric-platform-skills-inter-agent-and-user-communication-protocols).

<a id="fabric-platform-skills-inter-agent-and-user-communication-protocols"></a>

### Inter-Agent and User Communication Protocols

![Diagram 57](diagrams/diagram-057.svg)

The [`fabric message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1) command is the designated method for all inter-agent and agent-to-user communication within the Fabric orchestration environment, where agents operate without visible terminal output. The guidance emphasizes fostering reliable and high-signal communication to prevent common failures associated with unclear or untimely information exchange.

Agents are instructed on addressing messages to specific recipients, including other agents ([`agent:<name>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/message.go#L57)), human users ([`user:<email>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/handlers_agent_messaging.go#L128)), or predefined groups ([`set[a,b,...]`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L28)). The use of broadcast messaging ([`--broadcast`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/message.go#L62)) is discouraged to avoid information overload and maintain message relevance.

Best practices for message content focus on functional and concrete details, such as file paths, branch names, URLs, and error messages. When human input is required, agents are encouraged to [`Surface Decisions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/contributing/architecture.md?plain=1#L314) by offering concrete options, which facilitates clear and efficient user interaction. Messages can be targeted to specific channels ([`--channel <name>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/message.go#L112)) or linked to existing conversations using a thread ID ([`--thread-id <id>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L55)).

Timing and cadence are important considerations for message delivery. Agents should provide [`Immediate Acknowledgment`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L37) for tasks, engage in [`Milestone Reporting`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L38) at significant stages, and offer updates if tasks extend beyond expectations to avoid prolonged silence. For situations where an agent is intentionally waiting for an external event, the [`fabrictool status blocked`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50) command should be used. This signals to the orchestration system that the agent is not stalled but is awaiting input, preventing misinterpretation of its state.

Advanced messaging capabilities are available through various [`fabric message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1) flags. These include [`--raw`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/message.go#L117) for sending literal keystrokes to an agent's [`tmux`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L74) terminal, [`--wake`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/message.go#L167) to resume suspended agents, and [`--interrupt`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric/SKILL.md?plain=1#L91) to halt an agent's current process. Agents can also subscribe to state-change notifications ([`--notify`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L192)), attach files to messages ([`--attach <file>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-telegram/internal/telegram/broker_v2.go#L699)), or schedule messages for delayed delivery ([`--in <delay>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L66) or [`--at <time>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L271)).

For inter-agent coordination, patterns like [`Coordinator Relay`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L71) can be used for communication between agents, [`Context Sharding`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L72) for distributing long tasks, and [`Self-Callback Heartbeat`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md?plain=1#L73) (using [`fabric message --in`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1)) for managing long-running processes.
