The guidelines also address multi-user communication, emphasizing independent replies and context isolation to maintain clarity in projects involving multiple human participants.

The [`skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric-messaging/SKILL.md) document explicitly outlines anti-patterns to avoid, such as excessive silence from an agent, low-signal messages, or using generic [`sleep`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/command_bus.go#L316) commands instead of [`fabrictool status blocked`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50). This framework is designed to optimize agent autonomy and coordination efficiency by distinguishing between an agent's internal cognitive processes and its external communication, thereby reducing noise and improving the overall effectiveness of multi-agent systems. The standardized [`fabrictool status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50) signaling protocol is further detailed in [Standard Agent Status Signaling Protocol](#fabric-platform-skills-standard-agent-status-signaling-protocol).

<a id="fabric-platform-skills-standard-agent-status-signaling-protocol"></a>

### Standard Agent Status Signaling Protocol

| Signal Name | Purpose | Post-Signal Agent Action |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `ask_user` | Signal that the agent is waiting for user or coordinator input. | Ask the question via `fabric message`. |
| `blocked` | Signal intentional waiting for an external event (e.g., child agent, scheduled event, user reply). | The agent remains idle until the blocking condition is resolved. |
| `task_completed` | Signal that the agent has successfully finished its assigned task. | The agent should stop execution. |

Fabric agents communicate their operational state to the orchestration system through a standardized signaling protocol, detailed in the [`SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/skills.go#L193) file within the [`skills/agent-status-signals`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/agent-status-signals) directory. This protocol is crucial for preventing false stall detections, enabling accurate notifications, and ensuring that users and the orchestration system have a clear understanding of an agent's current activities. Every agent template is expected to incorporate this skill, ensuring consistent behavior across the platform.

The protocol defines three mandatory signals that agents send using the [`fabrictool status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50) command:

- **[`ask_user`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13)**: This signal indicates that an agent is awaiting input from a user or coordinator. Following this signal, the agent is expected to use the [`fabric message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1) command to pose a specific question.
- **[`blocked`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L436)**: This signal denotes that an agent is intentionally waiting for a particular event, such as the completion of a child agent's task, a scheduled event, or a user's reply. By explicitly signaling a [`blocked`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L436) state, the system avoids misinterpreting intentional pauses as stalls. The [`blocked`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L436) status automatically clears when the agent resumes its work. Agents waiting for new assignments must use [`fabrictool status blocked`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L50) to prevent triggering stall detection.
- **[`task_completed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13)**: This signal reports that an agent has successfully finished its current task. Upon signaling completion, agents are expected to summarize their work and then cease further activity.

This explicit state signaling mechanism differentiates between intentional waiting and unintentional stalls, which helps prevent premature termination or erroneous notifications. This design ensures that both the orchestration system and users receive precise updates regarding an agent's operational status. The [`task_completed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L13) signal provides a clear conclusion to an agent's work without requiring further prompts or actions. For more details on inter-agent communication, refer to [Inter-Agent and User Communication Protocols](#fabric-platform-skills-inter-agent-and-user-communication-protocols).

<a id="fabric-platform-skills-git-workflow-for-sandboxed-environments"></a>

### Git Workflow for Sandboxed Environments

![Diagram 58](diagrams/diagram-058.svg)

The Git workflow protocol for Fabric agents operating in restricted, non-interactive sandbox or worktree environments is defined in [`skills/git-sandbox/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/git-sandbox/SKILL.md). This protocol establishes mandatory syntax and guidelines for Git operations within such environments, primarily to prevent execution errors and processes from hanging due to environmental constraints. This ensures agents can manage changes without direct user intervention or network access for remote Git operations.

Key aspects of this workflow include:

- **Local-Only Operations**: Agents are instructed to treat the local [`main`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabric/main.go#L19) branch as the definitive source of truth, as the environment is air-gapped from [`origin`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/LICENSE#L141). Commands that involve network interaction, such as [`git fetch`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102), [`git pull`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102), or [`git push`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102), are expected to fail. Instead, agents perform rebases or merges against the local [`main`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabric/main.go#L19) branch directly.
- **Worktree-Aware Branch Management**: When operating within a Git worktree, agents cannot directly [`git checkout main`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102) if [`main`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabric/main.go#L19) is already checked out elsewhere. The protocol guides agents to perform comparisons, rebases, and merges from their current branch by referencing [`main`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabric/main.go#L19) directly. This includes patterns like [`git diff main...HEAD`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102) for viewing changes and [`git show main:path/to/file.ext`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102) for inspecting file content on [`main`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabric/main.go#L19) without switching branches.
- **Non-Interactive Conflict Resolution**: The protocol addresses the challenge of resolving conflicts in an environment where terminal-based editors (like Vi or Vim) are unavailable and would cause processes to hang. Agents are instructed to use environment variables and flags to automate commit message generation and continue rebases. For instance, [`GIT_EDITOR=true git rebase --continue`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102) is used to proceed with a rebase, and [`git merge main --no-edit`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102) facilitates merges without requiring an editor for the commit message.
- **Structured Conflict Resolution**: A structured approach to resolving conflicts is provided. This involves identifying conflicted files using [`git status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102), resolving conflicts within the source files, staging the resolved changes with [`git add <resolved-files>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102), and then finalizing the rebase or merge with [`GIT_EDITOR=true git rebase --continue`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102). This systematic process ensures that agents can navigate and resolve conflicts autonomously.

<a id="fabric-platform-skills-fabric-agent-lifecycle-and-project-management"></a>

### Fabric Agent Lifecycle and Project Management

![Diagram 59](diagrams/diagram-059.svg)

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) platform provides a command-line interface and associated scripts for orchestrating concurrent Large Language Model (LLM)-based agents. These agents are designed to operate in parallel, each within isolated workspaces and with distinct credentials and identities. The system introduces several core concepts for agent management:

- **Projects:** Agents are organized into projects, represented by a [`.fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L34) directory. Projects can be local to a specific repository or global, residing in [`~/.fabric/`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/project.go#L121).
- **Agents:** An agent is an isolated LLM instance executing within a container. Each agent possesses its own Git worktree as a workspace, dedicated credentials, and specific configuration.
- **Templates:** Templates act as blueprints for agent creation, defining their initial setup and characteristics. Examples include templates for [`gemini`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L26), [`claude`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L27), [`opencode`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L83), and [`codex`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L83) agents.
- **Harnesses:** A harness specifies the particular LLM interface an agent utilizes, such as the Gemini CLI or Claude Code.

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) command-line tool offers a comprehensive set of subcommands for managing the lifecycle of these agents, as detailed in [`skills/fabric/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric/SKILL.md). Commands are available for project initialization ([`fabric init`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1)), starting agents ([`fabric start`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1)), listing active agents ([`fabric list`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1)), attaching to interactive agent sessions ([`fabric attach`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1)), and sending messages between agents ([`fabric message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1)). Agents can be stopped ([`fabric stop`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1)), resumed ([`fabric resume`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1)), and deleted ([`fabric delete`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1)), with options to preserve associated Git branches during deletion. The [`fabric sync`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1) command facilitates workspace synchronization, and [`fabric templates`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1) enables management of agent templates, including listing, showing configurations, creating new templates, and updating defaults. Configuration settings for [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) can be managed using [`fabric config`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1), allowing for both local and global modifications.

Supporting scripts within [`skills/fabric/scripts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric/scripts) simplify common agent operations by wrapping [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI commands. These include scripts to retrieve agent status ([`skills/fabric/scripts/agent-status.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric/scripts/agent-status.sh)), list agents ([`skills/fabric/scripts/list-agents.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric/scripts/list-agents.sh)), send messages ([`skills/fabric/scripts/send-message.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric/scripts/send-message.sh)), and start agents ([`skills/fabric/scripts/start-agent.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/fabric/scripts/start-agent.sh)). These scripts handle argument parsing and forward them to the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) utility, streamlining command execution for users. For further details on inter-agent communication, refer to [Inter-Agent and User Communication Protocols](#fabric-platform-skills-inter-agent-and-user-communication-protocols).

<a id="fabric-platform-skills-team-creation-and-multi-agent-orchestration-templates"></a>

### Team Creation and Multi-Agent Orchestration Templates

![Diagram 60](diagrams/diagram-060.svg)

The [`team-creation`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L10) skill provides mechanisms for generating and extending [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) agent templates from high-level descriptions. This facilitates the creation of multi-agent teams with specialized roles, defining workflows, and integrating reusable harness skills, all structured within the [`.fabric/templates/`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/init.go#L357) directory.

Each agent template is represented by a directory under [`.fabric/templates/`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/init.go#L357) and includes several key files:

- [`fabric-agent.yaml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/team-creation/SKILL.md?plain=1#L40): Configures metadata such as [`schema_version`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/admin-server-config.ts#L189), [`description`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L666), references to behavioral instructions ([`agents.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L173)), and persona framing ([`system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/provision.go#L960)). It can also define optional parameters like [`max_turns`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/shared/types.ts#L328), [`max_duration`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/shared/types.ts#L330), environment variables ([`env`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L162)), and service dependencies.
- [`agents.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L173): Contains the behavioral instructions for the agent, outlining its responsibilities and task constraints.
- [`system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/provision.go#L960): Defines the agent's persona, expertise, and perspective. This file is optional; if omitted, the [`system_prompt`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/agent-configure.ts#L39) entry is removed from [`fabric-agent.yaml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/team-creation/SKILL.md?plain=1#L40).
- [`skills/`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.gcloudignore#L31): An optional directory for reusable skill definitions, each conforming to the [agentskills.io](https://agentskills.io/) standard, with its own [`SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/skills.go#L193) file. These skills are designed to be harness-agnostic and are automatically integrated into the appropriate harness-specific location during agent provisioning. The [`team-creation`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/README.md?plain=1#L10) skill itself is defined by [`skills/team-creation/SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/skills/team-creation/SKILL.md).

The design of multi-agent teams typically follows an "Orchestrator Pattern":

- **Orchestrator**: A single orchestrator agent serves as the entry point for the team. Its instructions define the available worker templates, the overall workflow, communication protocols, and criteria for task completion.
- **Workers**: Other agents are workers, managed and initiated by the orchestrator. They communicate primarily with the orchestrator, simplifying communication flow within the team.

New teams are created by analyzing requirements, designing the team structure, generating templates for each role, adding specialized skills, and validating adherence to defined formats. Existing teams can be extended by reviewing current configurations and applying changes to roles, workflows, or capabilities while maintaining consistency across templates.

Key design principles include:

- **Inheritance**: Custom templates inherit from a built-in [`default`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L433) template, providing base [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) infrastructure without requiring duplication.
- **Separation of Concerns**: [`agents.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L173) focuses on agent actions ("what"), while [`system-prompt.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/provision.go#L960) defines agent identity ("who"), promoting clarity and modularity.
- **Harness Portability**: Skills defined in [`SKILL.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/skills.go#L193) are designed to function across different LLM harnesses.
- **Centralized Orchestration**: Worker agents communicate exclusively with the orchestrator, streamlining inter-agent communication.

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture"></a>

## Design Specifications and Architecture

![Diagram 61](diagrams/diagram-061.svg)

The [`.design`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design) directory serves as the central repository for technical design specifications and architectural decisions within the Fabric project. This directory organizes documents into categories such as [`.design/hosted`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/hosted) for distributed architecture, [`.design/kubernetes`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/kubernetes) for deployment and sandboxing, [`.design/metrics`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/metrics) for observability, and [`.design/_archive`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/_archive) for historical specifications. Top-level markdown files address core design aspects related to local architecture and CLI features, as documented in [`.design/README.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/README.md).

The design documents provide foundational blueprints for various system components. Key architectural principles include Fabric's Manager-Worker pattern, where [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) acts as a Grove Manager orchestrating agents (Grove Workers) within isolated containers. This isolation is crucial for managing concurrent agents and ensuring resource separation. Programmatic access to core agent logic is achieved by decoupling it from the CLI, introducing a clear separation between data types and business logic in [`pkg/api`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api) and business logic in [`pkg/agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent).

Agent state and lifecycle management are central to Fabric's design. The system includes a refactored agent state model that captures an agent's [`Phase`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L576), [`Activity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L577), and [`Detail`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/state/state.go#L225), providing a more granular view of its operational status, as detailed in [`.design/agent-state-refactor.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agent-state-refactor.md). Mechanisms are also in place to address agent resume functionality, crash handling, and auto-suspension, particularly within Docker runtimes, described in [`.design/agent-state-lifecycle-fixes.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agent-state-lifecycle-fixes.md). To manage resource consumption, agents can be configured with execution limits such as [`max_turns`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/shared/types.ts#L328) and [`max_duration`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/shared/types.ts#L330), enforced by [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44), which are documented in [`.design/agent-limits.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agent-limits.md). The design also specifies how agent configurations are assembled from various sources during provisioning and runtime launch, analyzed in [`.design/agent-config-flow.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agent-config-flow.md).

LLM agnosticism is achieved through a [`Harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L23) abstraction, which encapsulates agent-specific logic for environment variables, command construction, and authentication. This design allows Fabric to integrate with various Language Model providers without requiring significant changes to the core platform. The template system has evolved to be harness-agnostic, defining an agent's role independently of the underlying LLM, as discussed in [`.design/agnostic-template-design.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agnostic-template-design.md).

Authentication and security are critical components of the design. A robust system propagates authentication credentials from the host to containerized agents, employing a multi-stage credential resolution pipeline. This pipeline resolves LLM credentials across different harness types and deployment modes, primarily using [`pkg/harness/auth.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness/auth.go) and data structures from [`pkg/api/types.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go), as detailed in [`.design/agent-credentials.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agent-credentials.md). The design also addresses secure secret access for sub-agents by introducing [`AllowProgeny`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L1084) metadata and integrating ancestry information into agent tokens, leveraging the policy engine for access control, as outlined in [`.design/agent-progeny-secret-access.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agent-progeny-secret-access.md). A phased plan to implement fine-grained access visibility for resources within the Hub is discussed in [`.design/access-visibility.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/access-visibility.md).

Fabric supports various runtime environments, including integration with Apple's native [`container`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/web/src/graph.ts#L32) CLI for macOS-native virtualization and [`tmux`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L74)-based solutions for persistent [`fabric attach`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1) functionality, as proposed in [`.design/_archive/tmux.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/_archive/tmux.md). The system also supports mounting non-Git workspaces into agent containers, as suggested in [`.design/_archive/non-git-workspace-mount.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/_archive/non-git-workspace-mount.md).

The [`fabric-a2a-bridge`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/README.md?plain=1#L1) is designed to enable external A2A agents to interact with Fabric agents. This bridge translates between the A2A protocol and Fabric's Hub API, dynamically generating agent card metadata, managing task lifecycles, and facilitating message translation. It supports real-time updates through Server-Sent Events (SSE) and push notifications. The evolution of this bridge includes migrating to the official [`a2a-go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/go.mod#L8) SDK for improved specification compliance and maintainability. For more details on the A2A bridge, refer to [A2A Bridge Design and Evolution](#design-specifications-and-architecture-a2a-bridge-design-and-evolution).

The design documents also cover developer experience aspects such as a Python-based hook processor for providing status visibility and detailed logging, described in [`.design/_archive/hooks.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/_archive/hooks.md), and a standalone visualizer tool for replaying agent activity from Google Cloud Logging exports, proposed in [`.design/agent-visualizer.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agent-visualizer.md). Additionally, the [`.design`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design) directory contains documents addressing technical debt, control plane design, and documentation migration strategies.

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture-core-architectural-principles-and-agent-management"></a>

### Core Architectural Principles and Agent Management

![Diagram 62](diagrams/diagram-062.svg)

Fabric operates on a Manager-Worker pattern, where the Fabric platform acts as the "Grove Manager," orchestrating various "Agent Workers" within isolated environments known as Groves. A Grove typically corresponds to a Git repository or a project workspace, and agents within a Grove can be configured to collaborate on tasks. Agent lifecycle management involves commands such as starting, listing, attaching to, and stopping these agents. Resource isolation is achieved by running agents in dedicated containers, each with its own filesystem, network, and [`git worktree`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102)-based workspaces, enabling concurrent code modifications.

Programmatic access to Fabric's core agent logic is provided through an API, which decouples the core functionality from the command-line interface. This API defines fundamental types for agent information, status events, and start options, while a dedicated [`Manager`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/manager.go#L33) interface handles the business logic for agent operations.

The platform employs a refined agent state model that tracks [`Phase`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L576), [`Activity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L577), and [`Detail`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/state/state.go#L225) dimensions, replacing a more fragmented system. This model helps in accurately representing an agent's current operational status, addressing issues related to resume functionality, crash handling, and automatic suspension. Agents can also have configurable execution limits, such as maximum turns or duration, which are enforced to prevent runaway processes and manage resource consumption. Support for sidecar processes, referred to as "services," is also integrated, allowing agents to launch and manage auxiliary functionalities alongside their primary tasks.

The agent's configuration flow involves a merging process where configurations are assembled during agent creation and at runtime launch. This ensures that agents are provisioned with the necessary settings and environmental variables to operate correctly. Resource specifications, including CPU, memory, and disk requirements, can be defined within the agent's configuration, catering to various runtime environments like Apple Container, Docker, and Kubernetes.

The overall architecture for the hosted mode further elaborates on this distributed nature, emphasizing Grove-centric operations, authentication, and authorization systems. Client-side interactions with the Hub and Runtime Broker APIs are designed to facilitate real-time updates and agent detail views in the frontend. For a detailed understanding of the overall architecture and historical context, refer to the [Design Specifications and Architecture](#design-specifications-and-architecture) section. Specific aspects of agent lifecycle management are also covered in [Agent Lifecycle Management and Orchestration](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-agent-lifecycle-management-and-orchestration).

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture-llm-agnosticism-and-harness-abstraction"></a>

### LLM Agnosticism and Harness Abstraction

![Diagram 63](diagrams/diagram-063.svg)

Achieving agnosticism to large language models (LLMs) and other agent types is a core architectural principle in Fabric, enabled through the [`Harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L23) abstraction. This abstraction centralizes agent-specific logic, allowing the platform to support various agents without tight coupling to their internal mechanisms. The [`Harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L23) interface, defined in [`pkg/harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness), encapsulates functionalities such as setting environment variables, constructing commands for agent execution, and managing authentication flows specific to each agent type. For instance, while [`GeminiCLI`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/concepts.md?plain=1#L32) might be an existing implementation, the design accommodates other agents like [`ClaudeCode`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/claude/provision.py#L108).

This approach extends to the template system, which has evolved to become harness-agnostic. Instead of embedding specific LLM details within agent templates, the system defines an agent's role independently, combining it with a [`harness-config`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L22) during agent creation. This enables greater flexibility and reususability of templates across different LLM backends. An example of this flexibility is demonstrated by the design for a third-party [`Amp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/amp/README.md?plain=1#L1) coding agent, where its harness is entirely implemented via scripts using a [`container-script`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L32) provisioner type, as detailed in [`.design/amp-harness-scripts.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/amp-harness-scripts.md). This design pattern ensures that [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) can integrate diverse agents with minimal changes to its core orchestration logic.

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture-authentication-and-security-design"></a>

### Authentication and Security Design

![Diagram 64](diagrams/diagram-064.svg)

The Fabric platform manages authentication and authorization across the host system, containerized agents, and the Fabric Hub. A primary focus is the secure propagation and management of credentials from the host to containerized agents, ensuring their operation within isolated environments.

Authentication credentials for agents are processed through a multi-stage resolution pipeline. This pipeline is detailed in [`.design/agent-credentials.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agent-credentials.md) and involves gathering authentication information, overlaying settings, resolving final credentials, and validating them. The process primarily uses the Go package [`pkg/harness/auth.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness/auth.go), which defines the logic for handling various authentication types and integrates with data structures from [`pkg/api/types.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go). For instance, in the context of large language models, the system discovers and injects credentials, such as API keys and application credentials, into the agent's runtime environment. This injection can occur via environment variables or by mirroring filesystem paths from the host. This ensures agents have the necessary permissions to interact with external services while remaining within their isolated containers. The documents [`.design/_archive/auth.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/_archive/auth.md) and [`.design/agent-auth-refactor.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agent-auth-refactor.md) further elaborate on the consistent implementation and validation of this system.

For secure secret access within agent hierarchies, particularly for sub-agents, a mechanism exists to manage user-scoped secrets. This involves associating [`AllowProgeny`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L1084) metadata with secrets and integrating ancestry information into agent tokens. This approach enables the policy engine to enforce access control, ensuring that only authorized sub-agents can access specific secrets. The design for this capability is outlined in [`.design/agent-progeny-secret-access.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/agent-progeny-secret-access.md).

The Fabric Hub employs a phased strategy for access visibility for resources, as documented in [`.design/access-visibility.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/access-visibility.md). This plan aims to evolve access control from simple metadata to a core mechanism with defined levels such as [`private`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/githubapp/githubapp.go#L495), [`team`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L21), and [`public`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L342). This granular control helps ensure that resources within the Hub are appropriately secured and accessible only to authorized users or teams.

Within the hosted mode, the authentication and authorization systems are further refined. The [`.design/hosted/auth`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/hosted/auth) directory details the use of Unified Identity and Secure Token Management, adhering to OAuth 2.0 standards. This includes defining user and agent identities, managing various token types (access, refresh, CLI, JWT), and implementing client-specific authentication mechanisms (OAuth for web/CLI, JWT for agents, API keys for direct API access). Server-side authentication uses [`authMiddleware`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/server.go#L289) for token validation, and the CLI implements a browser-based OAuth flow with PKCE for secure credential acquisition. Agents utilize Hub-generated JWTs for authentication, with scopes for authorization, while runtime brokers use HMAC-based mutual authentication with the Hub. The permissions design introduces [`principal`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/handlers_principals.go#L38) and [`Group`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L1129) models, defining [`Principals`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/hub-admin/permissions.md?plain=1#L12), [`Resources`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L319), [`Actions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L1207), and [`Policies`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/handlers_policies.go#L33) to enforce authorization via an `AuthzMiddleware`. The design also supports agent-to-agent interaction with defined scopes like [`ScopeAgentCreate`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/agenttoken.go#L51) and [`ScopeAgentLifecycle`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/agenttoken.go#L53), configured via an `hub_access` field in agent templates. This capability allows agents to create and manage other agents within their grove with appropriate permissions.

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture-runtime-environments-and-integration"></a>

### Runtime Environments and Integration

![Diagram 65](diagrams/diagram-065.svg)

The design of the Fabric platform incorporates various runtime environments to execute agents. One notable integration is with Apple's native [`container`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/web/src/graph.ts#L32) CLI, detailed in [`.design/_archive/apple-container.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/_archive/apple-container.md). This allows Fabric agents to leverage macOS-native virtualization, providing a lightweight and secure execution environment on Apple hardware. The design addresses configuration, runtime adaptations for [`container`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/web/src/graph.ts#L32)-specific flags, mount constraints, and network considerations unique to this environment.

To enhance the user experience, particularly for [`fabric attach`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1) functionality, [`tmux`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L74) integration is proposed in [`.design/_archive/apple-container-attach.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/_archive/apple-container-attach.md) and [`.design/_archive/tmux.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/_archive/tmux.md). This solution allows for persistent interactive sessions with agents, even when the underlying [`container`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/web/src/graph.ts#L32) CLI might not natively support such persistence. By installing [`tmux`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L74) within the agent image and modifying the agent's entrypoint, users can attach to and detach from agent sessions without losing context. This includes adapting the [`Run`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/wsclient/pty.go#L156) and [`Attach`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/mock.go#L83) commands in the CLI to interact with [`tmux`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L74) sessions.

Beyond Git-based workspaces, the platform also envisions supporting non-Git workspaces. The document [`.design/_archive/non-git-workspace-mount.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/_archive/non-git-workspace-mount.md) proposes mounting project roots directly into agent containers at a designated [`/workspace`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L39) path. This feature would involve updating the [`ProvisionAgent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/provision.go#L400) function to handle [`VolumeMount`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L248) entries in the agent's configuration, allowing agents to operate on arbitrary filesystem directories provided by the user.

For further details on how Fabric handles the deployment and management of its core components, refer to [Google Cloud Run Deployment and Management](#developer-utilities-and-local-development-google-cloud-run-deployment-and-management) and [Google Cloud Engine Starter Hub Deployment](#developer-utilities-and-local-development-google-cloud-engine-starter-hub-deployment).

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture-a2a-bridge-design-and-evolution"></a>

### A2A Bridge Design and Evolution

![Diagram 66](diagrams/diagram-066.svg)

The [`fabric-a2a-bridge`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/README.md?plain=1#L1) is designed to enable external A2A agents to interact with Fabric agents. This bridge acts as a translator, converting requests between the A2A protocol and Fabric's internal Hub API. Its architecture features a self-managed broker plugin and an HTTP frontend for communication.

A core function of the bridge is dynamic agent card generation, which creates JSON metadata for Fabric agents based on their templates and current runtime state. This metadata is then served to A2A clients, allowing them to discover and understand the capabilities of available Fabric agents.

The bridge manages the lifecycle of A2A tasks by translating them into Fabric agent messages. It tracks task states such as [`submitted`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/LICENSE#L51), [`working`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L175), [`completed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/resource_import.go#L97), [`failed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/agents.go#L154), and [`input-required`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/README.md?plain=1#L275), persisting this state in an SQLite database. This ensures that the interaction flow between A2A clients and Fabric agents is consistent and reliable. The design also addresses the issue of premature task completion in multi-turn interactions, ensuring that tasks remain active as long as the Fabric agent is processing or awaiting input, rather than marking them as complete after the first message. This is achieved by allowing content messages to be broadcast as [`StatusUpdate`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/fabrictool/hub/client.go#L134) events without altering the task's state or closing subscriptions, as detailed in [`.design/a2a-multi-turn-lifecycle.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/a2a-multi-turn-lifecycle.md).

For message exchange, the bridge translates [`a2a.Message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/translate.go#L230) objects into Fabric [`StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L33) and vice versa. This translation includes handling various content types, such as text, URLs (as attachments), structured data, and raw binary. Real-time updates are supported through Server-Sent Events (SSE), allowing the bridge to fan out broker messages to active streams for [`SendStreamingMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/stream.go#L175) and [`SubscribeToTask`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/stream.go#L271) functionalities. Push notifications are also supported, dispatching A2A task updates to configured webhooks for disconnected clients.

Authentication is a critical component, covering external A2A client authentication (API Key, JWT Bearer, OAuth2) and internal authentication to the Fabric Hub with user impersonation capabilities. The bridge also maps A2A [`contextId`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/state/state.go#L39)s to specific Fabric agent instances, supporting multi-turn conversations and offering configurable agent auto-provisioning.

An important evolution of the [`fabric-a2a-bridge`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/README.md?plain=1#L1) involves migrating from a custom A2A protocol implementation to the official [`a2a-go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/go.mod#L8) SDK, as described in [`.design/a2a-sdk-migration.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/a2a-sdk-migration.md). This migration aims to improve A2A spec compliance, reduce maintenance overhead by replacing custom JSON-RPC, task lifecycle, and streaming implementations with SDK equivalents, and gain multi-transport capabilities. The new architecture introduces a [`FabricExecutor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/executor.go#L57) that implements [`a2asrv.AgentExecutor`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-a2a-bridge/internal/bridge/executor.go#L51) to translate SDK messages to Fabric [`StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L33)s, send them to the Hub, and yield SDK events. While core Hub routing, the broker plugin, agent lookup, context resolution, and auto-provisioning are preserved, the SDK handles JSON-RPC processing, task lifecycle, and streaming, relying on the [`SQLite`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L59) store for context mapping and broker correlation. The migration strategy focuses on gradually adopting the SDK's components while maintaining existing functionalities.

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture-hosted-mode-architecture-and-client-side-interaction"></a>

### Hosted Mode Architecture and Client-Side Interaction

![Diagram 67](diagrams/diagram-067.svg)

Fabric's hosted mode provides a distributed architecture for managing agents, focusing on grove-centricity, location transparency, and robust security. The architecture emphasizes the Hub as a centralized authority and the Runtime Broker for handling agent lifecycles, with [`fabrictool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/glossary.md?plain=1#L44) within agents reporting heartbeats and observability data. Grove-centricity implies that Git remote URLs serve as the primary identity for groves, supporting Hub-first creation and agent workspace provisioning. Location transparency is achieved through the Hub API, allowing communication without needing to know the physical location of agents or brokers. NAT traversal is a key feature for Runtime Brokers to connect to the Hub, and direct-to-storage synchronization facilitates handling large data. Multi-context security ensures that agents operate within secure boundaries.

Central to the system is a comprehensive authentication and authorization framework. This includes Unified Identity, Secure Token Management, and OAuth 2.0-compliant developer experience. User, agent, and runtime broker authentication are supported, with distinct token types and mechanisms. For instance, CLI authentication uses a browser-based OAuth flow with a [`LocalhostAuthServer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/auth/localhost_server.go#L129) and [`PKCE`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/handlers_auth.go#L63), storing credentials locally in [`~/.fabric/credentials.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/reference/security.md?plain=1#L17). Agents authenticate using Hub-generated JSON Web Tokens (JWTs) passed via the [`FABRIC_HUB_TOKEN`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L494) environment variable, with scopes like [`agent:status:update`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/agenttoken.go#L45) for authorization. Runtime brokers utilize HMAC-based mutual authentication with the Hub. The system enforces policy-based authorization using [`principal`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/handlers_principals.go#L38) and [`Group`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L1129) models, defining Principals (Users, Groups), Resources (hub, grove, agent), Actions (CRUD), and Policies. Middleware enforces authorization via the [`CheckAccess`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/authz.go#L94) method. This framework also enables a "lead agent" to create and manage "sub-agents" within its grove using new scopes like [`ScopeAgentCreate`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/agenttoken.go#L51) and [`ScopeAgentLifecycle`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/agenttoken.go#L53), configured via an `hub_access` field in agent templates. This allows for autonomous multi-agent workflows while maintaining strict grove isolation, where agents can only operate on resources within their designated [`grove_id`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L176). The design for access control for environment variables and secrets further refines authorization by leveraging existing [`CheckAccess`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/authz.go#L94) to ensure scope-based authorization, identity enforcement, and policy-based access for user, grove, and broker scopes, without introducing new resource types for simplicity. See [Authentication and Security Design](#design-specifications-and-architecture-authentication-and-security-design) for more details.

Client-side interaction with the Fabric Hub and Runtime Broker APIs is facilitated by Go client libraries. A shared client infrastructure in [`pkg/apiclient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/apiclient) provides a [`Transport`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/apiclient/transport.go#L31) layer for HTTP requests, an [`Authenticator`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/apiclient/auth.go#L20) interface for credentials, and structured error handling. The Hub API client in [`pkg/hubclient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient) exposes services for managing agents, groves, runtime brokers, templates, users, environment variables, secrets, and authentication. Similarly, a Runtime Broker API client in [`pkg/brokerclient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/brokerclient) manages agent operations, information retrieval, and health checks on a Runtime Broker, including WebSocket-based PTY connections for interactive sessions. The Fabric Hub's REST API and WebSocket interfaces define conventions and data models for various entities, supporting both standard CRUD operations and real-time interactions via WebSocket endpoints for agent PTY, status streams, and events. Enhancements to the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI completion allow merging local scans with Hub API calls for agent name suggestions, using a fast-path client with timeouts and caching. Furthermore, the [`fabric message`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1) CLI command integrates with the Hub for consistent message routing, supporting single-agent, broadcast, and all-agents messaging. For more details on API interactions, refer to [Fabric Hub API Client and Services](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-fabric-hub-api-client-and-services) and [Runtime Broker API Client and Agent Interaction](#fabric-agent-orchestration-and-management-runtime-broker-api-client-and-agent-interaction).

The frontend development focuses on a single-page application (SPA) that serves as the primary user interface. Key milestones include a Koa server foundation, Lit SSR integration, a web component library, and robust authentication flows. The frontend interacts with the Hub API via a proxy and features dedicated pages for managing groves and agents. Real-time updates are driven by Server-Sent Events (SSE) and a NATS server infrastructure, enabling client-side state management. The agent detail page, for example, is redesigned to present a clear Header with actions and two tabs ([`Status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L2629) and [`Configuration`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/apple_container.go#L178)) to differentiate between dynamic runtime state and static creation-time settings. The [`Status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L2629) tab displays real-time information such as [`Phase`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L576), [`Activity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L577), [`Tool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L253), [`Detail`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/state/state.go#L225), [`Current Task`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L476), [`Limits & Usage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/init.go#L48), [`Connectivity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/fabrictool/commands/doctor.go#L59), and [`Notifications`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/client.go#L73), with many elements updated via SSE. The [`Configuration`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/apple_container.go#L178) tab shows static settings like [`Identity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/identity.go#L25), [`Harness & Model`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L438), [`Runtime Environment`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102), [`Limits`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L338), and [`Initial Task`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L470). This separation improves user clarity and experience. The frontend also incorporates a terminal component for interactive sessions. Although the web dashboard, built with Node.js Koa and Lit SSR, is currently distinct from the main [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) Go binary, plans exist to embed built frontend assets using [`//go:embed`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L80) and to implement an [`EventBus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/eventbus.go#L40) interface for seamless integration in both local and clustered environments. More information about the web UI can be found in [Fabric Web User Interface](#fabric-web-user-interface).

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture-kubernetes-integration-and-sandbox-evolution"></a>

### Kubernetes Integration and Sandbox Evolution

![Diagram 68](diagrams/diagram-068.svg)

The Fabric platform integrates with Kubernetes to provide a scalable, isolated, and manageable runtime environment for [`fabric-agent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/common.go#L525) instances. This integration allows agents to run as Kubernetes Pods, leveraging the cluster's resource management and orchestration capabilities while maintaining a developer experience consistent with local Docker environments.

The design for Kubernetes integration has evolved, moving from direct Pod management towards a more abstracted approach using custom resources. Initially, the system directly managed Kubernetes Pods, enabling immediate support for custom images, environment variables, and command propagation without relying on external Custom Resource Definitions (CRDs). This allowed the [`KubernetesRuntime`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/k8s_runtime.go#L49) to directly create and manage [`corev1.Pod`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/k8s_runtime.go#L429) objects.

A significant architectural shift involves the adoption of the [`agent-sandbox`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/temp-cluster-walkthrough.md?plain=1#L3) standard, which utilizes [`SandboxClaim`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/k8s/api/v1alpha1/types.go#L153) and [`SandboxTemplate`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/k8s/api/v1alpha1/types.go#L122) custom resources for agent management. This approach provides improved isolation, lifecycle management, and policy enforcement across a fleet of agents, decoupling the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI from low-level Pod details. The CLI interacts with high-level [`SandboxClaim`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/k8s/api/v1alpha1/types.go#L153) objects, and a [`Sandbox Controller`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/temp-cluster-walkthrough.md?plain=1#L20) reconciles these claims to create the actual [`Sandbox`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/k8s/api/v1alpha1/types.go#L89) CRs, which in turn provision the agent Pods and Services.

Context synchronization is a critical aspect of this integration, bridging local development environments with remote Kubernetes Pods. This is achieved through a "snapshot" mechanism where the local project directory is archived ([`tar`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/templates.go#L305)) and streamed to the Pod's [`/workspace`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L39) directory upon startup. For interactive development, [`fabric sync <agent-name>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/sync.go#L92) provides explicit bidirectional file transfer, with [`Mutagen`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-08-changelog.md?plain=1#L6)-based live synchronization enabling real-time updates between local and remote environments.

SCM integration, specifically for Git repositories, addresses the challenge of providing source code to remote Pods where local Git worktrees are impractical. The design incorporates an [`Init Container`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L44) that performs a [`git clone`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L1) into an [`emptyDir`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/template_bootstrap_test.go#L891) volume within the Pod before the main agent container starts. This process handles repository URL resolution and various authentication strategies, including GitHub Apps, Personal Access Tokens, and GCP Secret Manager.

The integration has followed a phased roadmap towards production hardening, focusing on feature parity, correctness, and operational maturity. This includes enhancements in configuration handling, authentication and environment variable propagation, and robust error handling. Future considerations for production readiness include refined secret management, status reconciliation, automatic cleanup of Kubernetes resources, and the application of [`SecurityContext`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/k8s_runtime.go#L1216) settings and resource requests/limits for enhanced security and resource optimization.

Project-specific Kubernetes settings, such as [`context`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L315), [`namespace`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L200), [`runtimeClassName`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L317), and resource allocations, can be defined in a [`kubernetes-config.json`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/paths.go#L204) file. This allows for flexible configuration tailored to specific projects, leveraging the user's standard KubeConfig for authentication within the cluster.

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture-opentelemetry-otel-design-for-observability"></a>

### OpenTelemetry (OTel) Design for Observability

![Diagram 69](diagrams/diagram-069.svg)

OpenTelemetry (OTel) within the Fabric project provides a standardized approach to collecting and managing metrics, logs, and trace data across various Large Language Model (LLM) agents. This standardization supports consistent monitoring and analytics for different agent implementations, such as Claude Code, Codex, Gemini CLI, and OpenCode. The foundational designs for this observability architecture are detailed in [`.design/metrics`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/metrics).

A core principle of the OTel design involves organizing data into a logical hierarchy: Session, Turn, and Event, as described in [`.design/metrics/metrics-data-findings.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/metrics/metrics-data-findings.md). A Session represents a long-lived interaction, such as a CLI execution or a persistent chat thread. A Turn encompasses a single round-trip, including user input, LLM processing, tool execution, and the final response. An Event captures discrete occurrences within a turn, like tool calls, API errors, or token count updates. This hierarchy accommodates both OTel-native instrumentation and JSON-log-based systems.

All OTel data is enriched with normalized metadata, referred to as Resource Attributes, to facilitate data slicing and analysis. These attributes include [`service.name`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/schemas/settings-v1.schema.json#L889) (identifying the service), [`session.id`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/run.py#L74) (a unique UUID for the conversation), [`user.id`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L1387) (an anonymized user identifier), [`project.id`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L1288) (a hash or name of the repository/workspace), and [`version`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L2630) (the agent software version).

Normalized metrics, adhering to OpenTelemetry semantic conventions for Generative AI, are captured to provide insights into usage, cost, performance, and reliability. These include counters for input, output, and cached tokens ([`gen_ai.tokens.input`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/metrics_dashboard.go#L207), [`gen_ai.tokens.output`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/metrics_dashboard.go#L211), [`gen_ai.tokens.cached`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/fabrictool/hooks/handlers/telemetry.go#L126)). Performance and latency are measured with `gen_ai.latency.ttft` (Time to First Token) and `gen_ai.latency.total` (Total duration), while reliability is tracked by `gen_ai.error.count` for API failures.

Normalized logs, structured for debugging and auditing, capture specific events throughout an agent's operation. Examples include [`agent.session.start`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/fabrictool/hooks/handlers/telemetry.go#L28) (emitted on chat initiation), [`agent.user.prompt`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/codex/provision.py#L193) (user input, with content redacted), [`agent.tool.call`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/scripts/inspect_logs.py#L100) (details of tool invocation), and [`agent.tool.output`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/templates_test.go#L1360) (results of tool execution). The Claude Code OTel design, outlined in [`.design/metrics/claude-otel.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/metrics/claude-otel.md), specifies log events such as [`agent.user.prompt`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/codex/provision.py#L193), [`agent.tool.call`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/scripts/inspect_logs.py#L100), and [`gen_ai.api.request`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/fabrictool/hooks/handlers/telemetry.go#L33). Similarly, the Codex OTel documentation in [`.design/metrics/codex-otel.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/metrics/codex-otel.md) details events like `codex.sse_event` (reporting events from the AI stream) and `codex.user_prompt`.

Configuration options are available for filtering, sampling, and forwarding this data to various telemetry backends. For instance, the Codex advanced configuration described in [`.design/metrics/codex-config.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/metrics/codex-config.md) enables OpenTelemetry log export and metrics, allowing control over the exporter type and event recording. The Gemini CLI utilizes a custom OTel forwarder, detailed in [`.design/metrics/gemini-custom-otel-forwarder.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/metrics/gemini-custom-otel-forwarder.md), which acts as a middleware to filter and transform observability data. This forwarder ensures that [`session.id`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/examples/adk_fabric_agent/run.py#L74) is preserved for correlation. PII masking is a critical aspect, with a mandate for collectors or forwarders to redact or hash sensitive information like user prompts unless explicitly opted in, as highlighted in [`.design/metrics/metrics-data-findings.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/metrics/metrics-data-findings.md).

For the Gemini CLI, the core logic for extracting and aggregating usage metrics from session data is explained in [`.design/metrics/gcli-session-core-logic.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/metrics/gcli-session-core-logic.md). This involves discovering session data files, merging and deduplicating entries, and calculating various statistics such as total sessions, message counts, token usage, model usage, and estimating costs.

The OpenCode ecosystem also catalogs its telemetry data, including LLM and agent telemetry (OpenTelemetry), infrastructure observability, CLI event streams (structured JSON), and internal business events. As described in [`.design/metrics/opencode-otel.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/metrics/opencode-otel.md), it leverages the Vercel AI SDK's experimental OpenTelemetry features and supports integration points like OTLP receivers, log tail consumers, and a plugin system for capturing and forwarding events.

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture-github-app-integration-and-security-management"></a>

### GitHub App Integration and Security Management

![Diagram 70](diagrams/diagram-070.svg)

The Fabric platform integrates with GitHub via a GitHub App to enable seamless interaction with repositories for tasks such as content management and pull request handling. This integration requires a structured setup, careful configuration, and robust procedures for credential rotation to ensure security and operational continuity.

The core of the integration involves registering a GitHub App and configuring it within a Fabric Hub instance, as documented in [`.design/docs/github-app-setup.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/docs/github-app-setup.md). This process includes defining the App's permissions (e.g., [`Contents`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L1894), [`Metadata`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/store.go#L217), [`Pull requests`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L659)) and subscribing to relevant events ([`Installation`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/githubapp/githubapp.go#L478), [`Installation repositories`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/githubapp/githubapp.go#L478)). A private key is generated for secure authentication, and a webhook secret is established to validate incoming events from GitHub. The Fabric Hub's configuration ([`settings.yaml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L58)) must be updated with the App's [`app_id`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/mutation.go#L10813), [`private_key_path`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/settings_v1.go#L301), and [`webhook_secret`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/settings_v1.go#L303). Once configured, the GitHub App is installed on a GitHub organization or user account, allowing the Hub to auto-match groves (groups of agents) by Git remote URL.

A critical aspect of maintaining security and operational continuity is the secure rotation of GitHub App credentials, detailed in [`.design/docs/github-app-rotation.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/docs/github-app-rotation.md). The rotation process for the private key is designed to be zero-downtime, leveraging GitHub's support for multiple active private keys. This allows for a graceful transition where a new key is generated, stored, and configured in the Fabric Hub, with verification before the old key is decommissioned. In contrast, webhook secret rotation involves a brief impact window, as GitHub does not support multiple active webhook secrets. The procedure requires updating the secret on GitHub and then immediately updating the Fabric Hub's configuration. To minimize disruption, it is recommended to perform this during low-activity periods and restart the Hub promptly.

Webhook troubleshooting is also a key consideration, especially if the Fabric Hub is not publicly reachable or if events are not being processed correctly. The documentation provides guidance on diagnosing issues, including checking Hub reachability, firewall rules, and the consistency of the webhook secret. If webhooks are not enabled, the Hub can rely on periodic health checks and token minting time checks to detect changes, with manual discovery options available.

<a id="design-specifications-and-architecture-investigations-and-post-mortems"></a>

### Investigations and Post-Mortems

![Diagram 71](diagrams/diagram-071.svg)

This section compiles analyses of critical system issues, offering insights into their root causes and proposed resolutions.
