A notable post-mortem details a metadata server 502 error, which surfaced as intermittent failures when fetching Google Cloud authentication tokens. Investigations revealed two primary contributing factors: CPU throttling affecting sidecar containers in applications and [`iptables`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L1286) rule interference.

The [`iptables`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L1286) issue specifically created a circular dependency. An [`iptables`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L1286) rule, implemented by [`setupIPTablesRedirect`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/fabrictool/metadata/iptables.go#L31) in [`pkg/fabrictool/metadata/iptables.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/fabrictool/metadata/iptables.go), redirected all outgoing traffic destined for the Google Cloud metadata server ([`169.254.169.254`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/fabrictool/hub/oidc.go#L224)) to a local [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) metadata sidecar. This interception, however, unintentionally captured the Hub's own Google Cloud SDK credential requests, leading to a loop where the Hub tried to reach the metadata server, was redirected to the sidecar, which then called back to the Hub, attempting to use credentials that were themselves stuck in the redirection loop. This problem was particularly insidious because it manifested only after cached Google Cloud access tokens expired, typically an hour after initial setup.

Another identified issue was a "thundering herd" problem in token caching. The metadata sidecar, specifically [`pkg/fabrictool/metadata/server.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/fabrictool/metadata/server.go), lacked a mechanism to consolidate multiple concurrent token refresh requests. When a cached token expired, numerous requests would independently attempt to fetch a new token, potentially overwhelming the Google Cloud IAM API despite existing rate limiters.

To address these issues, solutions included modifying the system to skip [`iptables`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L1286) metadata interception when operating in host network mode and implementing a singleflight mechanism within [`pkg/fabrictool/metadata/server.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/fabrictool/metadata/server.go) to ensure that concurrent token fetches coalesce into a single upstream call. The post-mortem also led to further code fixes, such as shortening sidecar timeouts, introducing a Hub-side token cache, and rectifying a goroutine leak in the rate limiter, as detailed in [`.design/post-mortems/2026-05-01-metadata-server-502.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.design/post-mortems/2026-05-01-metadata-server-502.md). These investigations highlight the importance of understanding network namespace sharing, robust error reporting, and carefully designed defense-in-depth mechanisms for system stability.

<a id="developer-utilities-and-local-development"></a>

## Developer Utilities and Local Development

| Script | Location | Purpose |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `setup.sh` | `hack/` | Sets up an isolated test environment, builds the `fabric` binary, and initializes a test grove. |
| `cleanup.sh` | `hack/` | Cleans up test artifacts, including stopping and removing agents and specific `.fabric` directories. |
| `smoke_test.sh` | `hack/` | Builds the `fabric` binary and runs basic functionality smoke tests (`--help`). |
| `test_auth.sh` / `test_oauth.sh` | `hack/` | Test authentication flows, including environment variables, `--no-auth` flag, and OAuth discovery. |
| `create-cluster.sh` | `hack/` | Creates a GKE Autopilot cluster and configures `kubectl` for interaction. |
| `version.sh` | `hack/` | Displays version information by extracting Git commit hash and build time for Go `ldflags`. |
| `merge-work.sh` | `hack/` | Merges an agent's branch onto main, with retries and rebase requests upon divergence. |
| `pr-deps.sh` | `scripts/` | Analyzes open PRs for dependency graphs, topological merge order, and file overlaps. |
| `hub-env-integration-test.sh` | `scripts/` | Tests CRUD operations for environment variables at user and grove scopes via Hub API. |
| `hub-secret-integration-test.sh` | `scripts/` | Tests CRUD operations for secrets at user and grove scopes, supporting various secret types. |
| `template-integration-test.sh` | `scripts/` | Comprehensive test suite for template management, including Hub API, upload/download flows, and runtime integration. |
| `dist.sh` | `hack/` | Builds and distributes the `fabric` CLI binary across platforms to a GCS bucket. |
| `install.sh` | `hack/` | End-user script to install the `fabric` CLI client from a GCS distribution bucket. |
| `gce-demo-*` scripts | `scripts/starter-hub/` | A suite of scripts for provisioning, deploying, and managing a Fabric Hub on a Google Compute Engine VM. |

The Fabric project provides a suite of developer utilities and scripts to streamline local development, testing, and infrastructure provisioning. These tools facilitate the setup of isolated environments, manage authentication flows, orchestrate Kubernetes clusters, and perform API-level integration and stress testing. They also include functionalities for code quality checks and the management of various project aspects like PR dependencies, templates, environment variables, secrets, and Cloud Run deployments.

The [`hack`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack) directory contains a collection of scripts and Go utilities that support development and operations rather than end-user tooling. Scripts like [`setup.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/setup.sh#L18) prepare an isolated test environment by building the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) CLI and initializing a [`grove`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L72), while [`cleanup.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/README.md?plain=1#L12) removes agents and configurations to ensure a clean state, particularly for testing. Authentication mechanisms are tested through [`test_auth.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/README.md?plain=1#L14) and [`test_oauth.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/README.md?plain=1#L14), which validate API key propagation and OAuth flows.

The [`hack/apitest`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/apitest) Go application is designed to validate the robustness and performance of Fabric hubs through API-level integration and stress testing, focusing on connection pooling, keepalive mechanisms, and multi-replica behavior under various load conditions. It performs phases like "Concurrent CRUD Storm" to simulate heavy load, "Cross-Replica Read-After-Write" to check replication consistency, "Concurrent Duplicate-ID Create" to test conflict resolution, and "Idle-then-Burst" to assess stale connection handling. Similarly, the [`hack/dbdiag`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/dbdiag) Go program diagnoses PostgreSQL database pool saturation by reporting CloudSQL connection and advisory lock usage. For local API integration testing, [`hack/minttoken`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/minttoken) provides a utility to mint long-lived user access-token JWTs.

Kubernetes integration is facilitated by scripts like [`create-cluster.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/README.md?plain=1#L17), which automates the creation of a GKE Autopilot cluster and configures [`kubectl`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/k8s-nfs/README.md?plain=1#L18). The [`hack/k8s-nfs`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/k8s-nfs) directory contains Kubernetes manifests specifically for testing NFS-based shared workspace coordination in GKE. Code quality is maintained by scripts such as [`check-project-compat-literals.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L74), which identifies and flags legacy "grove" terminology in Go source files, ensuring consistency with updated vocabulary.

The [`scripts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts) directory extends these capabilities with additional integration tests and developer utilities. For example, [`pr-deps.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/README.md?plain=1#L7) analyzes dependencies within GitHub pull requests, providing topological merge order and detecting file overlaps. Diagnostic tools like [`scripts/vm-pulse.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/vm-pulse.sh) offer a "pulse check" for virtual machines, gathering performance metrics. Integration tests like [`scripts/checktemplate-2.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/checktemplate-2.sh), [`scripts/hub-env-integration-test.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/hub-env-integration-test.sh), [`scripts/hub-secret-integration-test.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/hub-secret-integration-test.sh), and [`scripts/template-integration-test.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/template-integration-test.sh) validate template management, Hub environment variables, secret storage, and the hosted template system, respectively. For deployment, the [`scripts/cloudrun`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/cloudrun) subdirectory manages the deployment of a scalable Fabric Hub/Web service and co-located Runtime Broker on Google Cloud Run, leveraging Cloud SQL, GCS, and Secret Manager. The [`scripts/starter-hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub) subdirectory provides scripts for deploying and managing a Fabric Hub on Google Cloud Engine, encompassing initial provisioning, configuration, and certificate management.

<a id="developer-utilities-and-local-development-api-integration-and-stress-testing"></a>

### API Integration and Stress Testing

![Diagram 72](diagrams/diagram-072.svg)

The [`apitest`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/README.md?plain=1#L25) Go application, found in [`hack/apitest`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/apitest), is a tool for evaluating the performance and resilience of Fabric Hub deployments. It focuses on validating network behavior such as connection pooling, keepalive mechanisms, and data replication under various load conditions, particularly when two Fabric hubs share a common PostgreSQL database instance. The tool is designed to be deployed on a VM geographically proximate to the hubs to ensure testing accuracy reflective of internal network latencies.

The testing methodology employs four distinct phases:

- **Concurrent CRUD Storm**: This phase simulates high concurrency by performing create, read, and delete operations on projects across both hubs simultaneously. It quantifies latency, success rates, and instances of significant operational delays.
- **Cross-Replica Read-After-Write**: This phase assesses the speed and consistency of data replication. Projects are created on one hub, and immediate read attempts are made from the other, differentiating between instant, delayed, and missed data visibility.
- **Concurrent Duplicate-ID Create**: This phase tests the API's conflict resolution capabilities by attempting to create projects with identical explicit IDs across multiple workers and hubs concurrently. The expected outcome is a single successful creation and subsequent conflict errors for duplicate attempts.
- **Idle-then-Burst**: This phase investigates how the system handles stale network connections. It initializes connection pools, then introduces an idle period before executing a burst of requests to determine if connections are appropriately managed or if performance stalls occur.

The application leverages Go's concurrency primitives, such as goroutines and [`sync.WaitGroup`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/stop.go#L200), to simulate real-world, multi-user scenarios. Metrics are collected using [`atomic.AddInt64`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/apitest/main.go#L92) for thread-safe counting and [`sync.Mutex`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/stop.go#L199) for protecting latency data. Configuration, including hub URLs and authentication tokens, is managed through environment variables, enhancing the tool's adaptability. Project uniqueness in tests is ensured by [`uuid.NewString`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L697), and [`http.Client`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L2645) timeouts prevent indefinite hangs during network operations. Detailed error reporting, including HTTP status codes and response bodies, is provided for any API failures.

<a id="developer-utilities-and-local-development-postgresql-database-diagnostics"></a>

### PostgreSQL Database Diagnostics

The [`dbdiag`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/README.md?plain=1#L26) Go program, located in [`hack/dbdiag`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/dbdiag), provides diagnostic information for PostgreSQL databases, specifically focusing on connection pool usage and advisory locks within CloudSQL environments. This tool helps identify and troubleshoot potential database saturation issues by reporting critical metrics.

It connects to a PostgreSQL database using connection string details from the [`PG_DSN`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/dbdiag/main.go#L15) environment variable. The program then queries the database to retrieve the configured maximum connections and the number of currently active connections. It also offers a detailed breakdown of connection states, categorizing active connections by the application name and their current state. Furthermore, [`dbdiag`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/README.md?plain=1#L26) reports the count of advisory locks currently held within the database. The [`main.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs/design/broker-fanout.md?plain=1#L437) file orchestrates these queries and presents the gathered statistics.

<a id="developer-utilities-and-local-development-kubernetes-nfs-shared-workspace-testing"></a>

### Kubernetes NFS Shared Workspace Testing

![Diagram 73](diagrams/diagram-073.svg)

The [`hack/k8s-nfs`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/k8s-nfs) directory provides Kubernetes manifests for testing and validating Network File System (NFS)-based shared workspace coordination within Kubernetes environments, particularly Google Kubernetes Engine (GKE). These resources aid developers in testing how Fabric agents interact with shared storage.

The core of this testing setup is in configuring persistent storage. The manifest file [`hack/k8s-nfs/README.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/k8s-nfs/README.md) details how [`PersistentVolume`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/k8s-nfs/README.md?plain=1#L7) (PV) and [`PersistentVolumeClaim`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/k8s-nfs/README.md?plain=1#L7) (PVC) are defined to connect to a shared NFS storage server. This ensures that agents can access a consistent and shared filesystem.

To validate different aspects of shared workspace behavior, various test scenarios are provided. For example, one scenario, described in [`hack/k8s-nfs/README.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/k8s-nfs/README.md), involves a single pod mounting a PVC at a subpath. This pod provisions a Git workspace via an init container and verifies permissions and filesystem isolation, confirming an agent's ability to correctly set up its environment within a shared volume. More complex scenarios, also outlined in [`hack/k8s-nfs/README.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/k8s-nfs/README.md), involve two concurrent pods sharing the same PVC but utilizing distinct subpaths. These tests validate parallel provisioning and runtime isolation, which is critical for orchestrating multiple agents. Additionally, an advanced multi-container pod template, further detailed in [`hack/k8s-nfs/README.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/k8s-nfs/README.md), allows for verification of volume mounts, mount boundaries, and runtime execution behavior in intricate agent configurations. These tests collectively ensure the stability and proper functioning of Fabric agents when they interact with shared storage in a Kubernetes cluster.

<a id="developer-utilities-and-local-development-jwt-minting-for-local-api-testing"></a>

### JWT Minting for Local API Testing

![Diagram 74](diagrams/diagram-074.svg)

The [`minttoken`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/identity/identity.go#L68) utility, located in the directory [`hack/minttoken`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/minttoken), is a Go program designed for generating long-lived JSON Web Tokens (JWTs) specifically for local API integration testing. This tool enables developers to obtain valid access tokens without needing to go through a full authentication flow, facilitating testing of API endpoints that require user authentication.

The utility operates by connecting to a PostgreSQL database to retrieve an existing user. It prioritizes finding an 'admin' user for testing purposes; otherwise, it selects the oldest created user. Once a user is identified, [`minttoken`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/identity/identity.go#L68) uses a configured signing key to generate a JWT for that user. This token is designed to have a long validity period (e.g., 30 days when using [`hub.ClientTypeCLI`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/hack/minttoken/main.go#L54)), which is beneficial for continuous integration and development environments where frequent token refreshes would be cumbersome. The generated JWT is then outputted for use in API requests, while user details are logged to standard error. The [`minttoken`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fabric-chat-app/internal/identity/identity.go#L68) utility is strictly for testing and development, and it is not integrated into the production system.

<a id="developer-utilities-and-local-development-google-cloud-run-deployment-and-management"></a>

### Google Cloud Run Deployment and Management

![Diagram 75](diagrams/diagram-075.svg)

The Fabric project leverages Google Cloud Run for deploying a horizontally scalable Fabric Hub and Web service, along with a co-located stateless Runtime Broker. This setup integrates deeply with various Google Cloud services, including Cloud SQL for PostgreSQL for transactional data, Google Cloud Storage (GCS) for artifact storage, and Secret Manager for sensitive configuration data. To ensure secure access, the deployment utilizes Cloud Run's native Identity-Aware Proxy (IAP).

The deployment process is primarily orchestrated by the [`deploy.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/README.md?plain=1#L72) script located in [`scripts/cloudrun`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/cloudrun). This script automates a comprehensive set of tasks, from configuring Google Cloud IAM service accounts with appropriate roles to building and pushing the Fabric Hub container image to Artifact Registry. It manages sensitive information, such as database passwords and session secrets, by storing them securely in Secret Manager.

The [`deploy.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/README.md?plain=1#L72) script is designed to be idempotent, allowing it to be run multiple times without adverse effects. It dynamically renders a [`hub-settings-template.yaml`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/cloudrun/deploy.sh#L137) file, substituting placeholders with actual deployment values to configure the Hub service for production. It also handles the configuration of IAP for the deployed service, either using custom OAuth clients or Google-managed ones, and grants necessary permissions for secure access. A key design choice is the script's ability to discover the deployed service's public URL and update the application settings if it changes, ensuring continuous connectivity.

The core of the Fabric Hub Cloud Run container is defined by the [`Dockerfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L138) in [`scripts/cloudrun`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/cloudrun). This multi-stage Dockerfile builds the web frontend, compiles the Go binary with embedded web assets, and creates a minimal Debian-based runtime environment. The [`entrypoint.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/cloudrun/README.md?plain=1#L149) script, also in [`scripts/cloudrun`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/cloudrun), is executed when the container starts. It prepares the server environment by handling secret-mounted settings and then launches the [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) server in foreground, production, hub, runtime broker, and web-enabled modes. This ensures the container functions as a complete Fabric Hub and Runtime Broker instance, ready to manage agents and their operations. For further details on the conceptual architecture, refer to [Hosted Mode Architecture and Client-Side Interaction](#design-specifications-and-architecture-hosted-mode-architecture-and-client-side-interaction).

<a id="developer-utilities-and-local-development-google-cloud-engine-starter-hub-deployment"></a>

### Google Cloud Engine Starter Hub Deployment

![Diagram 76](diagrams/diagram-076.svg)

The process for deploying and managing a Fabric Hub on Google Cloud Engine (GCE) is outlined by a set of scripts located in the [`scripts/starter-hub`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub) directory. These scripts manage initial provisioning, configuration, environment setup, SSL certificate management, code deployment, and teardown, and support both Docker-based deployments and optional Google Kubernetes Engine (GKE) deployments.

The deployment relies on a central configuration script, [`scripts/starter-hub/hub-config.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/hub-config.sh), which defines variables like [`HUB_NAME`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/README.md?plain=1#L17) and [`BASE_DOMAIN`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/README.md?plain=1#L18), allowing for parameterized and repeatable deployments across different environments (e.g., staging, production). This script is sourced by all other scripts to ensure consistent settings.

The overall deployment is orchestrated by [`scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-deploy.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-deploy.sh), which executes a sequence of modular scripts. Before any resources are provisioned, [`scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-preflight.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-preflight.sh) performs comprehensive checks to validate the local development environment, [`gcloud`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/build.go#L170) authentication, environment file configuration, GCP APIs, IAM permissions, and DNS readiness. This preflight step consolidates warnings and errors to help streamline problem resolution.

Infrastructure provisioning, including the GCE virtual machine, associated service accounts, and firewall rules, is handled by [`scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-provision.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-provision.sh). This script can also optionally provision a GKE cluster using [`scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-cluster.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-cluster.sh) and a dedicated service account for telemetry data via [`scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-telemetry-sa.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-telemetry-sa.sh).

After the infrastructure is in place, [`scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-setup-repo.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/gce-demo-setup-repo.sh) prepares the GCE instance by setting up a dedicated [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) user and cloning or updating the Fabric Git repository. Certificate management is then handled by [`scripts/starter-hub/gce-certs.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/gce-certs.sh), which automates the setup of Cloud DNS and obtains Let's Encrypt wildcard certificates. Finally, [`scripts/starter-hub/gce-start-hub.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/starter-hub/gce-start-hub.sh) deploys and manages the Fabric Hub application, including building binaries, uploading configurations, and managing the [`systemd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L93) service and Caddy web server.

The scripts are designed to be largely idempotent, meaning they can be re-run without causing unintended side effects, and they emphasize modularity, allowing individual components of the deployment to be managed separately. For managing various Cloud Run deployments, see [Google Cloud Run Deployment and Management](#developer-utilities-and-local-development-google-cloud-run-deployment-and-management).

<a id="developer-utilities-and-local-development-pr-dependency-analysis-and-merge-ordering"></a>

### PR Dependency Analysis and Merge Ordering

![Diagram 77](diagrams/diagram-077.svg)

The [`pr-deps.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/README.md?plain=1#L7) script, located at [`scripts/pr-deps.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/pr-deps.sh), is a utility for analyzing dependencies within open GitHub pull requests. It provides functionalities for visualizing branch dependencies, determining a topological merge order, and detecting file overlaps to streamline development workflows.

The script identifies dependencies by performing ancestry checks between pull request branches using [`git`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L102) commands, fetching remote [`refs/pull/<number>/head`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/pr-deps.sh#L179) to analyze local ancestry. After identifying all ancestry-based dependencies, it applies a transitive reduction to simplify the dependency graph, retaining only direct dependencies.

To determine a valid merge order, the [`cmd_order`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/pr-deps.sh#L368) function within [`pr-deps.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/README.md?plain=1#L7) performs a topological sort on pull requests using [`jq`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/pr-deps.sh#L102). This process includes logic to detect and report cycles in the dependency graph, which can prevent a clear merge order.

For detecting file overlaps, the [`cmd_files`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/pr-deps.sh#L438) function fetches file lists for pull requests using the [`gh pr view`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/pr-deps.sh#L138) command and then utilizes [`jq`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/pr-deps.sh#L102) to identify and report any pairwise file overlaps. This helps prevent merge conflicts by highlighting potential areas of contention before merging.

The script offers options to visualize dependencies in Graphviz DOT format via [`cmd_graph_dot`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/pr-deps.sh#L349), which can aid in understanding complex relationships between pull requests. It leverages the GitHub CLI ([`gh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/create.go#L147)) for API interaction and [`jq`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/pr-deps.sh#L102) for efficient JSON data manipulation, allowing for robust processing of pull request information.

<a id="developer-utilities-and-local-development-vm-pulse-health-diagnostics"></a>

### VM Pulse Health Diagnostics

The [`scripts/vm-pulse.sh`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/vm-pulse.sh) script serves as a diagnostic tool designed to provide a "pulse check" of a virtual machine's health and performance. It gathers various metrics to identify potential bottlenecks or issues affecting system resources, scheduler behavior, Docker container performance, and I/O latency.

The script's functionality is organized into four main diagnostic areas. It first provides an overview of **System Resources**, reporting host memory usage and, if available, CPU and memory Pressure Stall Information (PSI) metrics. This is followed by an analysis of **Scheduler & Thread Density**, which includes virtual memory statistics and counts of threads for critical processes like [`dockerd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/vm-pulse.sh#L52) and [`containerd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/vm-pulse.sh#L52). For environments utilizing Docker, the script identifies **Docker Top Offenders** by listing containers with high CPU consumption and checks for kernel-level cgroup throttling. Finally, it assesses **I/O & Latency** by providing extended I/O statistics and reporting on context-switching tasks, distinguishing between voluntary and involuntary switches.

A key design choice for the script is its use of the [`check_tool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/scripts/vm-pulse.sh#L27) function, which verifies the availability of command-line utilities required for each diagnostic step. This ensures that the script can run gracefully, even if some tools are not installed, preventing errors and allowing partial execution. The script produces colorized output to enhance readability, using ANSI escape codes to emphasize headers and warnings.

<a id="issue-and-pull-request-management"></a>

## Issue and Pull Request Management

| Template Type | File Path | Purpose/Key Information Requested |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Pull Request | `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md` | Provides a checklist for PRs, ensuring tests pass and documentation is updated. |
| Bug Report | `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/bug_report.md` | Collects detailed information about bugs, including steps to reproduce, expected/actual behavior, debug output, and environment details. |
| Feature Request | `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/feature_request.md` | Solicits suggestions for new features or improvements, covering problem/motivation, proposed solution, and alternatives. |

The Fabric project utilizes GitHub issue and pull request templates to standardize contributions and streamline development workflows. These templates guide users through providing necessary information, ensuring issues are actionable and contributions align with project goals.

For bug reporting, a structured template, located at [`.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/bug_report.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/bug_report.md), prompts users to detail the problem, steps to reproduce, expected versus actual behavior, and environmental context. This includes crucial diagnostic information such as debug output and server logs, encouraging the use of the [`--debug`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L51) flag for comprehensive data. The template also requests specific details about the Fabric version, runtime environment (e.g., Docker), and agent harness (e.g., Claude) in use.

Similarly, feature requests use a dedicated template at [`.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/feature_request.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/feature_request.md). This template encourages contributors to articulate the problem or motivation for a new feature, propose solutions, and mention any alternatives considered. Issues created using this template are automatically labeled as [`enhancement`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L1316).

For code contributions, a pull request template, found at [`.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md), serves as a checklist and guide. It reminds contributors to link their pull requests to existing issues, verify that all tests pass, and consider documentation updates. The template also recommends opening an issue for discussion prior to coding changes, fostering collaboration and alignment on proposed modifications.

<a id="issue-and-pull-request-management-standardized-bug-reporting-process"></a>

### Standardized Bug Reporting Process

![Diagram 78](diagrams/diagram-078.svg)

The process for submitting bug reports in the Fabric project is standardized through the use of a dedicated template, located at [`.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/bug_report.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/bug_report.md). This template guides users in providing comprehensive diagnostic information, which is critical for efficient issue resolution.

When a bug is reported, the template prompts for several key pieces of information: a clear description of the bug, detailed steps to reproduce it, the expected behavior, and the actual behavior observed. To aid in debugging, users are specifically asked to include [`Debug Output`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L106) and [`Server logs`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/AGENTS.md?plain=1#L35) generated by re-running relevant [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) commands with the [`--debug`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go#L51) flag. These logs, often extensive, are encapsulated within expandable Markdown [`<details>`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtimebroker/nfs_mount.go#L241) tags to maintain readability of the issue.

Furthermore, the template requires environmental details, such as the [`Fabric version`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1) (obtained via the [`fabric version`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L1) command), the specific [`Runtime`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L583) environment (e.g., Docker, Apple Virtualization, Kubernetes), and the [`Harness`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness.go#L23) being used (e.g., Claude, Gemini). This structured approach ensures that developers receive all necessary context upfront, minimizing the back-and-forth required to gather information and accelerating the debugging process. The overarching issue management process is further detailed in [Issue and Pull Request Management](#issue-and-pull-request-management).

<a id="issue-and-pull-request-management-feature-request-submission-guidelines"></a>

### Feature Request Submission Guidelines

Feature requests for the Fabric project are submitted using a structured template to ensure clarity and provide necessary context for efficient evaluation and implementation. The template, found at [`.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/feature_request.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/feature_request.md), prompts contributors to articulate the problem or motivation behind the requested feature, propose a solution, list any alternatives considered, and provide additional relevant context. When this template is used, the system automatically labels the new issue as an [`enhancement`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L1316), streamlining the categorization of contributions. For broader context on how issues and pull requests are managed, see [Issue and Pull Request Management](#issue-and-pull-request-management).

<a id="issue-and-pull-request-management-pull-request-submission-and-checklist"></a>

### Pull Request Submission and Checklist

The Fabric project standardizes the pull request (PR) submission process through a dedicated template, defined in [`.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md). This template guides contributors to link their PRs to existing issues, ensuring traceability and providing necessary context for changes. It also includes a pre-submission checklist that prompts contributors to verify that tests pass and that documentation updates have been considered, promoting code quality and maintainability. Furthermore, the template encourages prior discussion of proposed changes by recommending that an issue be opened for discussion before coding begins. This approach helps align contributions with project goals and streamlines the review process. For detailed guidelines on bug reporting and feature requests, refer to [Standardized Bug Reporting Process](#issue-and-pull-request-management-standardized-bug-reporting-process) and [Feature Request Submission Guidelines](#issue-and-pull-request-management-feature-request-submission-guidelines).

<a id="fabric-broker-protobuf-and-grpc-services"></a>

## Fabric Broker Protobuf and gRPC Services

![Diagram 79](diagrams/diagram-079.svg)

The Fabric platform utilizes Protocol Buffers (Protobuf) and gRPC for inter-service communication within its broker component, defining the mechanisms for message exchange, configuration management, and health monitoring. This approach ensures strong typing, language independence, and efficient serialization for communication between various Fabric agents and services.

The core of this system is the [`BrokerService`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L23), defined in Protobuf and implemented as a gRPC service. This service facilitates several key operations:

- **Message Brokering**: Agents can publish messages, subscribe to topics, and unsubscribe from them. Messages are structured using [`StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L33), a comprehensive data structure that includes fields for versioning, timestamps, sender and recipient identification, message content, type, channel, and metadata, enabling robust inter-agent communication.
- **Configuration Management**: The service allows for dynamic configuration of the broker, enabling runtime adjustments to its behavior.
- **Health and Information Checks**: Clients can query the broker's operational status and retrieve general information about its capabilities and state, supporting system monitoring and diagnostics.

The [`BrokerService`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L23)'s definitions in Protobuf are used to generate Go client and server interfaces, located in [`proto/broker/v1`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1). The [`BrokerServiceClient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker_grpc.pb.go#L50) provides the client-side API for interacting with the broker, while the [`BrokerServiceServer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker_grpc.pb.go#L133) interface defines the contract for server implementations. The use of [`UnimplementedBrokerServiceServer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker_grpc.pb.go#L148) ensures forward compatibility, allowing new methods to be added to the service definition without breaking existing server implementations. This generated code is fundamental for integrating diverse components within the Fabric ecosystem, enabling seamless and reliable communication among agents.

<a id="fabric-broker-protobuf-and-grpc-services-message-brokering-rpcs-and-structuredmessage"></a>

### Message Brokering RPCs and `StructuredMessage`

![Diagram 80](diagrams/diagram-080.svg)

The Fabric message broker, defined by Protobuf and gRPC services in [`proto`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto), facilitates inter-agent communication within the Fabric ecosystem. This broker provides core functionalities for agents to [`Publish`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/config.go#L136) messages, [`Subscribe`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/events.go#L52) to message topics, and [`Unsubscribe`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/fanout.go#L274) from them.

The central data structure for these interactions is the [`StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L33), which encapsulates various fields to ensure robust and context-rich communication. These fields include [`Version`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L2630), [`Timestamp`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L839), [`Sender`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/events.go#L186), [`Recipient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/events.go#L188), [`Msg`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/events.go#L190) (the message content itself), [`Type`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L48), [`Channel`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L1556), and [`Metadata`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/store.go#L217) (a map for additional key-value data). Other important fields include [`Plain`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L2059) (for plain text messages), [`Raw`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/skill_uri.go#L30) (for raw data), [`Urgent`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/events.go#L192) (to indicate high priority), [`Broadcasted`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/events.go#L193) (for messages intended for all subscribers), [`ObserverOnly`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/messages/types.go#L104) (for messages only meant for monitoring), [`Status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L2629) (for status updates), [`Attachments`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/messages/types.go#L106) (for linked resources), [`ThreadId`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.pb.go#L59) (for conversational threading), and [`Visibility`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L597) (to control message audience).

The gRPC client-side interface, [`BrokerServiceClient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker_grpc.pb.go#L50), allows agents to interact with the broker by invoking RPCs like [`Publish`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/config.go#L136) (using a [`PublishRequest`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L62) containing a [`Topic`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/projectcompat/topics.go#L46) and a [`StructuredMessage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L33)), [`Subscribe`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/events.go#L52) (with a [`SubscribeRequest`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L69) specifying a [`Pattern`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/broker_plugin.go#L52) for topics), and [`Unsubscribe`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/eventbus/fanout.go#L274) (with an [`UnsubscribeRequest`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L75) and its associated [`Pattern`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/broker_plugin.go#L52)). For a more detailed look at the client-side and server-side implementations, refer to [Generated Go Client and Server Interfaces](#fabric-broker-protobuf-and-grpc-services-generated-go-client-and-server-interfaces).

<a id="fabric-broker-protobuf-and-grpc-services-broker-configuration-and-information-retrieval"></a>

### Broker Configuration and Information Retrieval

![Diagram 81](diagrams/diagram-081.svg)

The [`BrokerService`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L23) offers two primary mechanisms for interacting with the broker's operational parameters and metadata: [`Configure`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/config.go#L142) and [`GetInfo`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/config.go#L144).

The [`Configure`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/config.go#L142) RPC, defined with [`ConfigureRequest`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L56) and [`ConfigureResponse`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L60), allows dynamic adjustment of the broker's settings. Clients can send key-value pairs representing configuration parameters to modify the broker's behavior at runtime. This provides a way to adapt the broker's operation without requiring a restart, supporting flexible deployments and administrative adjustments.

Conversely, the [`GetInfo`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/config.go#L144) RPC (using [`GetInfoRequest`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L89) and [`GetInfoResponse`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L91)) enables clients to retrieve detailed operational information and metadata about the Fabric broker. This includes fundamental attributes like the broker's name, version, and the minimum compatible Fabric version. It also provides insight into the broker's [`ChannelId`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.pb.go#L700) and a list of its [`Capabilities`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L354), which can inform clients about the broker's feature set and operational limits. These RPCs are part of the core [`BrokerService`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L23) interface, with their definitions residing in [`proto/broker/v1/broker.pb.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.pb.go) and their gRPC client/server interfaces in [`proto/broker/v1/broker_grpc.pb.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker_grpc.pb.go). For more details on the messaging structures used in these RPCs, refer to [Message Brokering RPCs and `StructuredMessage`](#fabric-broker-protobuf-and-grpc-services-message-brokering-rpcs-and-structuredmessage).

<a id="fabric-broker-protobuf-and-grpc-services-health-check-mechanisms-and-status-reporting"></a>

### Health Check Mechanisms and Status Reporting

The [`BrokerService`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L23) provides a [`HealthCheck`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/plugin/config.go#L146) RPC, enabling clients to query the operational status of the Fabric message brokering service. This mechanism is critical for ensuring the reliability and availability of inter-agent communication within the Fabric ecosystem. By allowing clients to ascertain the broker's health, it facilitates proactive monitoring and rapid response to potential service disruptions. The [`HealthCheckRequest`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L81) and [`HealthCheckResponse`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L83) messages, defined in [`proto/broker/v1/broker.pb.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.pb.go), are used to initiate and respond to these health checks, respectively. This allows for straightforward integration into monitoring systems and ensures that agents and other Fabric components can confirm the broker's readiness to process messages.

<a id="fabric-broker-protobuf-and-grpc-services-generated-go-client-and-server-interfaces"></a>

### Generated Go Client and Server Interfaces

The Protobuf definitions within the [`proto`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto) directory generate Go code that facilitates client-side interaction with and server-side implementation of the [`BrokerService`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker.proto#L23). The [`BrokerServiceClient`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker_grpc.pb.go#L50) is the interface clients use to interact with the broker's functionalities, such as publishing and subscribing to messages, configuring the broker, and checking its health. On the server side, the [`BrokerServiceServer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker_grpc.pb.go#L133) interface defines the contract that any implementation must satisfy to provide these broker services. For integrating a server implementation with a gRPC runtime, the [`RegisterBrokerServiceServer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker_grpc.pb.go#L178) function is used, which binds the concrete [`BrokerServiceServer`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1/broker_grpc.pb.go#L133) implementation to the gRPC server. This generated code, located in [`proto/broker/v1`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/proto/broker/v1), ensures type safety and a structured approach to inter-service communication within the Fabric ecosystem.

<a id="task-management-and-onboarding"></a>

## Task Management and Onboarding

![Diagram 82](diagrams/diagram-082.svg)

The [`.tasks`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks) directory serves as a central repository for the development and maintenance of the workstation onboarding experience for the Fabric project. This includes detailed task breakdowns, records of bug fixes, and instructions for rebasing feature branches into the main codebase.

The onboarding process is structured into several development phases. Initial phases (as documented in [`.tasks/phase-0-1-foundations-identity.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-0-1-foundations-identity.md) and [`.tasks/phase-2-system-api.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-2-system-api.md)) focus on foundational server configurations, managing user identities, and establishing core system API endpoints. These APIs ([`/api/v1/system/check`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts#L687), [`/api/v1/system/runtime`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts#L757), [`/api/v1/system/status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts#L488), [`/api/v1/system/identity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L2760), [`/api/v1/system/init`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L2764)) provide diagnostics, runtime configuration, onboarding status, identity management, and machine initialization. Access to these endpoints is restricted to workstation environments and protected by authentication.

Subsequent phases, such as the one described in [`.tasks/phase-3-wizard-shell.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-3-wizard-shell.md), introduce the web-based onboarding wizard. This wizard guides users through steps like identity collection, system checks, runtime selection, and initial harness seeding. It is designed to be resumable and handles daemon launch behavior, including automatically opening the browser to the onboarding URL if the machine is not yet onboarded. Image pulling and local build options, detailed in [`.tasks/phase-4-images.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-4-images.md), provide users with mechanisms to acquire necessary container images, with real-time progress streamed via Server-Sent Events (SSE).

The "linked groves" functionality, outlined in [`.tasks/phase-5-linked-groves.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-5-linked-groves.md), enables users to designate local directories as Fabric projects. This involves server-side directory browsing with robust path safety checks to prevent unauthorized access or conflicts with Fabric's internal directories. This feature is integrated into both the project creation UI and the onboarding wizard.

Throughout these development phases, the [`.tasks`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.gcloudignore#L65) directory also captures efforts to address bugs and refine the user experience. For example, [`.tasks/onboarding-bugs-3-4-5.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/onboarding-bugs-3-4-5.md) details fixes for issues like the wizard skipping steps on fresh installs, incorrect display of image names, and the unavailability of local builds for Homebrew installations. Enhancements for phantom daemon processes and a forced stop mechanism for [`fabric server stop`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) are documented in [`.tasks/phantom-daemon-fix.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phantom-daemon-fix.md). Feedback from code reviews is systematically addressed, as shown in [`.tasks/pr-264-feedback.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/pr-264-feedback.md), [`.tasks/review-fixes-round-1.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/review-fixes-round-1.md), and [`.tasks/review-fixes-round-2.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/review-fixes-round-2.md), covering aspects like error handling, concurrency, and security vulnerabilities.

Finally, the project finalization and integration tasks, described in [`.tasks/phase-6-polish.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-6-polish.md) and [`.tasks/rebase-workstation-improvements.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/rebase-workstation-improvements.md), ensure the feature's correctness, usability, and documentation. This includes writing comprehensive tests, updating user-facing documentation, and providing instructions for rebasing the feature branch while resolving potential conflicts. An overall CI fixup strategy is also documented in [`.tasks/ci-full-fix.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/ci-full-fix.md), ensuring that all continuous integration checks pass before final integration.

<a id="task-management-and-onboarding-workstation-onboarding-feature-development-phases"></a>

### Workstation Onboarding Feature Development Phases

![Diagram 83](diagrams/diagram-083.svg)

The workstation onboarding experience is developed in phases, each addressing a distinct aspect of setting up a Fabric environment for local development.

The initial foundational phase ([`Phase 0`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/list.go#L3)) establishes core server configurations and identity management for the workstation, as outlined in [`.tasks/phase-0-1-foundations-identity.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-0-1-foundations-identity.md). This includes modifying the [`hub.ServerConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/hub_config.go#L282) by adding a [`Workstation bool`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/server.go#L28) field to delineate workstation-specific functionality and safeguarding access to certain API endpoints using a [`requireWorkstation`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L2852) middleware. It also enables the retrieval of an embedded broker ID via the [`GetEmbeddedBrokerID()`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L1389) accessor to support subsequent linked-grove creation processes. Identity management is enhanced by adding [`Username`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/devauth.go#L87), [`DisplayName`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/devauth.go#L93), and [`Email string`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L72) fields to [`DevAuthConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/hub_config.go#L188) (found in [`pkg/config/hub_config.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/hub_config.go)) and [`V1AuthConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/settings_v1.go#L421) (in [`pkg/config/settings_v1.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/settings_v1.go)), which are then used to construct [`DevUser`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/devauth.go#L40) (in [`pkg/hub/devauth.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/devauth.go)) and can be updated via a dedicated [`PUT /api/v1/system/identity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L237) endpoint. This phase also includes textual updates to standardize the terminology of "developer token" across the CLI (in [`cmd`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd)), UI (in `/pdlc-os/fabric/web/src/`), and documentation.

Building upon this foundation, [`Phase 2`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/list.go#L3) introduces a set of system API endpoints under [`/api/v1/system/`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L190) to facilitate the workstation onboarding wizard, as detailed in [`.tasks/phase-2-system-api.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-2-system-api.md). These endpoints act as thin wrappers around existing Go logic, exposing functionalities for diagnostics ([`GET /api/v1/system/check`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L146)), runtime configuration management ([`GET`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L903), [`PUT /api/v1/system/runtime`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L237)), overall onboarding status reporting ([`GET /api/v1/system/status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L146)), identity updates ([`PUT /api/v1/system/identity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L237)), and machine initialization ([`POST /api/v1/system/init`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L237)). All these endpoints are protected by the [`requireWorkstation`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L2852) middleware, ensuring they are only accessible in workstation environments, and by standard authentication mechanisms. The [`GatherDiagnostics`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go#L49) function, which extracts diagnostic logic and returns [`DiagnosticResult`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go#L38) structs, supports structured reporting of system health. Similarly, the [`OnboardingStatus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go#L295) struct provides a comprehensive view of the onboarding progress, and the [`InitMachine`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/init.go#L554) function, designed to be idempotent, handles the initial setup including the seeding of selected harness configurations. New routes are registered within the [`MountHubAPI`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L565) function in [`pkg/hub/web.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go), and handler implementations reside in [`pkg/hub/system_handlers.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go).

[`Phase 3`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/list.go#L131) focuses on the development of the web-based onboarding wizard itself, as described in [`.tasks/phase-3-wizard-shell.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-3-wizard-shell.md). Accessible via the [`/onboarding`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/server_daemon.go#L518) route (registered in [`web/src/client/main.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/main.ts)), this wizard guides users through a linear, step-by-step first-run setup process, covering identity collection, system checks, runtime selection, and harness installation. The wizard integrates with the API endpoints established in [`Phase 2`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/list.go#L3) to manage state and actions. For instance, it calls [`PUT /system/identity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L237) to save user details and [`GET /system/check`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L146) to validate system prerequisites. This phase also modifies the daemon launch behavior (in [`printWorkstationQuickstart`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/server_daemon.go#L519) within [`cmd/server_daemon.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/server_daemon.go)) to automatically direct users to the [`/onboarding`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/server_daemon.go#L518) URL if the workstation is not yet onboarded, and can auto-open the URL in a browser for a seamless initial experience. The [`fabric-page-onboarding`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts#L1454) Lit page implements the wizard's UI, managing steps and validating input.

In [`Phase 4`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/list.go#L131), image management capabilities are integrated into the onboarding process, as detailed in [`.tasks/phase-4-images.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-4-images.md). This includes Go-native image pulling with per-image progress updates delivered via Server-Sent Events (SSE), and the option for local image building, also with streaming log output. The wizard's "Images" step orchestrates these operations, using core logic for image operations. The [`PullImages`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/imagepull.go#L55) function manages the sequential pulling of images and communicates their status (e.g., "queued," "pulling," "done," "error") using [`PullResult`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/util/git.go#L643) structs. Both image pulling and local builds are initiated as background jobs, providing a [`jobId`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go#L556) to the client for real-time status tracking via SSE. The "Images" step is designed to be non-blocking, allowing users to skip image installation and proceed. The UI orchestration for these operations occurs within [`web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts).

Finally, [`Phase 5`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L206) introduces "Linked Groves" functionality, enabling users to link existing local directories as projects, primarily for workstation use, as outlined in [`.tasks/phase-5-linked-groves.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/phase-5-linked-groves.md). This involves new API endpoints in [`pkg/hub/system_handlers.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go) for safe filesystem interaction, including listing directory contents ([`GET /api/v1/system/fs/list`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L146)), creating new directories ([`POST /api/v1/system/fs/mkdir`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L237)), and validating paths ([`POST /api/v1/system/fs/validate-path`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L237)). These endpoints are strictly guarded by [`requireWorkstation`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L2852) and [`assertLoopback`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L2863) to ensure they are only accessible on local workstation environments. A [`PathClass`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/fs_safety.go#L40) struct and [`ClassifyPath`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/fs_safety.go#L52) function in [`pkg/hub/fs_safety.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/fs_safety.go) classify paths based on their existence, type, Git status, and whether they are Fabric-managed, with a "hard-fail" rule to prevent linking internal project structures. The [`fabric-dir-browser`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/shared/dir-browser.ts#L441) Lit element component is introduced for navigating the local filesystem within the UI, used in both the project creation flow ([`web/src/components/pages/project-create.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/project-create.ts)) and the onboarding wizard's workspace step ([`web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts)). The process for linking a local directory involves creating a hub-native project and then adding the local path as a provider, allowing for retry mechanisms. The [`EmbeddedBrokerID`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go#L303) is also included in the [`OnboardingStatus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go#L295) response to support this functionality.

<a id="task-management-and-onboarding-onboarding-bug-fixes-and-refinements"></a>

### Onboarding Bug Fixes and Refinements

![Diagram 84](diagrams/diagram-084.svg)

This section addresses several issues identified within the Fabric onboarding wizard and the underlying daemon process management. The fixes aim to improve user experience during initial setup and enhance system stability.

One area of refinement concerns the onboarding wizard's behavior on fresh installations. Initially, the wizard might skip steps due to logic designed to resume progress. This was resolved by introducing a flag, persisted in [`sessionStorage`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/main.ts#L244), to differentiate between a new user experience and a returning one. This ensures that new users consistently start from the first step, providing a guided onboarding journey. See [Workstation Onboarding Feature Development Phases](#task-management-and-onboarding-workstation-onboarding-feature-development-phases) for more details on the wizard's phases.

Another set of improvements focuses on image name display and local build capabilities within the onboarding process. The wizard now accurately presents full registry-qualified image names, which was achieved by extending the backend API to expose the configured image registry, ensuring consistency between backend configuration and frontend display. Furthermore, the "Build locally" option is now conditionally presented, preventing its invocation for environments where the necessary build scripts are unavailable, such as Homebrew installations. This involves a backend check for script availability and a corresponding frontend adjustment to hide the option if building locally is not supported.

To enhance system robustness, particularly after unclean shutdowns or reinstallation, fixes were implemented to handle "phantom" daemon processes. These processes could continue occupying server ports without a corresponding PID file, leading to conflicts during subsequent server starts. This issue was tackled in two ways: first, by introducing a port conflict detection mechanism in the server startup process. Before a new [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) server instance starts, it probes the required ports to identify any existing listeners. If conflicts are found, the server start is blocked, and the user is advised to forcefully stop any lingering processes. Second, a [`--force`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L140) flag was added to the [`fabric server stop`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) command. When activated, this flag enables the command to actively identify and terminate processes listening on Fabric's ports, even if no PID file exists, thereby resolving potential port contention. This functionality typically uses platform-specific tools like [`lsof`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/daemon/ports.go#L44) to identify PIDs associated with occupied ports and then terminates them.

<a id="task-management-and-onboarding-code-review-feedback-and-security-fixes"></a>

### Code Review Feedback and Security Fixes

| Issue | File Path | Solution Implemented |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **H1** | `web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts` | Added `else-if` branch to handle top-level error events in image pull mode, preventing infinite spinner. |
| **H2, H3, M1** | `web/src/components/shared/dir-browser.ts` | Normalized Windows path separators to `/`, fixed `navigateToBreadcrumb` to correctly handle Windows drive letters, and updated `..` entry condition to exclude Windows drive roots. |
| **M2** | `pkg/hub/system_handlers.go` | Added a check for `scanner.Err()` after the `bufio.Scanner` loop to publish errors if a log line exceeds the buffer size. |
| **M3** | `pkg/runtime/imagepull.go` | Implemented `ctx.Err()` check at the beginning of each iteration in the image pull loop to allow for context cancellation during server shutdown. |
| **M4** | `pkg/hub/system_handlers.go` | Added an `atomic.Bool` to the `Server` struct to prevent multiple concurrent image build requests, returning `StatusConflict` if a build is already in progress. |
