| **M1 (Round 1)** | `pkg/hub/system_handlers.go` | Replaced home-boundary check with `resolved != home && !strings.HasPrefix(resolved, home+sep)` to prevent sibling-prefix bypass. |
| **M2, N1 (Round 2)** | `pkg/hub/system_handlers.go` | Modified `handlePutRuntime` to update the `Runtime` field of the active profile and ensured `handleGetRuntime` uses the same "default" fallback for empty `ActiveProfile`. |
| **M3 (Round 1)** | `pkg/hub/system_handlers.go` | Added documentation to `handleFSValidatePath` explicitly stating the intentional lack of a home-boundary fence for linked groves and ensured `assertLoopback` is applied. |
| **m1, m2, m3, m5 (Round 1), m4, m5 (Round 2)** | Various | Addressed minor issues including using the binary's executable path for build scripts, increasing `ClassifyPath` project cap, using `apiFetch` in `project-create.ts`, replacing `context.Background()` with a server-lifetime context in goroutines, and removing `devUser` self-shadowing. |

This section details the implementation of fixes based on code review feedback, addressing various issues identified during the development process. These fixes enhance the stability, security, and user experience of the Fabric platform, covering critical areas such as image pulling, path handling, concurrency, and context management.

A set of high-priority fixes targeted the image pulling mechanism and directory browsing. For instance, an infinite spinner issue in the web UI, located in [`web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts), was resolved to ensure proper error handling during early image pull failures. This ensures that the UI accurately reflects the build status, preventing indefinite loading states. Path normalization for Windows systems was also a focus, particularly in [`web/src/components/shared/dir-browser.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/shared/dir-browser.ts), to correctly handle backslashes and drive letters, which are crucial for consistent directory navigation and display across different operating systems. This prevents incorrect breadcrumb generation and ensures that the parent directory ([`..`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/Makefile#L56)) entry behaves as expected on Windows drive roots.

Further refinements addressed potential vulnerabilities and inconsistencies. A significant security fix in [`pkg/hub/system_handlers.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go) and [`pkg/hub/fs_safety.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/fs_safety.go) corrected a home-directory boundary check to prevent "sibling-prefix bypasses," ensuring that agent operations are strictly confined to their designated home directories. This improves the isolation and security of agent environments. Concurrency control for local image builds was introduced in [`pkg/hub/system_handlers.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go) to prevent multiple simultaneous builds, which could lead to race conditions and instability. This uses an atomic boolean to ensure only one build process is active at any given time, gracefully handling concurrent requests.

In terms of system stability and resource management, [`context.Background()`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L736) instances in goroutines, particularly within image pull and build operations in [`pkg/hub/system_handlers.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go) and [`pkg/runtime/imagepull.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/imagepull.go), were replaced with server-lifetime contexts. This change is crucial for ensuring that goroutines are properly canceled during server shutdowns, preventing resource leaks and improving the overall shutdown process. Additionally, a check for [`scanner.Err()`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/agents.go#L718) was added in [`pkg/hub/system_handlers.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go) after log scanning loops to catch errors, such as excessively long log lines, which could otherwise go unnoticed and lead to incomplete or corrupted log processing.

Finally, user authentication and API interactions also received attention. For consistency with other authenticated API calls, [`apiFetch()`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/client/api.ts#L25) was implemented for project creation in [`web/src/components/pages/project-create.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/project-create.ts). This standardizes how the frontend interacts with the backend, leveraging existing authentication and error handling mechanisms. An edge case in [`handlePutRuntime`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go#L173) in [`pkg/hub/system_handlers.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go) was addressed to ensure consistent behavior when [`ActiveProfile`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/types.go#L202) is an empty string, preventing discrepancies between setting and retrieving runtime configurations. These fixes collectively contribute to a more robust, secure, and user-friendly Fabric platform.

<a id="task-management-and-onboarding-project-finalization-and-rebase-instructions"></a>

### Project Finalization and Rebase Instructions

| File Path | Status | Purpose/Feature |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `pkg/daemon/ports.go` | New | Phantom daemon detection |
| `pkg/hub/system_handlers.go`, `pkg/hub/system_identity.go`, `pkg/hub/fs_safety.go` | New | `/system/*` API endpoints, identity management, and file system safety checks |
| `pkg/runtime/imagepull.go` | New | Go-native image pulling |
| `web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts`, `web/src/components/shared/dir-browser.ts` | New | Onboarding wizard and directory browser UI components |
| `cmd/root.go` | Conflict-Resolved | Git worktree detection and version check guarding |
| `cmd/server_daemon.go` | Conflict-Resolved | Onboarding status, quickstart output, and port conflict detection |
| `cmd/server_foreground.go`, `cmd/server.go` | Conflict-Resolved | Hosted mode adjustments and `stop --force` flag |
| `pkg/hub/server.go` | Modified | Server configuration, middleware (`requireWorkstation`, `assertLoopback`), and embedded broker ID |
| `pkg/hub/web.go`, `pkg/hub/seed.go`, `pkg/hub/auth.go`, `pkg/hub/devauth.go` | Modified | Developer auto-login, user seeding, and authentication logic |
| `pkg/config/settings_v1.go`, `pkg/config/hub_config.go` | Modified | Added fields for developer authentication configuration |
| `web/src/components/app-shell.ts`, `web/src/components/pages/project-create.ts` | Modified | UI updates for onboarding and linked grove project creation |

The Fabric project's workstation onboarding feature undergoes a finalization process that includes comprehensive testing, documentation updates, and end-to-end verification before integration into the main codebase. Go tests are written for new functionality, such as the [`requireWorkstation`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/server.go#L2852) middleware, which ensures access control based on workstation status, and the [`ClassifyPath`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/fs_safety.go#L52) function in [`pkg/hub/fs_safety.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/fs_safety.go), responsible for validating linked grove paths. Documentation, including the primary [`README.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L83) file, is updated to reflect the new workstation onboarding experience, providing quick-start guides and ensuring consistency in CLI output.

The integration of the workstation onboarding feature into the main codebase involves a rebase strategy, as detailed in [`.tasks/rebase-workstation-improvements.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/.tasks/rebase-workstation-improvements.md). This process prioritizes preserving all changes from the feature branch while incorporating upstream updates. New files specific to the onboarding experience, such as [`pkg/hub/system_handlers.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/system_handlers.go) for system API endpoints and [`web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/onboarding.ts) for the onboarding wizard, are preserved without conflict. For files that have been modified in both the feature branch and upstream, conflict resolution ensures that both sets of changes are retained. This includes modifications to [`cmd/root.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/root.go) for Git version checks and [`cmd/server_daemon.go`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/server_daemon.go) for port conflict detection, among others. The rebase process concludes with a verification step, ensuring that the project builds successfully and all tests pass before the rebased branch is force-pushed.

<a id="changelogs-and-release-notes"></a>

## Changelogs and Release Notes

| Date | Component | Category | Summary |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 2026-02-19 | Core Architectural Enhancements | Breaking Change | Consolidated web server into a single Go binary, removed NATS and Koa dependencies. |
| 2026-02-22 | Agent Management | Feature | Implemented soft-delete lifecycle for agents and initial execution limits. |
| 2026-02-23 | Workspace | Feature | Introduced Hub-Managed Groves for creating workspaces directly via Hub API/UI without Git. |
| 2026-02-28 | Core Architectural Enhancements | Breaking Change | Canonical agent state refactor completed, unifying `Status` and `SessionStatus`. |
| 2026-03-04 | Authentication | Breaking Change | Unified `ResolvedAuth` model replaced legacy harness-specific authentication methods. |
| 2026-03-06 | Configuration | Breaking Change | Runtime profiles and runtimes are now managed globally, not at the grove level. |
| 2026-03-09 | Core Architectural Enhancements | Breaking Change | Project rebranded to `pdlc-os/fabric`, Go module renamed. |
| 2026-03-13 | Workspace | Breaking Change | Linked Git Grove IDs unified to deterministic 16-char hex hash (later UUID). |
| 2026-03-14 | Core Architectural Enhancements | Breaking Change | All Grove IDs standardized to unified UUID format. |
| 2026-03-18 | Authentication | Breaking Change | User Access Tokens (UATs) replaced legacy API key system (`sk_live_*`). |
| 2026-03-22 | Template | Breaking Change | Custom templates now automatically inherit from `default` template's `home/` directory. |
| 2026-03-29 | Workspace | Breaking Change | Transitioned from deterministic hashing to random UUIDs for grove IDs to support multiple groves per git repository. |
| 2026-03-30 | Security | Breaking Change | Hub-scoped secrets are now uniquely namespaced by Hub Instance ID to prevent collisions. |
| 2026-03-31 | Authentication | Breaking Change | Rotating user-signing-key now invalidates all active sessions and redirects to "session expired" page. |
| 2026-04-02 | Template | Breaking Change | `POST /api/v1/groves/{groveId}/sync-templates` endpoint replaced with `POST /api/v1/groves/{groveId}/import-templates`. |
| 2026-04-03 | Authentication | Breaking Change | ADC secret renamed, and `GOOGLE_APPLICATION_CREDENTIALS` no longer set by default. |
| 2026-04-06 | Messaging | Breaking Change | Google Chat App migrated to Workspace Add-on architecture, requiring configuration updates. |
| 2026-04-07 | Authentication | Breaking Change | Hub fails to start if GCP Secret Manager signing key verification fails. |
| 2026-04-21 | Security | Breaking Change | Agent CLI now blocks resource management commands inside containers without a reachable Hub endpoint. |
| 2026-04-27 | Template | Breaking Change | Claude harness environment variables (`ANTHROPIC_MODEL`, `ANTHROPIC_SMALL_FAST_MODEL`) moved from `settings.json` to `config.yaml`. |
| 2026-05-04 | Messaging | Breaking Change | Chat App `/fabric` command split into `/fabric` (messaging) and `/fabricAdmin` (admin tasks). |
| 2026-05-08 | Lifecycle | Breaking Change | `fabric start` now defaults to resuming suspended agents; `fabric suspend` is gated on harness support. |
| 2026-05-11 | Core Architectural Enhancements | Feature | Comprehensive, multi-phase migration of "Grove" terminology to "Project" across the ecosystem. |
| 2026-05-14 | Core Architectural Enhancements | Breaking Change | The term "Grove" has been officially retired in favor of "Project." |
| 2026-05-14 | State | Breaking Change | `ActivityIdle` renamed to `ActivityWorking` for more accurate agent status reflection. |
| 2026-06-01 | CLI / Internal API | Breaking Change | `fabric broker` renamed to `fabric runtime-broker` to avoid confusion with message brokers. |
| 2026-06-05 | Workspace Pathing | Breaking Change | Workspace file browser now resolves to `groves/` instead of `projects/`. |
| 2026-06-06 | Agents | Breaking Change | Agent slugs are now enforced to be unique within a single project. |

The [`fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L1) platform maintains a detailed changelog in the [`changelog`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog) directory, which documents architectural shifts, new features, and bug fixes across various components. These changelogs serve as a historical record of continuous improvements and development milestones, structured to highlight significant changes for each release.

Core architectural enhancements include the consolidation of the web server into a single Go binary, unifying the Hub API and Web server on a single port for simplified deployment. A unified scheduling system manages recurring Hub tasks and one-shot timers, providing automated heartbeat timeout detection for "zombie" agents. A daemon mode for the [`fabric server`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1) is available for workstation use with integrated lifecycle management.

Agent management and lifecycle have seen continuous improvements. The agent status model has been refined for consistent activity representation across the Hub, Store, Runtime Broker, CLI, and Web UI. Agents can now be soft-deleted and restored, and execution limits such as [`max_turns`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/shared/types.ts#L328) and [`max_duration`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/shared/types.ts#L330) have been implemented. Agent isolation has been enhanced through externalizing non-Git grove data and agent home directories using [`tmpfs shadow mounts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/common.go#L154), and structured logging captures agent state transitions.

Authentication and authorization features have been significantly advanced. Production secret backends are now strictly required for secret [`Set`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/auth.go#L555) operations, and a "secrets-gather" flow provides interactive CLI prompts for missing values. Policy-based authorization enforces strict rules based on [`grove membership`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L311) and agent ownership, with a capability-based access control system. Unified harness authentication supports [`API Key`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L31), [`Vertex AI`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness/generic.go#L52), [`ADC`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L517), and [`OAuth`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/hub_config.go#L302), and user access tokens ([`UATs`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub_token.go#L40)) provide granular scoping. GCP identity and metadata server emulation are supported for agents, including a Web UI for Service Account management.

Workspace and grove management has evolved with hub-first Git workspaces, allowing remote workspaces to be created directly from Git URLs. Hub-managed groves support project workspace creation via the Hub API and Web UI without external Git, and direct workspace file management. Grove IDs are unified to UUIDs to support multiple groves per Git remote, and persistent, mutable shared directories are available for agents. A [`Grove Workspace Sync`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/store/models.go#L138) system includes [`WebDAV Support`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-31-changelog.md?plain=1#L10) and [`Linked Grove Cache Relay`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/project_webdav.go#L52).

The template and configuration system has been refined to support harness-agnostic templates with [`agent_instructions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/agent-configure.ts#L40), [`system_prompt`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/agent-configure.ts#L39), and [`default_harness_config`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/mutation.go#L36744) fields. Template bootstrapping automatically loads local agent templates into the Hub database on server startup. Grove template synchronization and management allow for API, CLI, and Web UI-based updates, and a refactored template import system expands template discovery to various sources. Robust support for harness skills within agent templates automatically merges and mounts them into harness-specific directories.

The Web UI/UX has been continuously enhanced with new list pages, client-side routing, and real-time updates via [`Server-Sent Events`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L1008) ([`SSE`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness_capabilities.go#L66)). Improvements to the web terminal include clipboard support and [`tmux`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L74) integration. The agent detail page has been re-architected into a high-density, tabbed layout, and an inline file editor with Markdown preview is available.

Observability and telemetry capabilities include telemetry injection into settings, a native OpenTelemetry (OTLP) pipeline with GCP credential injection and exporters, and an end-to-end cloud log viewer. The metrics pipeline has been overhauled to enrich OTel resource attributes, and a 3D agent activity visualizer tool dynamically discovers agents and files from log events.

Messaging and notification systems have been developed with a multi-phase framework for real-time subscriptions to agent status events, an integrated notification system with [`SSE`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/harness_capabilities.go#L66) delivery and browser push support, and a bidirectional messaging system with a message store, human inbox, and [`MessageBrokerProxy`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/messagebroker.go#L46).

Kubernetes integration includes native secret mounting, GKE security enhancements like [`Workload Identity`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L318), native GKE runtime support, PTY support, and Autopilot compatibility. GitHub App integration provides JWT-based authentication, automated token refresh, Git credential helper functionality, and an Admin Management UI.

<a id="changelogs-and-release-notes-core-architecture-and-infrastructure-updates"></a>

### Core Architecture and Infrastructure Updates

![Diagram 85](diagrams/diagram-085.svg)

The Fabric platform's core architecture has undergone significant evolution to enhance its efficiency, scalability, and maintainability. A key architectural shift involved consolidating the web server and the Hub API into a single Go binary, unifying what were previously separate [`Node.js Koa`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L20) and [`NATS`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/GLOSSARY.md?plain=1#L145) components. This consolidation, documented in the [Changelogs and Release Notes](#changelogs-and-release-notes) (specifically, [`changelog/2026-02-19-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-19-changelog.md) and [`changelog/2026-02-20-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-20-changelog.md)), streamlined the serving of the web frontend, SPA routing, and Server-Sent Events (SSE) through a single process. All API traffic is now routed under [`/api/v1/`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/web.go#L569), simplifying local deployments and addressing Cross-Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) issues.

Further infrastructural improvements include the introduction of a unified scheduling system for managing recurring and one-shot tasks within the Hub. This system, detailed in [`changelog/2026-02-28-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-28-changelog.md), also incorporates automated heartbeat timeout detection to identify and manage "zombie" agents. To support administrative operations and platform maintenance, a new UI was developed, providing tools for triggering actions such as image pulls and server rebuilds, complete with run histories and configurable executors (documented in [`changelog/2026-03-31-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-31-changelog.md)). Additionally, a daemon mode for the [`fabric server`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1) was introduced in [`changelog/2026-03-07-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-07-changelog.md), optimizing its operation for workstation environments with integrated lifecycle management. These changes collectively aim to create a more robust, integrated, and easily manageable platform for agent orchestration.

<a id="changelogs-and-release-notes-agent-management-and-lifecycle-enhancements"></a>

### Agent Management and Lifecycle Enhancements

![Diagram 86](diagrams/diagram-086.svg)

Agent lifecycle management in Fabric has undergone continuous refinement to improve agent autonomy, reliability, and security. A significant change involved the refactoring of the agent status model, unifying [`SessionStatus`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-20-changelog.md?plain=1#L6) into a primary [`Status`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L2629) field and introducing "sticky" statuses like [`WAITING_FOR_INPUT`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L44) and [`COMPLETED`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L44). This change provided a more consistent representation of agent activity across the Hub, store, runtime broker, CLI, and web UI. See [Core Architecture and Infrastructure Updates](#changelogs-and-release-notes-core-architecture-and-infrastructure-updates) for further details.

To manage agent data more effectively, a full soft-delete lifecycle was implemented for agents. This includes Hub-side archiving, a [`fabric restore`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/restore.go#L22) command for recovery, filtering for deleted agents, and automated background purging, as described in [`changelog/2026-02-22-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-22-changelog.md). Server-side settings were also introduced to configure soft-delete retention periods and workspace file preservation.

Agent execution is now subject to defined limits, with an infrastructure supporting [`max_turns`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/shared/types.ts#L328) and [`max_duration`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/shared/types.ts#L330) constraints. Exceeding these limits transitions an agent into a [`LIMITS_EXCEEDED`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/notifications.go#L49) state, as noted in [`changelog/2026-02-22-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-22-changelog.md) and further refined in [`changelog/2026-03-01-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-01-changelog.md) to include [`max_model_calls`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/shared/types.ts#L329).

Enhanced agent isolation and security are achieved by externalizing non-Git grove data and agent home directories using [`tmpfs shadow mounts`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/common.go#L154), as detailed in [`changelog/2026-03-08-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-08-changelog.md). This approach prevents agents from persisting unauthorized changes outside their designated work areas.

Structured logging was added to the broker for agent state transitions (creation, start, stop, deletion), including [`agent_id`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/mutation.go#L5939) and [`grove_id`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L176) metadata. This provides better observability into the agent lifecycle, aiding in debugging and monitoring, as documented in [`changelog/2026-03-23-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-23-changelog.md). These logging enhancements contribute to the overall [Observability, Telemetry, and Visualization](#changelogs-and-release-notes-observability-telemetry-and-visualization) efforts within the Fabric platform.

<a id="changelogs-and-release-notes-authentication-authorization-and-security-features"></a>

### Authentication, Authorization, and Security Features

![Diagram 87](diagrams/diagram-087.svg)

Advancements in authentication and authorization provide secure access and controlled operations for Fabric agents and users. Secrets management is a core component, with a production secret backend (e.g., Google Cloud Secret Manager) becoming a strict requirement for [`Set`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/auth.go#L555) operations across user, grove, and runtime broker scopes, replacing plaintext fallbacks for enhanced security. For Kubernetes agents, native secret mounting is supported, including [`GKE CSI`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/doctor.go#L38) drivers, for robust credential management. The environment gathering pipeline also includes a "secrets-gather" mechanism, allowing templates to define required secrets and providing interactive CLI prompts for missing values, with secrets securely backed by the configured provider.

Policy-based authorization, introduced on February 24, 2026, enforces strict access controls for agent operations. Agent creation requires [`grove membership`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L311), while interaction (PTY, messaging) and deletion are restricted to the agent's owner or system administrators. This access control extends hierarchically with [`Transitive Agent Access (Ancestry)`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-26-changelog.md?plain=1#L6). A [`Capability-Based Access Control`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/docs-site/src/content/docs/hub-admin/permissions.md?plain=1#L50) system further refines access, utilizing [`_capabilities`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/shared/types.ts#L50) annotations in API responses.

Unified harness authentication provides a centralized [`AuthConfig`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/auth.go#L31) that supports various methods, including [`API Key`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L31), [`Vertex AI`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/harness/generic.go#L52), [`ADC`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/api/types.go#L517), and [`OAuth`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/config/hub_config.go#L302). This multi-phase refactoring of the agent authentication pipeline aims for consistency and security across different environments. User Access Tokens (UATs), designated as [`fabric_pat_*`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/auth.go#L79) tokens, replace legacy API keys, offering granular scoping and CLI management through [`fabric auth tokens`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/hub.go#L362).

GCP identity and metadata server emulation enables agents to securely access GCP resources. This includes a Web UI for Service Account management and [`iptables`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/agent/run.go#L1286) interception to ensure that agents can leverage GCP services with hub-minted service accounts. GitHub App integration facilitates secure communication and token management for Git-based operations. This integration provides JWT-based authentication, automated token refresh, and Git credential helper functionality.

<a id="changelogs-and-release-notes-workspace-and-grove-management-evolution"></a>

### Workspace and Grove Management Evolution

![Diagram 88](diagrams/diagram-088.svg)

The management of agent workspaces and groves within the Fabric platform has undergone a significant evolution, moving towards a more integrated and flexible system. Initially, the platform introduced the concept of Hub-first Git workspaces, allowing for the creation of remote workspaces directly from Git URLs. This provided a centralized approach to version-controlled agent environments.

This was further expanded with the introduction of Hub-managed groves, decoupling workspace management from external Git repositories. This allowed for project workspace creation directly via the Hub API and Web UI, automatically initializing with a standard [`.fabric`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L34) structure. The ability to directly manage workspace files through the Hub API further reduced reliance on external Git for these groves, as noted in [`changelog/2026-02-24-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-24-changelog.md).

To standardize and unify identifiers, Grove IDs were transitioned to UUIDs, initially using deterministic hex hashes and later moving to random UUIDs to support multiple groves per Git remote, as documented in [`changelog/2026-03-14-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-14-changelog.md) and [`changelog/2026-03-29-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-29-changelog.md).

For agents requiring persistent storage, the platform introduced shared persistent directories within a grove. These directories support various storage backends, including local filesystems and Kubernetes [`PersistentVolumeClaims`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/k8s_runtime.go#L808), and are manageable via [`fabric shared-dir`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/cmd/cli_mode.go#L9) CLI commands, as detailed in [`changelog/2026-03-12-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-12-changelog.md).

Workspace synchronization capabilities were also enhanced with the completion of the Grove Workspace Sync system, incorporating WebDAV support, a linked grove cache relay, and new CLI [`sync`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/runtime/mock.go#L101) commands, as outlined in [`changelog/2026-03-31-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-31-changelog.md).

Finally, a new grove type emerged, combining remote Git repositories with local workspaces. These hybrid Git-workspace groves feature automated provisioning, offering a flexible environment for agents that benefit from both version-controlled code and dynamic local modifications, as described in [`changelog/2026-03-28-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-28-changelog.md). This evolution in workspace and grove management provides a robust and adaptable framework for agent operation within Fabric.

<a id="changelogs-and-release-notes-template-and-configuration-system-refinements"></a>

### Template and Configuration System Refinements

![Diagram 89](diagrams/diagram-089.svg)

The Fabric platform has undergone significant enhancements to its template and configuration system to improve flexibility, consistency, and ease of management for agents. A key development is the introduction of harness-agnostic templates, which allow agents to define their roles and instructions independently of specific Large Language Model (LLM) implementations. This is achieved through fields such as [`agent_instructions`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/agent-configure.ts#L40), [`system_prompt`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/web/src/components/pages/agent-configure.ts#L39), and [`default_harness_config`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/ent/mutation.go#L36744), enabling templates to specify an agent's behavior without being tied to a particular harness. This evolution is documented in [`changelog/2026-02-24-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-24-changelog.md).

To streamline development and deployment, a template bootstrapping mechanism was introduced, automatically loading local agent templates into the Hub database upon server startup, as noted in [`changelog/2026-02-25-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-25-changelog.md). This ensures that newly defined or updated templates are immediately available within the system.

Further refinements include robust support for harness skills within agent templates. These skills are automatically merged and mounted into harness-specific directories (e.g., [`.claude/skills`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/harnesses/claude/config.yaml#L34)), ensuring that agents have access to the necessary tools and capabilities for their designated harness. This feature significantly enhances the modularity and reusability of agent configurations, as detailed in [`changelog/2026-03-13-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-13-changelog.md).

For managing templates at a broader scope, grove template synchronization and management capabilities were added. This allows for synchronizing grove-level templates with the Hub via API endpoints like [`POST /api/v1/groves/{groveId}/sync-templates`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-14-changelog.md?plain=1#L10), CLI commands ([`fabric templates sync --all`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/agents.md?plain=1#L1)), and through the Web UI. This ensures consistency across different groves and simplifies the distribution of templates within projects, as described in [`changelog/2026-03-14-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-14-changelog.md).

A significant architectural overhaul of the template import system replaced the previous container-based approach with a direct server-side import mechanism. This refactor expanded template discovery to include deep GitHub paths, archives, [`rclone`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/go.mod#L33) URIs, and direct Fabric template imports, moving from [`POST /api/v1/groves/{groveId}/sync-templates`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-14-changelog.md?plain=1#L10) to [`POST /api/v1/groves/{groveId}/import-templates`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-04-02-changelog.md?plain=1#L6). This change, documented in [`changelog/2026-04-02-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-04-02-changelog.md), streamlines the process of integrating diverse template sources into the Fabric platform, offering greater flexibility and efficiency in agent setup and configuration.

<a id="changelogs-and-release-notes-user-interface-and-experience-ui-ux-improvements"></a>

### User Interface and Experience (UI/UX) Improvements

| Feature Area | Specific Enhancement | Timeframe |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Agent Management** | Advanced filtering options ("My Agents", "My Groves"), consistent action buttons across real-time updates, Broker column in table view, dedicated "Create Agent" UI. | Mar 2026 - Apr 2026 |
| **Workspace & Files** | Dot-file visibility toggle, hybrid search for file browsers, content previews, shared directory ZIP downloads, improved GitHub URL rendering. | Mar 2026 - May 2026 |
| **Terminal & PTY** | Tmux mouse toggle, native copy/paste, Shift+Enter support, terminal activity badge, improved window switcher, `DISCONNECTED` overlay. | Mar 2026 - Jun 2026 |
| **Notifications & Messaging** | Browser push notifications, Discord/Telegram integration, real-time message stream for agents, dedicated inbox tray with unread counts, improved message rendering. | Mar 2026 - May 2026 |
| **Admin & Configuration** | Web-based server config editor, integrated update mechanism, unified user/invite/allow list management, project rename support. | Mar 2026 - Jun 2026 |
| **Visualizations** | Agent activity visualizer with log replay, 3D graph, enhanced animations, Markdown rendering for inter-agent messages. | Mar 2026 - Jun 2026 |
| **Branding & UI Consistency** | SVG favicon, standardized icons, Dark Mode improvements, consistent error messaging. | Mar 2026 - Apr 2026 |
| **Performance** | Optimistic UI updates, SSE connection pooling, route-based code splitting, SQLite connection pooling. | Mar 2026 - May 2026 |
| **Project Management** | New "Project" terminology (formerly "Grove"), dedicated settings tabs (General, Limits, Resources), workspace mode selector. | May 2026 - Jun 2026 |
| **Auth & Identity** | User Access Tokens (UATs), GitHub App integration, GCP Identity/metadata emulation, automated token refresh, Google IAP auth proxy. | Mar 2026 - Jun 2026 |

The Fabric platform's Web UI/UX has undergone continuous refinement to enhance user interaction and provide real-time visibility into agent operations. Early improvements included the introduction of new list pages for various entities, the implementation of client-side routing, and the integration of real-time updates via Server-Sent Events (SSE). These enhancements facilitate a dynamic user experience, where changes to agents and other resources are reflected promptly without requiring page reloads. The use of SSE for real-time updates is further elaborated in [Real-time State Management and SSE](#fabric-web-user-interface-real-time-state-management-and-sse).

A significant area of focus has been the web terminal, which has seen numerous improvements to boost usability and functionality. These include the addition of native clipboard copy/paste support, making it easier for users to interact with agent outputs and inputs. Further enhancements integrated [`tmux`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L74) functionalities, such as mouse toggling and key binding support ([`C-b m`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-11-changelog.md?plain=1#L7)), to provide a more robust and familiar terminal experience directly within the browser.

The agent detail UI has been re-architected to present information more efficiently. This overhaul introduced a high-density, tabbed layout, segmenting agent details into logical categories like "Status," "Configuration," and "Messages," thereby improving navigation and information accessibility.

Most recently, an inline file and template editor was introduced, featuring integrated Markdown preview and fuzzy filtering. This editor enables users to browse and edit template files directly within the web interface, streamlining the process of managing agent configurations and instructions. The evolution of templating and configuration systems is further discussed in [Template and Configuration System Refinements](#changelogs-and-release-notes-template-and-configuration-system-refinements). Additionally, the development of a cloud log viewer system, including a new Hub API for log retrieval and a dedicated "Messages" tab in the Web UI, provides comprehensive visibility into agent activities and communications.

<a id="changelogs-and-release-notes-observability-telemetry-and-visualization"></a>

### Observability, Telemetry, and Visualization

![Diagram 90](diagrams/diagram-090.svg)

Advancements in observability and telemetry within Fabric have focused on providing comprehensive insights into agent activity and system health. This includes the introduction of telemetry injection into the settings schema, as noted in the changelog for [`changelog/2026-02-19-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-19-changelog.md).

A native OpenTelemetry Protocol (OTLP) pipeline was established, enabling the system to receive and forward logs, with support for Google Cloud Platform (GCP) credential injection. This pipeline was further enhanced with native Google Cloud Trace and Cloud Logging exporters, as detailed in the changelogs for [`changelog/2026-03-03-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-03-changelog.md) and [`changelog/2026-03-06-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-06-changelog.md). This integration allows for standardized data collection and export to GCP services for comprehensive monitoring.

An end-to-end cloud log viewer system was implemented, featuring a Hub API for log retrieval and a dedicated [`Messages`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hubclient/client.go#L94) tab within the Web UI, which is documented in [`changelog/2026-03-07-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-07-changelog.md). This provides a centralized interface for reviewing agent and system logs.

The metrics pipeline underwent an overhaul, enriching OpenTelemetry (OTel) resource attributes to capture more detailed telemetry, particularly for tools like [`Codex`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/README.md?plain=1#L83), to track tool usage and token counts, as described in [`changelog/2026-03-12-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-12-changelog.md).

For visualizing agent activity, a 3D agent activity visualizer tool was developed. Initially, this tool dynamically discovered agents and files from log events, and later incorporated [`fs-watcher`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/fs-watcher-tool/go.mod#L1) for filesystem telemetry, enabling a log-driven approach to visualization. These developments are highlighted across changelogs, including [`changelog/2026-03-22-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-22-changelog.md), [`changelog/2026-03-24-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-24-changelog.md), [`changelog/2026-03-25-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-25-changelog.md), and [`changelog/2026-03-28-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-28-changelog.md). This visualizer assists in understanding agent communications, file interactions, and overall workflow. Additional details on the [`agent-viz`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/extras/agent-viz/go.mod#L1) tool can be found in [Agent Activity Visualization with `agent-viz`](#auxiliary-tools-and-integrations-agent-activity-visualization-with-agent-viz).

<a id="changelogs-and-release-notes-messaging-and-notification-system-development"></a>

### Messaging and Notification System Development

![Diagram 91](diagrams/diagram-091.svg)

The Fabric platform features a comprehensive messaging and notification system designed to facilitate real-time communication within the ecosystem. This system has undergone a multi-phase evolution, culminating in a robust framework for agent-to-agent and agent-to-user interactions.

A core component of this system is the capability for real-time subscriptions to agent status events. This is supported by a notification dispatcher and corresponding Hub API endpoints, which allow for the tracking of agent activities. This framework was further expanded into an integrated notification system that leverages Server-Sent Events (SSE) for delivery, offering agent-scoped filtering and browser push support for user notifications. The web user interface also includes a notification tray to centralize these updates.

The messaging system enables bidirectional communication, which has evolved to include a dedicated message store for persistence. A "human inbox" provides a centralized location for users to manage messages from agents, accessible via both the command-line interface and the Hub API. For real-time delivery of messages, a [`MessageBrokerProxy`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/pkg/hub/messagebroker.go#L46) is utilized, ensuring that agents can send outbound messages efficiently. Further details on how agents utilize the messaging system can be found in [Inter-Agent and User Communication Protocols](#fabric-platform-skills-inter-agent-and-user-communication-protocols).

The development milestones of these features are extensively documented in the changelog, particularly from [`changelog/2026-02-24-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-02-24-changelog.md) to [`changelog/2026-03-28-changelog.md`](https://github.com/pdlc-os/fabric/blob/b11448f8f01fdcf12deab96204417d87f8d46ab3/changelog/2026-03-28-changelog.md), which detail the continuous enhancements and architectural decisions that shaped the messaging and notification capabilities within Fabric.

<a id="changelogs-and-release-notes-kubernetes-and-github-integrations"></a>

### Kubernetes and GitHub Integrations

![Diagram 92](diagrams/diagram-092.svg)

The platform provides extensive integration with Kubernetes environments, particularly Google Kubernetes Engine (GKE), and GitHub.

For Kubernetes, a key focus has been on enhancing agent security and operational efficiency. The system now supports native secret mounting for Kubernetes agents, a crucial component for securely injecting sensitive information into agent containers. This is achieved through mechanisms that leverage CSI drivers, providing robust fallback paths for credential access. Further security enhancements include the integration of GKE-specific features like [Workload Identity](https://cloud.google.com/kubernetes-engine/docs/how-to/workload-identity), which strengthens the authentication of applications running on GKE by associating Kubernetes Service Accounts with Google Service Accounts. Native support for GKE runtimes has been introduced, streamlining the deployment and management of agents within GKE clusters, alongside corresponding cluster provisioning scripts. The Kubernetes runtime has matured to achieve feature parity with other execution environments, with a strong emphasis on production hardening and launch readiness. This includes native PTY (pseudo-terminal) support via the Kubernetes Go client API for interactive agent sessions and compatibility with GKE Autopilot, Google Cloud's managed Kubernetes service.

On the GitHub integration front, a multi-phase approach has been implemented to integrate Fabric Hub instances with GitHub via a GitHub App. This integration provides JWT-based authentication, allowing secure communication between the Fabric Hub and GitHub. It includes infrastructure to link groves (logical groupings of agents and resources) with GitHub App installations. The system also features automated token refresh capabilities, ensuring continuous and secure access without manual intervention. A Git credential helper functionality has been introduced, simplifying Git operations for agents by handling authentication seamlessly. Additionally, an administrative management UI provides tools for configuring and monitoring these GitHub integrations. The system allows for enhanced authentication token minting directly from source Groves, further streamlining the workflow for agents interacting with GitHub repositories.
